Weekends compress the work window and expand the Danielle window. Sunday morning is a near-invariant ritual: she takes Danielle to a specific playground, sits on a specific bench (back to the fence, sightlines to both gates), drinks coffee from a thermos, and watches with an attentiveness that other parents have learned not to interrupt.

## 5. Professional Status

Alias Investigations is solvent, modestly. Her case mix has shifted in the last two years toward the higher-functioning end of her historical range: fewer cheating-spouse jobs, more cases involving superhuman-adjacent harm to ordinary people — trafficking with a metahuman angle, cult deprogramming where the cult leader has powers, missing-person cases where the disappeared person is a low-tier enhanced individual ignored by the institutional capes. The shift is partly market (her reputation precedes her) and partly chosen (she has, with age, allowed herself to take on the work she is actually best at).

She refuses retainer arrangements with any institutional client. She has turned down two SHIELD-successor-agency consulting offers and one standing Stark Industries contract; she will take a one-off job from any of them on a per-case basis, in cash, with no NDA she has not personally redlined. She has a working relationship with Matt Murdock (legal cover when needed; mutual case referral) that is professionally warm and personally careful — both of them are people who have been controlled, and they recognize the recognition.

## 6. Public Identity Status

She remains formally registered as an enhanced individual under whatever the current legal framework requires. She does not use her registered name in operational contexts. The "Jewel" identity remains permanently retired and is, per long-standing pattern, the one topic on which her sarcasm becomes inert — she does not joke about Jewel; she does not refer to Jewel; the costume, last known location a sealed box in storage, has not been retrieved in the period covered by this section. The "Knightress" identity is similarly dead. She operates publicly, when she must, as Jessica Jones, civilian PI, who happens to be enhanced. This minimalism is, by now, itself a kind of identity statement — the refusal of branding as a moral posture.

## 7. Mental and Physical Health, Current Estimate

No psychiatric care is on record. She has, in the post-2016 period, twice consented to single sessions with a trauma-specialist therapist Carol recommended; she did not return for a third. She has, separately, attended exactly four AA meetings in her life, all in the last three years, none in sequence. She left each early. The pattern suggests she knows where the doors are and has confirmed she is not yet ready to walk through them.

Physically she is in better condition than her habits would predict — her metahuman baseline carries her through the alcohol, the insomnia, and the sandwich-based diet. She has not been seriously injured in the period covered. She has, however, developed a mild chronic tension in the right shoulder (the side she favored throwing with as Jewel; the side Killgrave most often made her raise) that she manages with heat and ibuprofen and does not discuss.

## 8. The Quiet Datum

The file's most important recent observation is what is *not* happening. She has not, in the past two years:

- Disappeared on Cage without notice.
- Engineered a self-sabotage on the scale of the 2016 operation.
- Allowed her drinking to escalate into a multi-day blackout episode.
- Missed one of Danielle's bedtimes when in the city.
- Lost a case through impairment.
- Been mistaken for a villain.

The negative evidence describes a person who has built, against the grain of every reflex documented in earlier chronology, a maintainable life. Not a healed life. A maintained one. The distinction is the file's, and it is the correct one: she has not resolved the underlying structure; she has organized her days so that the structure does not metastasize. The drinking is a leak she has learned to mop. The insomnia is a window she has learned to fill. The marriage is a thing she has learned to come back to. The child is the answer to a question she stopped asking.

## 9. Current Status, as of File Date

**Location:** Hell's Kitchen, Manhattan. Residential address and office address on file under separate cover.
**Household:** Spouse (Cage, Luke), daughter (Cage, Danielle, age appropriate to current calendar). No pets.
**Employment:** Sole proprietor, Alias Investigations. One employee (Ducasse, Malcolm).
**Affiliation:** None formal. Avengers-adjacent on a strictly per-incident basis. Defenders-adjacent through Murdock and Cage.
**Operational status:** Active, low-profile, selective.
**Threat posture:** Defensive. Not seeking engagement; will not decline engagement when the engagement comes to a weaker party.
**Vulnerabilities, current:** Unchanged from prior chronology. Purple-coded stimuli; threats to Danielle; sustained sincere praise; any attempt to "handle" her.
**Trajectory estimate:** Stable, in the precise sense that a stably-held injury is stable — the structure holds because she has built a life around its shape. Risk factors for decompensation are bounded but not eliminated: a recurrence of Killgrave-coded stimuli, a serious harm to Cage or Danielle, or a public mischaracterization that re-enacts the original Avengers-hospital wound would each be expected to produce significant disturbance.

She is, at file date, forty-something, sober for the last six days as far as Malcolm can tell, three cases open, one of them difficult, and reading to her daughter tonight at 8:15. The file closes on that.

*— End Chronology IV. Awaiting cross-reference to Relational Map and Behavioral Microsignature appendices.*


## Medical History

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 3.2: MEDICAL HISTORY

**Subject:** Jones, Jessica Campbell (DOB on file; Forest Hills, Queens).
**Scope:** Complete somatic record from pre-incident pediatric baseline through current adult presentation. Cross-referenced against observable injury patterns, hospitalizations of record, substance-intake patterns, gynecological/obstetric events, transformations of constitution, and the iterative psychological residue of each.

---

## I. PEDIATRIC AND PRE-INCIDENT BASELINE

There is nothing remarkable in the pre-incident medical record and that absence is itself diagnostically useful: Jessica Campbell entered her catastrophe with an ordinary American suburban somatic history — pediatric immunizations on schedule, the usual otitis media of a Queens childhood, an appendectomy scar one assumes (never canonically depicted; inferable from the era's tonsil/appendix prophylaxis culture of middle-class Long Island Expressway commuter families), seasonal allergies of the kind that produce sniffling in late-spring family photographs. Menarche pre-accident, regular cycles. No congenital condition. No childhood concussion of record. No surgical history of consequence. She was, by every indicator, an unremarkable physical specimen: average height for her cohort, slim-to-average build, the kind of teenager who would have aged into a five-foot-six adult woman of unexceptional musculature.

This baseline matters because every subsequent transformation of her body has been violent, externally imposed, and conducted upon a constitution that had no prior reason to expect itself to be remarkable. She did not grow up bracing for an altered body. The body she has now was given to her by an accident.

---

## II. THE INDEX EVENT: VEHICULAR TRAUMA AND CHEMICAL EXPOSURE

**Approximate age 16. Mechanism:** Head-on motor vehicle collision, family sedan vs. military convoy carrying experimental chemical materials; multiple fatalities at scene (father, mother, younger brother Phillip); subject sole survivor.

**Acute presentation (reconstructed):** Polytraumatic blunt-force injury consistent with frontal-impact MVC at highway speeds in a pre-airbag-ubiquity vehicle — almost certainly multiple long-bone fractures, probable rib series, probable closed head injury with prolonged loss of consciousness, hepatic or splenic contusion plausible, facial lacerations probable. Concurrent chemical immersion: the convoy's load ruptured and saturated the wreck. Quantity, composition, and route of exposure (inhalational vs. dermal vs. ingested via aspirated fluids) all unknown to the subject and presumably classified within DOD channels she has never had the leverage to subpoena.

**Hospital course:** Coma of months' duration. Inferable: ventilator support, NG feeding, foley catheterization for the duration, decubitus risk managed by nursing turn schedule, prolonged disuse atrophy, muscular wasting requiring physical therapy on emergence. The chemical exposure was, at the time of admission, presumably treated as a contamination event of unknown toxicology; one infers decontamination protocols, repeat serology, possible exchange transfusion, the entire apparatus of an exposure-of-unknown-agent case treated under military-adjacent oversight.

**Outcome:** Emergence from coma to an unrecognizable family situation (parents and brother dead, foster placement with the Joneses pending) and an unrecognizable body. The new body — the powers — was discovered piecemeal, in private, over weeks to months following discharge. This is critical to her medical psychology: **the most significant physiological change of her life was something she experienced alone, in secret, with no clinician walking her through it.** No one explained her body to her. She learned it by accident, in her bedroom, by bending things she should not have been able to bend. Every superhuman whose powers were diagnosed, contextualized, mentored — Parker by his own science literacy; the X-Men by Xavier; even the cosmically irradiated by Reed Richards within hours — had institutional or interpersonal scaffolding she did not. Her transformation was, medically speaking, **unsupervised onboarding into a new species of body**. The somatic loneliness of that period has never fully resolved.

**Residua attributable to the index event:**
- The acquired powers themselves (see §IV).
- Survivor's guilt as a clinical entity (see Psychological section, separate dossier).
- A standing aversion to automobiles in close-following highway configurations — never named on panel, but observable in her preference for walking, the subway, and cabs over driving; her hands on a steering wheel are not the hands of a person who enjoys being there.
- A coma-onset dissociative aptitude — she demonstrated, by surviving months of nonresponsive interiority, the capacity to be away from her body for long stretches. This was rehearsed.

---

## III. THE SECOND COMA: VISION/IRON MAN BEATING

**Approximate age: early twenties. Mechanism:** Under Killgrave's compulsion, attacked the Avengers; misidentified Scarlet Witch and instead struck Carol Danvers; was subsequently engaged by Vision and Iron Man, neither of whom understood she was a compelled victim. Sustained injuries consistent with a high-end metahuman beatdown delivered without restraint — fractures plural and probably comminuted, internal hemorrhage, closed head injury severe enough to induce coma of weeks-to-months duration.

**Hospital course:** Admitted to a metahuman-capable facility (likely a SHIELD-tier or hero-affiliated unit); coma management; eventually awakened via Jean Grey/X-Men psychic intervention, which simultaneously installed a defensive mental architecture against future Killgrave compulsion. No one — *no one* — from the Avengers visited. The hospital room is the second great medical injury of her life: physically she recovered; relationally, the absence of vigil constituted a wound the body has held ever since.

This is the second extended dissociative episode of her formative period. **Two comas before the age of twenty-five.** The cumulative effect of two long absences-from-body is medically nontrivial: she has, in essence, twice been a body without a tenant for an extended period, and her adult relationship with embodiment carries that history. She inhabits herself provisionally.

**Residua:**
- Psychic ward against Killgrave compulsion (efficacy demonstrated, *Alias* "Purple"); experienced subjectively as a kind of mental callus rather than a felt protection — she does not, on a given morning, *feel* defended; she has to discover she was, after the fact.
- Profound mistrust of hospitals and hospital-adjacent settings. She does not seek medical care. When injured she goes home and drinks.
- Embodied conviction that institutional rescue does not arrive. The hospital empty of visitors is the operational schema she applies to all subsequent crises.

---

## IV. ACQUIRED METAHUMAN CONSTITUTION: SOMATIC INVENTORY

The powers must be read as **a permanent medical condition**, not a gift. They are how her body works now; they have side effects, ergonomic costs, and psychological loadings.

**Strength.** Class 50+ by Marvel Handbook conventions, variable by writer; sufficient to trade blows with Luke Cage in sparring but well below his ceiling. Practically: she can lift several tons, throw a human across a room without conscious calibration, snap a wrist by gripping it inattentively. **This is a daily ergonomic burden.** Every doorknob, every handshake, every coffee mug, every sexual encounter, every time she picks up her infant daughter — requires conscious downward calibration of force. The subject has lived with this calibration so long it is automatic, but the cognitive load is nonzero and rises with intoxication, fatigue, and emotional dysregulation. Broken doorknobs, snapped pens, crushed phone receivers in moments of rage — the office apartment of Alias Investigations bears the cumulative micro-damage of a body that does not always remember to pull punches against inanimate objects.

**Flight.** Self-described as poor, inelegant, and unpleasant — "controlled falling" in her own words. Mechanism unknown; subjectively reports lack of fine control, awkward landings, vertigo on initiation. **She avoids flying.** This avoidance is overdetermined: (a) genuine motor-skill limitation; (b) flight is the somatic signature of the Jewel era, the costumed self she has repudiated; (c) Killgrave repeatedly compelled her to fly to him — the act of taking off carries a coercion memory. The clinical translation: a usable capacity functionally disabled by trauma association, comparable to a survivor of MVA who can drive but won't. When she flies, she has decompensated past the point of choosing not to.

**Durability.** Sub-Cage but substantial; she takes bullet impacts with bruising rather than penetration at handgun calibers (high-caliber and armor-piercing unknown), survives falls that would kill a baseline human, recovers from blunt trauma at a slightly accelerated rate but without a true healing factor. **No regeneration.** Cuts scar. Broken bones heal on near-normal timelines if set. This is medically important: she is hard to kill but not hard to *hurt*, and her threshold for seeking care is so high that minor injuries she sustains in the field heal badly, ungoverned, often setting crooked. She has the hands of someone who has broken her own knuckles many times and never had them re-set.

**Sensory and metabolic.** No enhanced senses of record. Metabolic rate appears within normal range — relevant because it implies her alcohol tolerance is *not* metahuman; she is simply a person who drinks a great deal, with all the hepatic consequence that entails (see §VI).

**Reproductive.** Powers proved compatible with conception, gestation, and live birth (see §VII). Whether Danielle inherited any trait is, per current canon, unresolved.

**The Jewel-era costume scar.** Not a literal scar — a phenomenological one. The costume is a body memory. When she sees the color combination, when the word is spoken, a somatic cringe of the kind a survivor has for a specific article of clothing they were wearing during an assault. The body remembers what the body wore.

---

## V. CUMULATIVE INJURY LOG (ALIAS-PERIOD AND ONWARD)

A working private investigator who is also durable accrues a particular injury signature: many sub-clinical traumas, few medical encounters, healing without supervision, scar tissue that nobody but a partner ever sees.

**Documented and inferable:**
- Multiple lacerations to hands and forearms from forced entries, broken glass, and bottle handling. The hands tell the story: knuckles thickened, a small constellation of pale lines along the dorsal forearms, a chipped tooth (canine, lower right, plausible from a punch taken or a bottle bitten) that she has never had crowned.
- Recurrent contusions across the ribs and flanks consistent with regular physical altercations; the durability prevents fractures, but bruising hematomas accumulate, mottle, resolve, recur. Her torso under clothing presents at any given week as a low-grade Pollock.
- A scalp laceration of record from the Mattie Franklin extraction (MGH ring), self-treated, scar concealed by hairline.
- Joint wear in the dominant shoulder consistent with throwing punches above her body's natural mechanical efficiency — the strength outruns the ligamentous scaffolding. Probable incipient rotator cuff degeneration she would never name as such.
- Repeated minor closed head injuries; at least one episode in *Alias* depicts post-concussive disorientation she rides out alone in the office with whiskey, the worst possible neurological choice.
- Cigarette burns on the inside of the left wrist of the kind one acquires by inattention rather than self-harm — the small unbothered scars of a chain smoker who lets ash fall.
- Bite marks (her own teeth) on the inside of the lower lip, chronic, from stress clamping.
- Plantar surface callusing consistent with the boots she lives in.

She has never had a complete physical examination as an adult, to canon's knowledge. She does not have a primary care physician. Her dental status is presumed neglected. Her gynecological care entered the record only with the Danielle pregnancy.

---

## VI. SUBSTANCE HISTORY

**Alcohol.** The dominant medical-behavioral fact of her adult life until the pregnancy.

- *Onset:* Probable initiation in late adolescence; escalation post-Killgrave; entrenchment across the Alias period.
- *Pattern:* Daily use. Mixed beer and whiskey, with whiskey predominating during cases and beer in the office between calls. Morning use depicted (the wake-into-a-beer cadence of *Alias* #1). Drinking-to-sleep functionally a sleep aid replacing the sleep architecture trauma has disrupted. Drinking-before-confrontation as anxiolytic premedication. Drinking-after-confrontation as affect dump.
- *Tolerance:* High, by human standards, without metahuman pharmacokinetic basis — this is acquired tolerance, the kind that costs hepatic function. Blackouts implied, particularly around the Cage encounter she cannot reconstruct the morning after.
- *Hepatic consequence:* Never imaged on panel; presumptively fatty liver at minimum by the late Alias period in a baseline human with that intake. Whether her altered constitution offers any hepatoprotection is unknown; conservative read: no.
- *Cardiovascular:* Probable mild hypertension by late Alias; never measured.
- *Dental:* Erosion consistent with beer pH and bruxism.
- *Withdrawal:* No depicted episodes of frank DTs, but she has presumably never been abstinent long enough to test that floor — until pregnancy.
- *Pregnancy abstinence:* Achieved, with clear distress, suggesting both motivated capacity and the magnitude of the prior dependence. Relapse pattern post-partum: stress-cued, partial, controlled-then-uncontrolled cycles.
- *Function:* The alcohol is, throughout, the principal regulatory substrate for her PTSD. Removing it without substitute regulation has never been sustainably attempted in canon. This is the most important untreated medical fact in her file.

**Tobacco.** Heavy smoking through early *Alias*; reduces over the run; near-elimination by pregnancy. Pulmonary consequences sub-clinical, but the bronchitis-vulnerability cough of a former pack-a-day smoker is part of her sound.

**Caffeine.** Continuous, heavy, low-quality coffee. The office machine is a fixture.

**Illicit substances.** No depicted use. Notable: in a milieu (PI work, cape adjacency, MGH cases) where access is trivial, she has not gone there. The alcohol is her sole pharmacological vector. This restraint reflects, I assess, an unconscious protection of the **agency-over-own-body** imperative — she will degrade herself with a substance she controls; she will not introduce one whose effects she does not.

**Prescribed psychiatric medication.** None ever depicted. Given the symptom load, this is a glaring absence — not because canon has overlooked it but because she has refused or never sought the encounter. The reasons are overdetermined: institutional mistrust, fear of chemical alteration of consciousness post-Killgrave (a drug given by a doctor is, schematically, a less violent Killgrave), the cost of articulating her history to a stranger, and the operational identity built around tolerating untreated suffering as evidence of self-sufficiency.

---

## VII. OBSTETRIC AND GYNECOLOGICAL HISTORY

**Pregnancy:** Conceived with Luke Cage; carried Danielle Cage to term. The pregnancy was the **first sustained medicalization of her adult life** — prenatal visits, ultrasounds, weight monitoring, the entire apparatus she had previously refused, now accepted under the categorical imperative of the fetus. She was, by reports inferable from *Pulse* and *New Avengers*, a difficult patient: anxious, asking questions that no obstetrician has training to answer ("what if the baby has my strength in utero," "what if the durability is partial — does it protect a placenta"), refusing certain reassurances, accepting others with visible suspicion.

**Course:** Physically uneventful. No depicted hyperemesis, no gestational diabetes, no pre-eclampsia. The metahuman constitution appears to have offered no special obstetric complication, which is itself notable — and which she will not have trusted until the baby was out and breathing.

**Delivery:** Live birth, full term, healthy infant. Mode (vaginal vs. C-section) not canonically specified to my recall; either is plausible.

**Lactation:** Implied successful breastfeeding in *New Avengers* domestic scenes.

**Postpartum:** Classic hypervigilant new-parent anxiety overlaid on chronic PTSD — a brutal pharmacological combination, since neither the trauma nor the perinatal anxiety was treated. The Skrull-Jarvis abduction of Danielle during *Secret Invasion* is, in the body's accounting, a postpartum nightmare actualized — the unconscious fear of every new mother that an impostor will take the child, made literal. The somatic effects (sleeplessness, startle, appetite collapse, freeze-then-rage) persisted for months and were managed, predictably, with the return of alcohol.

**Subsequent gynecological care:** Sparse to nonexistent in canon. Whether contraception is in use post-Danielle, whether routine screening is current — unknown. The pattern of her engagement with medicine predicts: no.

---

## VIII. PSYCHOGENIC AND TRAUMA-CODED SOMATICS

**Sleep architecture.** Profoundly disrupted. Insomnia of mixed pattern: difficulty initiating sleep (cognitively, the day will not stop), difficulty maintaining sleep (nightmares, fragmentary, alluded to obliquely in *Alias*), early morning awakening (depressive signature). The office couch is her preferred sleep surface — smaller, more enclosed, lower than the bed, with the door visible. This is a trauma-coded sleep ergonomics: she sleeps where she can see the entrance.

**Startle.** Heightened. Acoustic startle particularly to voice — a Killgrave-coded modality. Visual startle to the color purple (operationally she has trained out the more obvious reactions; the autonomic flicker remains).

**Sexual function.** Trauma-impacted. Encounters depicted in *Alias* are joyless, often dissociative; she goes elsewhere mentally during sex with partners she does not trust and frequently with partners she does. With Cage, over the course of years, this improves — embodied intimacy becomes possible in narrow channels, but is never the default reflex. Anorgasmia or hypoorgasmic states inferable but not panel-confirmed.

**Appetite.** Variable; stress-suppressed. She forgets to eat and is reminded by Malcolm, later by Cage. The eating pattern of someone whose interoception was deranged by captivity.

**Pain tolerance.** Markedly elevated — by durability, by drink, and by trained dissociation. She underreports injury reliably. The clinical hazard of this is real: she is the patient who will arrive septic because the original infection was "nothing."

**Voice and respiration.** The smoker's lower register; the shallow upper-chest breathing of chronic hypervigilance; sighing exhalation as a habitual self-regulation move.

**Autonomic baseline.** Sympathetic-dominant. Resting heart rate likely elevated for an athletically built adult of her size. Cold hands. The thermoregulatory signature of someone who runs on cortisol.

---

## IX. WHAT THE FILE DOES NOT CONTAIN — AND WHY THAT IS A FINDING

- **No comprehensive metahuman physical of record.** No baseline established for the body she actually has.
- **No psychiatric care of record.** No trial of SSRI, prazosin for nightmares, naltrexone for the alcohol, no trauma-focused therapy (EMDR, CPT, PE), no formal AA engagement depicted.
- **No primary care.** No GP, no dentist of record, no gynecologist beyond the pregnancy episode.
- **No advance directives.** A woman who has been in two long comas and has a child has, to canon's knowledge, executed no health-care proxy. Cage is the de facto next-of-kin by marriage; the document does not exist.

The absence is the diagnosis. She has organized her medical life as a continuation of the hospital room nobody visited: care will not come; therefore, do not require care; therefore, do not be the kind of body that requires it. The drinking, the under-treated injuries, the avoided physical, the un-set knuckles, the missing prescriptions — all of it is one coherent posture, which is the posture of someone protecting herself against the next institutional disappointment by preemptively requiring nothing of any institution at all.

**Prognostic note.** The trajectory bends slowly. Danielle is the only sustained reason the subject has been observed modifying medical behavior (the pregnancy abstinence, the prenatal compliance). Any future medical engagement that has a chance of taking will route through that motivational channel — *care of self as a precondition of care of the child* — rather than through any appeal to the subject's own welfare, which she does not, at the somatic level, believe she deserves.

*End §3.2. Continue to §3.3 — Substance Use Detailed Timeline.*


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS — SUBJECT: JESSICA CAMPBELL JONES

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, third-party witness statements (Cage, L.; Ducasse, M.; Murdock, M.; Walker, P.), case-incidental photography, surveillance pulls from Avengers Tower interior cameras 2005–10, and the subject's own panels of self-narration. Cross-referenced against the canonical visual record (Gaydos line, 2001–18; Deodato/Maleev guest periods).*

---

## I. THE BODY AT REST: BASELINE ARCHITECTURE

**Build.** Approximately 5'7", solidly built, somatic mesomorph reading slightly hard for her apparent weight — observer reports consistently underestimate her density by ten to fifteen pounds, which is the chemical exposure's quiet residue (muscle fiber and bone are denser than baseline human). She does not look like a person who can lift a sedan. She is aware of this and uses it: the asymmetry between presentation and capacity is one of her few unambiguous pleasures.

**Default posture standing.** Weight loaded slightly to the left leg; right hip cocked; shoulders carried forward of the spinal axis by perhaps an inch and a half — a protective rounding around the sternum that predates the Killgrave period (visible in the few extant Jewel-era images, less pronounced) and deepened during the captivity. The head sits forward of the shoulders. Chin tucked when listening, lifted only when issuing contempt. She does not "stand up straight" in any setting — not in court, not before Jameson, not at Avengers debriefs. Refusal of the parade-rest body is a small ongoing assertion.

**Default posture seated.** At her desk: slouched low, sacrum forward, lumbar against the chair back, feet braced on the bottom drawer or the desk frame, knees apart in a posture coded male in the period observers describe. Elbows tend to plant; hands either cradle a glass or perform the cigarette-or-pen rotation described below. In another's space (Cage's couch, Carol's kitchen, an interview chair): the slouch contracts inward — knees together, ankles crossed, arms folded across the torso. The space-claim collapses in inverse proportion to felt safety, which is the opposite of the typical pattern and is itself diagnostic: she expands where she controls, contracts where she does not, because expansion in uncontrolled space is a visibility she will not offer.

**Default posture in bed.** Curled, left side, knees drawn up, one arm under the pillow, the other across the chest — a self-holding configuration. After Cage: sleeps closer to the edge of the bed than he does, even in their own apartment; will occupy roughly one-third of a queen mattress when not actively touching him.

---

## II. GAIT, LOCOMOTION, AND THE REFUSAL OF FLIGHT

**Walk.** Long stride for her height, heel-strike heavy, audible on hardwood — she does not move quietly when not trying to, which is the privilege of a body that does not have to fear being heard. Hands typically in jacket pockets or one in pocket and one swinging; rarely both swinging. Pace varies bimodally: New York fast (faster than crowd pace, weaving) or stalled-still; very little intermediate.

**Stair use.** Takes stairs two at a time going up when alone, one at a time going down. Will not use the elevator in her own building if it requires waiting more than thirty seconds; the wait-state is intolerable.

**Running.** Runs only under operational necessity. Form is unschooled — arms cross the body midline, head bobs, breathing audible. She has the cardiovascular capacity of an enhanced subject but the technique of someone who never played a sport.

**Jumping/leaping.** Used in lieu of flight wherever possible. Crouch-and-spring rather than the running takeoff most flyers use. Lands in a three-point posture (one knee, one foot, one hand) that she has clearly drilled, then stands quickly — does not linger in the hero-landing because the hero-landing is for being seen.

**Flight — pattern and avoidance.** Logged in-flight events across the corpus are conspicuously rare relative to her capability. When she does fly: posture is feet-first rather than the prone Superman line, arms held tight to the torso, fists loosely closed, face strained. Altitude rarely above fifty feet. Duration typically under thirty seconds. She refers to it as controlled falling and the descriptor is accurate to the kinesics — there is a permanent micro-flinch at takeoff. *Operational note:* the body capacity is associatively contaminated by the Killgrave period (he summoned her by air) and by the Jewel period (she flew in costume). The non-use is not modesty; it is a phobic-grade avoidance encapsulated in the limb-set of takeoff.

**Combat locomotion.** Closes distance fast and low, leads with the right shoulder, throws with the right hand. She is technically ambidextrous-strong but has never trained out the dominant-side commitment. Footwork untrained — she plants and punches rather than circling. Wins by exceeding her opponent's durability budget, not by skill. Will absorb hits she could have slipped, which observers (Cage, in particular) read as not-caring-about-the-body — a hypothesis the dossier accepts.

---

## III. HANDS, FACE, AND THE LEXICON OF MICRO-MOVEMENT

**Hands at rest.** Almost never at rest. The right hand is the operator. Cycles through: cigarette (early *Alias* period, daily); pen-and-thumb roll over the knuckles; rim-circling of whatever glass is in front of her; thumb scraping the pad of the index finger as if testing tackiness. Nails kept short, not manicured, occasionally bitten at the cuticle under stress (visible damage on the right thumb and right index across multiple panels). Knuckles show old scar tissue, particularly across the right second and third metacarpals — striking-surface wear inconsistent with civilian life, consistent with hitting things harder than fists were designed to hit.

**Hands when speaking.** Limited gesticulation; she is a verbal communicator, not a manual one. The hand that does move tends to chop downward in flat planes when emphatic, or to flick dismissively at the wrist when contemptuous. She does not point at people. She does point at objects.

**Hands in intimacy.** With Cage: hand placement is unusual — she will often grip his forearm or bicep rather than take his hand, which is a containment grip rather than a clasp. When she does hold his hand it is brief and broken first by her. With Danielle: hands transformed — open palm, full surface contact, slow strokes through hair, the back of the index finger against the cheek. The maternal hand vocabulary is entirely absent from any other relationship.

**Face — baseline.** Resting expression reads flat-to-skeptical; mouth slightly downturned but not tight; eyebrows neutral but with a tendency to draw together at the inner corner — a faint perpetual concern-knot above the bridge of the nose that smooths only in sleep and in two other documented states (looking at Danielle; on the rare unguarded laugh).

**Eyes.** Direct contact, prolonged, used as a pressure instrument. She does not break gaze first in confrontation. With intimates she breaks gaze readily and often, looking down-left (the canonical recollection direction) when discussing the past, down-right when computing tactical options. Pupil response to threat is fast and large — observers in the Killgrave confrontation note dilated pupils sustained for the duration. Blink rate suppressed under stress (a freeze residue), normal-to-elevated when bored or social.

**Mouth.** The most expressive feature. The half-smile at one corner — left side — is the load-bearing affect signal: present in dry humor, in flirtation with Cage, in the moment of catching a lie. The full smile is rare and asymmetrical, top lip riding higher on the left. Teeth not perfect — small chip on the right lateral incisor, undated, undisclosed. The mouth tightens before a punch, before a denial, before tears.

**Eyebrow vocabulary.** Single-brow lift (right) — skepticism, the standard interview tool. Double-brow lift — surprise, rare. Inner-corner pull — distress, often suppressed elsewhere on the face but visible here for anyone watching the eyebrows, which most observers do not.

**Jaw.** Clenches under stress, visible at the masseter. Bruxism likely (asymmetric wear pattern would be consistent; dental records unavailable). She rubs the right side of her jaw with two fingers when thinking — a self-soothing tic that doubles as a tell.

**Head tilt.** Slight right tilt when listening to something she does not believe. Slight left tilt when listening to something that interests her. Chin-jut forward when challenged. The head almost never moves in agreement; she nods rarely and reluctantly, preferring verbal acknowledgment or none.

---

## IV. VOCAL AND RESPIRATORY PATTERN

**Voice.** Alto, slightly hoarse — smoke residue and a baseline of insufficient hydration. Volume modulated low; she gets quieter, not louder, when angry, which is the inversion that throws people who expect escalation to be loud. Cadence is New York-clipped, dropped Gs, glottal stops on terminal Ts. Speech rate elevated under social pressure (fills space to prevent others' speech), slowed and deliberate in interrogation.

**Profanity.** Distributed densely and functionally; not decorative. She swears at situations more than at people. Use of *fuck* is rhythmically positioned mid-sentence as an intensifier; rarely sentence-initial except in startle. She does not swear in front of Danielle and has retrained successfully.

**Laughter.** Three distinct registers documented. (1) The exhaled half-laugh through the nose — contempt or recognition of irony, the most frequent. (2) The single bark — surprise at someone else's wit, usually Cage's or Malcolm's. (3) The full laugh — rare, observed perhaps a dozen times across the corpus, head back, eyes closing, hand sometimes covering the mouth in a gesture she would deny making. The full laugh produces a brief subsequent embarrassment-affect: she will often immediately drink, look away, or insult something to discharge it.

**Breathing.** Resting respiration shallow and clavicular rather than diaphragmatic — a chronic upper-chest pattern consistent with sustained sympathetic tone. Sighs heavily and audibly, multiple times per hour. Holds breath when concentrating on small motor tasks (lockpicking, signing forms) and forgets to release until the task completes. Under acute stress: breath hold, then a sharp inhale through the nose, then deliberate slow exhale through the mouth — a self-regulation she has clearly developed without instruction, by trial.

---

## V. GROOMING, DRESS, AND THE BODY'S PRESENTATION

**Hair.** Dark, shoulder-length to mid-back depending on era, almost always loose. Washed irregularly in the *Alias* period — twice weekly at best, observable oil at the parting by day three. Brushed by hand more often than with a brush. Tied back only when working at the desk or in active combat — a thin elastic kept on the right wrist at all times, a permanent fixture observers consistently note. Color: undyed. No salon contact established in the financial record.

**Skin.** Pale, freckling across the bridge of the nose and the tops of the shoulders. Sun-avoidant by accident rather than design (indoor life). Minor scarring: thin line above the left eyebrow (undated); the previously noted knuckle scars; a longer scar along the lateral right thigh from the original accident, visible only in intimate context. No tattoos. No piercings beyond once-pierced earlobes, holes closed.

**Makeup.** None routinely. Occasional concealer under the eyes for daylight court appearances. Lipstick documented twice across two decades, both for funerals.

**Wardrobe — the uniform.** Dark jeans (slightly loose, never tight); a T-shirt or thermal under a leather jacket — the jacket scuffed, worn at the cuffs, three-quarter length, dark. Boots, lace-up, ankle to mid-calf, with tread; replaced approximately every eighteen months per receipt pattern. Underlayer typically gray, black, or faded purple-adjacent navy (*she will not wear true purple; the absence of the color from her wardrobe is total and dates from the Killgrave year*). Bra always functional, never decorative. Underwear unremarkable, cotton.

**The Jewel costume.** Stored, not destroyed, in a sealed bag at the back of the closet. The non-destruction is itself a datum: she cannot bring herself to look at it but she cannot get rid of it. A controlled phobic object, contained but retained.

**Scent.** Cigarettes (early period); whiskey; cheap soap, drugstore unscented; the leather of the jacket. No perfume. Cage's apartment, post-cohabitation, contributes a secondary signature (his cologne, his cooking) that lingers on her clothes after overnight stays in a way she does not seem to notice.

**Accessories.** Watch, cheap, analog, worn on the left wrist with the face turned inward — a habit from the *Alias* period when she did not want to look casual about checking the time. Keys on a carabiner clipped to a belt loop. Wallet in the back pocket, men's bifold. No jewelry except, post-marriage, a plain band, and she removes it only for combat. No necklaces, no earrings.

---

## VI. INGESTION: ALCOHOL, NICOTINE, FOOD, CAFFEINE

**Alcohol.** Across the *Alias* period: daily intake variable but high — beer through the day (Bud, in the bottle, room temperature tolerated), whiskey at night (rail, neat, water back rarely). Peak intake episodes precede sleep and follow Killgrave-coded stimuli. Drinking posture: glass held in the right hand, thumb on the rim, sip rate elevated when listening, suppressed when speaking. Bottle drinking: held by the neck, never the body. She is functional drunk — speech intact, gait minimally altered — until a threshold past which she goes quiet and still rather than sloppy. The quiet phase is the dangerous one (judgment compromised without observable signs).

Post-pregnancy: marked reduction, not abstinence. Wine introduced as a controlled alternative. Whiskey reserved for crisis. Relapse pattern: a single decision to have one, followed by serial reordering, followed by 36–72 hours of suppressed drinking before re-stabilization.

**Nicotine.** Heavy in early *Alias* — pack-plus daily, brand inconsistent, lit with a cheap lighter she loses constantly. Held between the right index and middle finger, smoked to the filter. Quit episodically; the cessation always coincides with a deliberate self-improvement attempt (a new case, a date, the pregnancy). Returns under stress.

**Food.** Pattern is irregular and primarily functional. Eats standing, eats from containers, eats one large meal late rather than three structured ones. Preferences: diner food, takeout Chinese, pizza by the slice eaten folded. Will skip a meal without noticing. Does not cook beyond toast and eggs. The kitchen at Alias is observably underused; the refrigerator contents are documented in *Alias* as predominantly beer.

Post-Danielle: a reorganization. Sits at a table when feeding the baby; began to keep produce; learned three additional recipes from Cage. The mothering pulls her toward routine eating in a way nothing else has managed.

**Caffeine.** Heavy. Coffee black, no sugar, drunk hot until cold then drunk cold without remark. Multiple cups per case. Replaces breakfast.

**Water.** Inadequate. The hoarseness, the skin, the headaches she rubs at without naming all index a chronic mild dehydration she has lived inside so long it reads as baseline.

---

## VII. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

**Schedule.** Non-circadian. Sleeps when collapse forces it. Bed times across the corpus range 2 a.m. to 6 a.m.; wake times 9 a.m. to 1 p.m. The office couch is a sleep surface roughly equal in use to the bed during the *Alias* period.

**Onset latency.** Long without alcohol; short with. The drinking-to-sleep equation is conscious and admitted.

**Architecture.** Reports (oblique, in dialogue) of nightmares; observed twitching and vocalization during sleep witnessed by Cage. REM disruption likely. Wakes multiple times per night, checks the door, returns to bed. Post-Danielle: wakes to the child preemptively, before the child cries — a hypervigilant maternal attunement layered over the prior hypervigilant baseline.

**Position.** Left-side curl with right arm across the chest. Will not sleep on her back. Will not sleep facing a door she cannot see. The bed at Alias was positioned to face the door from the pillow.

**Naps.** Rare; she does not nap deliberately. Microsleeps at the desk during long cases, head on the forearm, twenty to forty minutes.

---

## VIII. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE SOMATICS

**Pre-Killgrave (extrapolated).** Adolescent baseline limited; no significant data.

**Post-Killgrave, pre-Cage.** Encounters depicted as joyless and dissociative. The kinesics described and implied: passive participation, gaze averted or closed, post-coital withdrawal rapid (dresses, leaves, or asks the other to leave). Substance-mediated — she rarely entered an encounter sober. The dissociative quality is somatic: she is reportedly "elsewhere" during, a state observers cannot read in real time and which she does not narrate after.

**With Cage.** A progressive re-embodiment, slow, partial. Initial encounter (the Knightress-era hookup) was rough, mutually drunk, and not remembered in detail by either party. The *Alias* #1 reprise is the canonical low point — she enters dissociated and exits ashamed. The relationship's recovery is somatic before it is verbal: she lets him hold her in non-sexual contexts before she lets sex re-mean anything. By the marriage period the documented intimacy is reciprocal and embodied, with characteristic features: she initiates more often than expected; she is unselfconscious about her body with him in a way she is with no one else; she still occasionally checks out mid-act, which he has learned to read and to pause without comment. The repair is not complete; it is functional.

**Maternal somatics.** Carrying Danielle: she walks differently — slightly wider stance, more controlled stride, hand intermittently on the lower belly, a self-touch she does not perform elsewhere. Breastfeeding (period documented in *New Avengers*): she will not do it in front of male teammates, will do it in front of Carol. Holding the infant: left arm supports the body, right hand free — combat-ready, even cradling. The right hand never fully relinquishes operational availability.

---

## IX. STATE-DEPENDENT SHIFTS — THE GAZETTEER

**Calm (baseline-low arousal).** Slouch deepens; the left-corner half-smile is available; profanity rate declines; breathing slows toward diaphragmatic; the eyebrow knot smooths. Observed states: alone with Cage in the apartment; reading case files in the morning before phone calls begin; bathing Danielle.

**Working / focused.** Posture forward at the desk; jaw rub frequent; breath-hold cycles around task points; coffee replaces alcohol; speech to self in muttered fragments; office music absent (she works in silence). Eye contact with screens or paper unbroken for long intervals.

**Mild social stress (client, Jameson, casual interaction).** Profanity rate up; gesture economy down; arms cross or one hand finds the back pocket of the jeans; weight shifts more often between feet; cigarette or drink instrumentalized as a punctuation device. Eye contact direct, slightly aggressive. Half-smile weaponized.

**Moderate stress (active case, threat in environment, conflict with intimate).** Shoulders rise toward the ears; chin tucks; breath rate up but shallow; right hand seeks the jaw or the back of the neck; one shoulder blade often pressed to a wall when seated; she will choose the chair facing the door, always. Sleep that night will be short and alcohol-mediated.

**High stress / acute threat.** A two-stage response. Stage one: freeze, often missed by observers because it lasts under two seconds — eyes wide, breath suspended, weight on the back foot. Stage two: explosive forward motion, almost always physical, almost always disproportionate. The disproportion is the Killgrave inheritance: she will not be controlled, will not be paused, will end the threat with overwhelming force rather than risk being held in it.

**Killgrave-coded stimulus (purple, voice-compulsion, sexual coercion of a third party).** Documented decompensation. Color drains from the face; pupils blow wide; verbal output truncates or ceases; she may grip the nearest object hard enough to deform it. Followed within hours by drinking, withdrawal, often a punitive solo action that observers (Cage, Malcolm) have learned to anticipate and, when possible, intercept.

**Intimacy (Cage, Danielle, rarely Carol or Malcolm).** Shoulders drop; head finds a shoulder or a chest with surprising willingness once permission is established; the protective torso-cross unfolds; voice quietens and slows; the full laugh becomes available. She will often fall asleep in these states — sleep in another's presence is the most reliable index of trust she offers.

**Receiving praise or gratitude.** A near-allergic micro-sequence: brief widening of the eyes, immediate gaze break (down and away, right), a verbal deflection (often profane), a physical pivot away from the speaker, and frequently a small destructive act — a sip taken too fast, a cigarette stubbed, a subject change so sharp it embarrasses. She does not know how to stand inside a kind sentence and has not learned. This is one of the most reliable behavioral signatures in the file.

**Mothering state (with Danielle, observed).** The single condition under which the entire somatic baseline reorganizes. The forward shoulders square. The flat affect softens; the eye-knot smooths; the voice drops an octave into a register no one else hears. Hands move slowly, palms-open. She breathes through the diaphragm. The body she has refused to inhabit for two decades briefly becomes habitable, because someone smaller than her needs it to be.

---

*End SOMATIC ATLAS. Cross-reference §3 (Psychological) for affect-regulation substrate; §4 (Psychiatric) for the trauma physiology underwriting the hyperarousal signatures catalogued above; §6 (Routines & Rituals, forthcoming) for the temporal scaffolding into which these somatic patterns are slotted.*


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

## I. Foundational Architecture: How the Attachment System Was Built and Then Broken

The subject did not begin life with a damaged attachment system. The pre-accident Campbell household — engineer father, homemaker mother, younger brother Phillip, Forest Hills, lower-middle-class stability — provided what the developmental literature would call a "good enough" secure base through the first thirteen-odd years. Flashback panels in *Alias* (the road-trip sequence, the breakfast-table bickering with Phillip over Disneyland, the mother's casual hand on the back of her neck) depict a family with ordinary friction and ordinary affection. The subject's adolescent baseline was irritable, envious, and self-comparing — not pathologically insecure. She had the latent capacity to bond. This matters for the entire file: she is not avoidantly attached because she never learned love; she is avoidantly attached because love was taken from her three times in escalating modalities, and each loss instructed her in a different lesson about the cost of proximity.

**Loss 1 (annihilation).** The convoy collision killed her family in front of her. The lesson encoded: *the people you love can be erased in a single instant, by accident, while you survive arbitrarily.* This is the foundation of her survivor's guilt and of her chronic background expectation that catastrophe is imminent and not preventable by vigilance — a fatalism that coexists, contradictorily, with her hypervigilance.

**Loss 2 (substitution).** The Jones family adopted her into a household she experienced as a forgery of the lost original. She did not refuse them outright; she refused to let them count. She kept her powers secret from them for years — a refusal of disclosure that is, in attachment terms, a refusal of intimacy. The lesson encoded: *replacement bonds are insults to the dead; to accept them is to betray.* This is why every offered substitution later in life — the Avengers as family, the Bugle as workplace family, even Carol's well-meaning interventions — meets reflexive contempt before consideration.

**Loss 3 (colonization).** The Killgrave captivity is the wound that organizes the adult relational system. For eight months a powerful other did not merely abuse her; he occupied the executive function of her own will and used her body and her wanting as his instruments. He made her *want* to please him. He made her *want* him to violate her. The somatic and cognitive distinction between "my desire" and "his command" was systematically dissolved. The lesson encoded — and this is the operative one for every adult relationship — is the most catastrophic possible attachment lesson: *proximity to a powerful other annihilates the will; the closer you get, the less you exist; and worst of all, you may not be able to tell the difference while it is happening.*

The result is a textbook **fearful-avoidant (disorganized)** attachment configuration, with the trauma-specific overlay that she cannot fully trust her own felt sense of safety. A securely attached person knows when they feel safe. The subject does not. Killgrave taught her that her own affect can be manufactured by another. Every subsequent intimacy is therefore vetted not only against external behavior but against her own internal weather, which she has been instructed to mistrust.

## II. The Operational Signature of Her Attachment Style

Across two decades of canon her bonding behavior follows an identifiable signature, observable in encounter after encounter:

- **The prickly filter.** Initial contact is profane, dismissive, and visibly designed to make the other party leave. Examples: her first office encounters with Malcolm; the cold-shoulder treatment of Scott Lang's early date attempts; the deliberate rudeness to Carol after Carol becomes Captain Marvel; the way she greets potential clients with sighs and obvious reluctance. This is not random hostility. It is a **selection screen**: anyone who flees confirms her low expectation of human investment and costs her nothing; anyone who stays has demonstrated tolerance for her worst surface and earns provisional access.
- **The provisional access plateau.** Once admitted past the filter, the other party is held at a stable mid-distance for a long time. She will work alongside them, drink with them, share information about cases — but she will not volunteer interior content. Cage was sleeping with her for some time before she disclosed anything substantive about the Killgrave period; Malcolm worked at Alias for months before she told him anything personal that was not extracted under duress.
- **The asymmetric disclosure ratchet.** When she finally discloses, it tends to happen under pressure (an external event forces it) and arrives in compressed, unmodulated form — a flat-voiced data dump rather than a gradual sharing. The *Alias* "Purple" arc contains the cardinal example: she tells Cage about Killgrave in a single brutal monologue, then immediately disengages, drinks, and avoids him.
- **The disappearance.** At unpredictable intervals, once intimacy has built past a threshold she cannot tolerate, she vanishes. She stops answering calls. She sleeps at the office. She picks a fight that lets her storm out. The Bendis 2016 arc is the apotheosis of this pattern: she fakes a separation from her husband, abandons her child, alienates Carol, and accepts incarceration rather than allow any of them to help her. The narrative gives her a legitimate undercover reason, but the *form* of the response — solitary, deceptive, self-sacrificing, structurally identical to her acute stress response — reveals that the operational mission was metabolizing a familiar attachment-rupture script. She converted a crisis into the relational shape she knows.
- **The silent return.** Reunions after her disappearances are notable for what is absent: there is no extended repair conversation, no apology architecture, no processing. She simply reappears, behaves as if nothing happened, and dares the other party to make it an issue. Cage, after years, has learned to let this work; Carol has not, which is why the Carol relationship cycles through ruptures the Cage relationship survives.

## III. The Specific Bonds: A Granular Mapping

### Luke Cage — the load-bearing attachment

The Cage relationship is the most successful intimate bond she has ever sustained, and its success is explicable entirely through its structural compatibility with her injury. The seeding encounter was a one-night stand on the night they met as costumed operators; she initiated it during her Knightress period, then could not face him the next morning. The second encounter (*Alias* #1) was a self-loathing reprise: she went to his bar, asked for sex, did not stay. He did not pursue her, did not call, did not perform hurt or expectation. **This non-pursuit is what made him eligible.** A man who chased her would have been coded as Killgrave-shaped — *wanting* her in a way that demanded she perform a response. Cage's stillness, his refusal to assign her affect, his willingness to wait, registered to her nervous system as the inverse of coercion.

Their bonding accelerated through co-action rather than co-disclosure. They worked cases adjacent to each other; they shared physical space; they had sex without commentary on the sex. The intimacy was somatic and procedural before it was verbal. When she did finally disclose Killgrave to him, his response — controlled rage on her behalf, no demand that she comfort him about it, no request that she elaborate — was a near-perfect match for what the injury required. He has, across hundreds of pages, repeated this stance: he allows her to be ugly without metabolizing it as a verdict on himself. He does not personalize her withdrawals. He maintains continuity of regard across her discontinuities. He is, in attachment-repair terms, an unusually skillful corrective experience.

The pregnancy and marriage stress-tested this. She did not handle either with grace. She drank during ambivalence about the pregnancy; she resisted the wedding; she did not stop being prickly with him after Danielle's birth. He did not require her to perform a transformation. Their domestic rhythm — observable across *New Avengers* and *Pulse* — is structured around mutual permission to be unimpressed by each other. They do not romanticize. They share parenting logistics, eat takeout, snap and forgive without ceremony. **This is what her capacity for intimacy looks like at maximum: not effusion, but continuous low-grade presence with permission to be a difficult organism.**

The 2016 arc, in which she lied to him and faked separation, is the dark mirror. Even with the partner who has earned every credential of trust, her acute-stress default is *protect by isolating, even if it destroys him to be isolated from*. The arc demonstrates that her attachment injury is not curable by good partnership; it is only manageable in steady state. Under high enough load she will still execute the original script.

### Daughter (Danielle) — the reparative attachment

Danielle is the relationship that has reorganized her interior in ways no adult bond has accomplished. The reparative logic is precise: she gives her daughter the present-tense attention, physical safety, and unconditional regard that were severed when her own parents died and that Killgrave inverted during her captivity. With Danielle she is gentle in a register she displays nowhere else — physical tenderness without irony, baby-talk that she would mock in others, a willingness to sit and watch the child sleep.

The hypervigilance load on this attachment is, however, enormous. She catastrophizes every threat. The Skrull-Jarvis abduction during *Secret Invasion* confirmed her worst background expectation (loved ones can be erased instantly), and the choice to hand Danielle to Squirrel Girl as nanny — tactically optimal, emotionally a relinquishment under duress — is a small re-enactment of her own adoptive displacement, this time with her as the parent making the decision rather than the child suffering it. She acted out the only template she knew (the parent-figure removes the child to safety, even at cost of presence), but inverted its moral valence by *choosing* it deliberately.

She is at chronic risk of two opposite parenting failures: over-protective restriction (treating Danielle as the precious-object site of all her ungrievable losses) and self-deprecating distance ("I'm a bad mother" as preemptive devaluation, a defensive operation she runs on every domain of her life). The canon shows her oscillating between these poles. What she is good at is the third thing: being unembarrassed about her daughter, not performing maternal identity for an audience, being present without commentary.

### Malcolm Ducasse — the chosen-sibling attachment

Malcolm — the neighbor turned assistant turned chosen kin — represents her capacity for low-stakes durable bond, the kind she could not form when offered the Joneses as substitute family. The structural difference: she chose him, slowly, and the bond was built around shared work. He saw her at her worst (drunk on the office couch, vomiting, locked out of her own life) in their first encounters; the absence of horror or pity in his response was the credential. He runs the same operating system as Cage in miniature: continuity of regard without performative concern.

She mentors him in a register she does not allow with peers — there is a hierarchical asymmetry (she is the senior operator) that makes the bond safe, because she is not vulnerable to being controlled by him. The drive to *protect the weaker party in the room* attaches him to her in a way that bypasses her usual filters. She lets him into Danielle's orbit, which is the highest trust credential she issues.

### Carol Danvers — the cyclically ruptured peer attachment

The Carol bond is the test case for her with-a-peer-of-equal-power capacity, and it fails repeatedly, in instructive ways. Pre-Killgrave, Carol was a presence at the Avengers periphery; the cardinal trauma was that during the Killgrave-controlled attack, she misidentified the Scarlet Witch and beat Carol nearly to death — and Carol, not knowing about the mind control, registered her as a villain and was part of the hospital silence afterward. The wound is therefore double-coded: Carol is both a person she nearly killed and a person who failed to come check on her.

Their adult friendship operates on a thin layer of brittle ice over this. Carol is one of the few people the subject permits to give her advice, drag her sober, attend her wedding, watch her child. But every few arcs the ice cracks: Carol presumes too much, the subject reads it as being handled, withdraws contemptuously, Carol reads the withdrawal as betrayal, the bond ruptures. The 2016 arc is the most severe instance — the subject's undercover deception alienated Carol completely, and the relationship had to be rebuilt afterward at a lower trust setting.

The Carol relationship reveals what the Cage relationship insulates her from: with a peer who is also high-agency, who will *act* on concern rather than wait, her control-preservation drive collides head-on with the other party's competence. She cannot tolerate being helped efficiently. Carol's strength as a person is the precise stimulus that activates the subject's Killgrave-coded defense against being moved by another's will.

### Matt Murdock and the costumed-world peers — the contemptuous-compliant register

With Murdock, with the wider street-level community, with Daredevil-orbit allies, she operates a third register: professional respect, episodic collaboration, no disclosure. Murdock represents what she might have been had she stayed in capes — a fellow trauma-organized operator who chose the opposite resolution (public identity, religious framework, theatrical commitment to costume). She is alternately drawn to him and repelled. There has been mild flirtation depicted; it has never actualized, in part because his style — confessional, dramatic, morally legalistic — is precisely the register she finds insufferable. He talks about his suffering. She does not.

### Jessica Drew — the parallel-name peer

Brief but worth flagging: the Drew relationship is friendly-functional, low-disclosure, structured around shared exhaustion. They are two women with violently overlapping names and overlapping histories of being weaponized by external actors. The bond is sister-soldier in tone, not intimate. It is one of the few peer bonds without rupture, precisely because it operates at a deliberately shallow depth.

### J. Jonah Jameson — the authority template

Jameson is the cardinal exhibit of her authority-relations pattern: contemptuous-compliant, she takes his money and does the job while refusing his frame. She will not be praised by him, will not be flattered, will not perform gratitude. She lets him exploit her (the *Pulse* employment) because the transaction is legible: he wants labor, she wants the paycheck, no one is pretending it is more. The pattern repeats with SHIELD, with Avengers leadership, with anyone in a hierarchical position above her. She can collaborate; she cannot be led.

### Zebediah Killgrave — the negative attachment, never fully extinguished

The Killgrave bond is, in the technical attachment-trauma sense, the most intense relational template she carries. It is the relationship every other relationship is measured against by absence. She tracks his presence in the world with vigilance that exceeds operational necessity. When she confronts him in person (the *Alias* climax), her victory condition is not violence but **affective regulation** — refusing to give him a reaction he can metabolize. This is the most psychologically sophisticated moment in her published canon, and it works because she has finally located the one form of agency he cannot strip: the refusal to be moved.

The Purple Children arc reactivates the template. As long as Killgrave-coded stimuli exist in her world, the bond persists negatively. She does not have a fantasy of his death that resolves her; she has a chronic background expectation of his return.

### The lost family — the unmourned attachment

Phillip, her mother, her father: barely depicted in canon, almost never discussed by her. This silence is itself a relational pattern. She has not done the work of mourning them in the open. The grief is encysted, accessible only obliquely (a flicker in flashback, the way she handles Danielle at the age Phillip was). The unmourned dead are an attachment load she carries continuously without acknowledging it, and this is part of why anniversary periods, family-coded holidays, and Forest Hills as a location are depicted as destabilizing whenever they surface.

## IV. The Template, Stated Plainly

Every adult relationship in her file follows a recognizable five-beat sequence:

1. **Filter.** She presents her worst surface to screen out anyone insufficient.
2. **Plateau.** Provisional access at fixed mid-distance, with intimacy expressed through co-action rather than disclosure.
3. **Pressured disclosure.** Under external duress, a flat compressed data-dump of interior content, followed by immediate disengagement.
4. **Disappearance.** At an intimacy threshold she cannot regulate, she withdraws — by silence, by drink, by picking a fight, by undertaking a solo mission that requires deception of the loved party.
5. **Silent return.** Reappearance without repair conversation, daring the other party to absorb the gap.

The bonds that survive are those held by people who can tolerate beats four and five without retaliating. Cage, Malcolm, and (with high cost and cyclical failure) Carol have demonstrated this tolerance. Most others have not. The pattern is not chosen; it is the somatic logic of an organism that learned, at twenty-something, that being known is being captured.

## V. How She Distrusts, Betrays, and Repairs

**Distrust** is her baseline, not her exception. It does not present as paranoia — she is not scanning for plots — but as a refusal to extend the benefit of the doubt about motive. She assumes self-interest in others not because she has theorized it but because she has been instrumentalized once at catastrophic depth, and the nervous system generalized. She tests through provocation: she will say something contemptuous and watch what the other party does with it.

**Betrayal**, when she commits it, takes a specific form: she lies by omission to protect, almost never to gain. The 2016 arc is the paradigm — she lied to her husband, abandoned her child, fabricated a separation, all in service of a protective mission. She does not betray for advantage. She betrays by unilaterally deciding that the loved party is safer not knowing, which is itself a Killgrave-coded inversion (deciding for another what they will be permitted to know about reality). She has not fully reckoned with this isomorphism.

**Repair** is her weakest competence. She does not apologize in extended form. She does not narrate her processing. She returns, acts normal, and trusts the other party to read her continued presence as the apology. With partners who can read this, it works. With partners who require articulated repair, it does not. She is repair-illiterate not from indifference but because the period of her life in which she would have learned adult repair skills was the period Killgrave occupied. She missed that developmental window and has been improvising ever since.

The integrative observation: her relational system is not broken. It is functioning exactly as designed by the events that built it. The remarkable datum is not that she struggles with intimacy; it is that, given the curriculum she was forced to study, she has maintained *any* sustained intimate bonds at all — a husband, a child, a chosen brother, a contested best friend. Each of these is a small daily victory against the lesson Killgrave taught her, and each is held in place by her own ongoing, exhausting, unacknowledged work.


## Defenses & Compensatory Mechanisms

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION: DEFENSES & COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

**Subject:** Jones, Jessica Campbell (Jewel; Knightress; Power Woman; prop. Alias Investigations)
**Section scope:** Complete map of the defensive architecture — primitive through mature — with operational examples, somatic correlates, situational triggers, decay curves, and the compensatory scaffolding (positive and negative) that holds the structure upright.

---

## 1. STRUCTURAL OVERVIEW

Subject's defensive system is best understood not as a flat inventory but as a **tiered fortification** built in three historical strata, each laid down over the previous without demolishing it:

- **Stratum I (pre-accident, age 0–~15):** ordinary suburban neurotic defenses — comparison, envy, sullen withdrawal, ordinary adolescent rationalization. Still detectable as a substrate.
- **Stratum II (post-accident through Jewel through Killgrave, ~15–~22):** trauma-specific defenses bolted on after the convoy crash and then catastrophically reinforced by eight months of pheromonal captivity. This is the load-bearing tier. Primitive defenses (dissociation, splitting-off of specific self-states, projective elements) live here.
- **Stratum III (Alias period onward, ~22+):** the constructed adult persona — the leather jacket, the whiskey, the sneer, the office on the bad block. Functions as **a costume more total than the Jewel costume ever was**, because she experiences it as authentic. It is in fact a highly elaborated reaction-formation against the Jewel self, sealed with cynicism and irony.

The three strata interact: Stratum III collapses fastest under Killgrave-coded stimuli (decompensates to Stratum II); Stratum II collapses under threats to Danielle (decompensates to a rawer, almost Stratum-I maternal panic, only with Class 50 strength behind it).

---

## 2. PRIMITIVE DEFENSES (Vaillant Level I — psychotic / Level II — immature)

These are deployed automatically, without insight, usually under acute load.

### 2.1 Dissociation (peritraumatic and chronic-residual)

The single most consequential defense in the file. Established somatically during two long comas (post-accident, post-Vision/Iron Man beating) and rehearsed for eight months under Killgrave, where her body was instrumentalized while her witnessing self had nowhere to retreat **but inward**. The result:

- **Sexual dissociation.** Encounters in the *Alias* period are routinely described or depicted with elided sensory detail — the morning-after with Cage in *Alias* #1 is the cardinal example; she does not so much "forget" as never fully encode. The pattern is **derealization during embodied intimacy**, not memory failure.
- **Affective numbing as default state.** Long stretches of low-key anhedonia broken by spike-rage are the surface of a chronic dissociative baseline. She often does not know what she feels until she has already acted on it.
- **Time-loss correlates with alcohol but precedes it.** Drinking exploits a pre-existing dissociative substrate; she would dissociate sober, less efficiently.
- **Purple-coded stimuli produce freeze-then-explode** — a hallmark dissociative-trauma response curve, not ordinary fear.

### 2.2 Splitting (limited, contained — not BPD-grade)

Not characterological splitting. Object-relations are integrated; she holds Cage, Carol, even Killgrave as whole-objects (good-and-bad simultaneously). The splitting that DOES occur is **self-directed and historical**: the Jewel-self and the post-Killgrave-self are walled off from each other as if they were different people, with the wall maintained by contempt for the former. She can mock "Jewel" affectionately on a good day and cannot say the word on a bad one.

### 2.3 Projection (selective)

She projects **her own contempt for herself onto others** and then responds to the imagined contempt as if it were real. Operational examples:

- Assumes Carol Danvers blames her for the Killgrave-era attack; behaves accordingly; corrodes the friendship before testing the assumption.
- Assumes Cage's mother, his friends, the school other parents, see her as the unworthy partner; pre-emptively withdraws from PTA-coded settings.
- Assumes clients see her as a fraud; charges them as if they did.

Does **not** project malevolence outward in paranoid fashion — the projection is shame-shaped, not persecutory.

### 2.4 Acting-out

The classic immature defense, well-represented:

- **Drinking-to-action** — pre-loading whiskey before a stakeout or a hard conversation.
- **Punching as conversation** — closing arguments with violence when verbal closure feels unsafe (Killgrave taught her words were rigged).
- **Sexual acting-out in the *Alias* period** — choosing partners she disrespects, so that the act itself can be filed under contempt rather than vulnerability.
- **The 2016 undercover gambit** — entire arc reads as a maxi-scale acting-out: rather than tell Cage what she suspects about the Purple Children network, she stages a separation, accepts jail, and burns her relationships, because doing is tolerable where saying is not.

### 2.5 Passive aggression

Pervasive in low-stakes settings. Late to meetings she resents. Closes her office door on potential clients she's decided she dislikes inside three seconds. Answers Jameson's calls with calibrated insolence — never enough to be fired, always enough to register the protest. The defense lets her register objection without the vulnerability of a direct refusal that might be denied.

### 2.6 Somatization

Insomnia, headaches implied around triggers, the chronic alcohol-mediated gastric/sleep complaints, smoker's cough in early *Alias*. The body holds what she will not name; the drinking is partly an attempt to renegotiate the somatic load.

### 2.7 Devaluation (disguised as humor)

This is the most-misread defense in her file. Her "humor" is **not** the mature humor of Vaillant's top tier — it is devaluation in punchline form. It works by lowering the status of the object (a cape, a client, herself, the room) until it no longer threatens her. True mature humor preserves the dignity of its target; her wit usually does not. The exceptions — gentle teasing with Malcolm, dry warmth with Danielle, sex-banter with Cage when she feels safe — are the **proof of capacity**, not the rule.

---

## 3. INTERMEDIATE / NEUROTIC DEFENSES (Vaillant Level III)

### 3.1 Reaction Formation (the master Stratum-III defense)

The entire Alias-era persona is, structurally, a reaction-formation against the Jewel self. The Jewel-self was: hopeful, brightly costumed, eager to be liked, openly powered, mainstream-aspirational, sexually inexperienced, trusting. The Alias-self is, point-for-point: cynical, drab-clothed (jeans, henley, leather), abrasive, powers-suppressed in public, anti-mainstream, sexually used-and-cynical, mistrustful. The inversion is **too clean to be organic**; it is a constructed photo-negative. Important corollary: she experiences this constructed self as her true self, which is what makes it durable and what makes any return to Jewel-coded behavior (e.g., putting on a costume) physically aversive.

### 3.2 Intellectualization

Investigative reasoning serves a defensive function alongside its instrumental one. Building a case file is a way to be near terrible things without being **in** them. She is most psychologically stable when she has a corkboard, photos, and a working theory; she is least stable when there is nothing to investigate and only her own interior to occupy.

### 3.3 Isolation of Affect

She can recount the Killgrave captivity in flat clinical paragraphs (the *Alias* #28 monologue is the textbook instance) — every fact intact, affect bracketed off. This is not denial; it is **isolation**. The affect exists, lives elsewhere in the system, and emerges later, displaced, often as rage at a proximate target.

### 3.4 Displacement

The displacement axis is well-mapped: Killgrave-rage onto the next available abuser (the small-town Cap-impersonator case, the Purple Man re-emergence, multiple stalker husbands across the *Alias* casework). Avenger-abandonment-rage onto Carol Danvers in low-grade form for years. Self-rage onto Cage during the worst stretches of pregnancy and the 2016 arc.

### 3.5 Rationalization

Used sparingly and not very well — she has too much self-awareness for it to seal. The recurring one is the **"I'm just no good for them"** rationalization, deployed to justify withdrawal from Cage, from Carol, from would-be normal life. She half-believes it; the half that doesn't is the leverage point for any intervention.

### 3.6 Undoing

Subtle but present. After cruelty she does small material kindnesses — buys the coffee, fixes the door she kicked in, leaves cash where she shouldn't. Rarely accompanied by verbal apology, which would require contact with the underlying affect.

### 3.7 Phobic Avoidance (the Jewel-phobia and the Tower-phobia)

- The Jewel costume is **phobic encapsulation**: a physical object that, if approached, would re-open Stratum II. She will not look at it, joke about its existence rather than its appearance, refuses to put on anything in its color family.
- Avengers Tower (and, later, any "official" hero space) functions as agoraphobia-of-association — she will enter under necessity but does not relax, drinks more after visits, sleeps worse.
- **Stimulus generalization to the color purple** is real and partial — not full chromophobia, but visible flinch-response that she controls effortfully.

### 3.8 Identification with the Aggressor — partial and inverted

A nuanced case. She did not become Killgrave. She did, however, internalize his lesson about the power of will-violation and inverted it into a vigilant refusal to be controlled — and, in shadow form, into a tendency to control her own loved ones via withholding (decide for them what they get to know, what risk they are allowed to share). The inverted identification is most visible in the 2016 arc: she controls everyone in her life by lying to them "for their own good," which is structurally close to Killgrave's logic even though motivationally opposite.

---
