## 4. MATURE DEFENSES (Vaillant Level IV) — emergent, intermittent

She has access to all four classic mature defenses, but they are **achieved, not default**. The capacity is real; the deployment is partial.

### 4.1 Sublimation

The strongest of her mature defenses. Alias Investigations sublimates hypervigilance, rage, and the protect-the-weak drive into paid socially-useful labor. The hyperarousal that would otherwise be pathology becomes professional acuity. **Note:** the work also enables less-mature defenses (intellectualization, acting-out), so its mature status depends on context.

### 4.2 Altruism

Slow-emerging and load-bearing in the post-Killgrave self-repair. Operative form: **protecting the weaker party in the room**, often at her own cost, without expectation of recognition. Becomes structural with Danielle and with Malcolm (who functions across late canon as a quasi-sibling/ward whose continued sobriety she silently invests in).

### 4.3 Humor — true form, restricted distribution

Distinguishable from devaluation by target-dignity preservation. She has it. She uses it mostly with Cage in bed, with Danielle at home, and rarely with Malcolm in the office. Its scarcity is itself diagnostic.

### 4.4 Suppression (as opposed to repression)

She can, with effort, **consciously set aside** an affect to handle a tactical situation and return to it later — particularly when Danielle is the stakes. This is mature suppression, not repression, and is the cleanest evidence that her ego-strength is high despite the symptom load. A weaker ego with her trauma history would not function at her professional level.

### 4.5 Anticipation

Weak. She is good at threat-anticipation in cases, poor at emotional-anticipation in her own life — she does not generally pre-plan how she will manage a hard conversation, a custody question, an anniversary of the captivity. Surprise-by-affect is a recurrent vulnerability.

---

## 5. POSITIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

Distinct from defenses: these are structures she has **built** that hold her up rather than fend off threat.

### 5.1 Work as identity scaffold

The PI practice is the spine of her adult self. Not merely income — it organizes her week, gives her a socially legible role, lets her feel competent every day, and provides a regulated stream of small wins. Lose the practice and the structure sags within days (visible in any arc that puts her on the bench).

### 5.2 Chosen family, narrow-channel

Cage (primary), Danielle (organizing), Malcolm (daily), Carol (intermittent and reparative), Matt Murdock (peer-grade, professionally bounded). She does not scale wide; she scales deep within a tight circle. This is **adaptive given her threat history** — a small, vetted circle is a defensible perimeter.

### 5.3 Refusal of grandiosity

Where another survivor with her power-set might have compensated with messianic heroics, she compensated downward. The refusal to be a "real" hero is, paradoxically, a positive ego-function: it accurately calibrates her capacities and protects against the inflation that would set her up for further fall. She does not need to be admired, which is one of the cleanest indicators of a non-narcissistic structure under severe shame load.

### 5.4 Reparative parenting

Mothering Danielle is doing for another what was not done for her: present-tense attention, narration of the world, physical safety, predictable return. Each successful parenting day is, in the structural sense, a small treatment session.

### 5.5 The moral floor

Across two decades and worst-case provocations she has not crossed certain lines: she does not kill where killing is unnecessary, does not take cases she finds repugnant beyond cash pressure, does not betray clients' confidences. This floor is **the artifact of selfhood Killgrave failed to dissolve**, and she stands on it. It functions defensively (she cannot be fully shamed while it holds) and compensatorily (it is the basis of her self-respect).

### 5.6 Tolerance of her own ugliness

A subtle and powerful asset. She does not require herself to be pretty, polite, or palatable. This makes her **structurally hard to manipulate by ordinary social levers** — flattery slides off, shame-attacks land on already-shamed ground that has been built on for years. An interrogator working her will find few of the usual handles.

---

## 6. NEGATIVE COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS

The shadow side — structures that hold her up in the short run and cost her in the long run.

### 6.1 Alcohol as primary regulator

Not merely a symptom of AUD — functionally a **prosthetic emotion-regulation system**. It downshifts hyperarousal, enables sleep, blunts intrusion, anesthetizes shame, and provides the social cover of "the drunk PI" that lets her decline intimacy without explanation. Removing it without replacement would expose every affect it has been managing for fifteen-plus subjective years; this is the central treatment problem.

### 6.2 Sexual self-punishment (Alias-era, recurrent)

Encounters chosen for their unworthiness, so that the disappointing aftermath confirms an existing self-view rather than threatening it. Functions as **controlled re-enactment**: she chooses the violation now in miniature, on her terms, to avoid being chosen by it again.

### 6.3 Preemptive rejection of help

The "leave before you are left" architecture, scaled up to "refuse before you are refused." Cost: she has repeatedly cut off resources (Carol, the Avengers' material support, formal therapy, even Cage's earnest offers) at exactly the moments she most needed them. Benefit: she has never had help weaponized against her — a calculus that made sense post-Killgrave and over-generalized.

### 6.4 Identity-via-contempt

Defining herself by what she scorns rather than what she is for. Cheap, durable, and corrosive. It builds a self quickly but a brittle one — anything that destabilizes the scorned objects (e.g., capes turning out to be decent, the Bugle doing real journalism, Jewel-her not being contemptible) destabilizes her.

### 6.5 Workaholic immersion

Cases as affect-avoidance. She will take an extra case the week of an anniversary, work through Cage's attempts to talk, sleep at the office. Productive on the surface, costly underneath — the unprocessed material accrues and discharges through 6.1 (alcohol) or through acting-out.

### 6.6 Smoking (early period)

Now intermittent / largely retired post-pregnancy, but in early *Alias* served as a micro-regulator — a paced breath, a manageable hand-task, a five-minute legitimate withdrawal from any room. Functionally similar to the drinking but with finer-grained dose control. Its decline is a small marker of improved regulation.

### 6.7 The leather jacket

Worth naming as the **portable fortification**. The jacket is armor, costume, identity-marker, sensory-comfort object, and a literal physical layer between her skin and the world. Its consistency across two decades of canon is not stylistic accident; it is the most reliable item in her self-soothing kit. Removal in canon correlates with safety (bed, bath, Danielle in arms); presence correlates with operational mode.

### 6.8 The office as den

The Alias office — dingy, badly lit, smelling of takeout and bourbon — functions as a **regulated environment** she controls absolutely. Sleeping on the couch rather than going home is, at bad stretches, a way of staying inside the controlled perimeter. Negative compensation because it substitutes for the harder work of making the apartment / shared home safe-feeling.

---

## 7. DEFENSIVE DECAY CURVE UNDER STRESS

A reliable sequence, useful for forecasting:

1. **Baseline:** sardonic humor (devaluation-form), sublimated investigation, controlled drinking, intermittent mature defenses available.
2. **+1 (irritation level):** humor sharpens toward cruelty, drinking ticks up one drink, passive-aggression toward Malcolm/Cage in micro-doses, sleep slips.
3. **+2 (case stress or relational friction):** intellectualization thickens, isolation of affect engages, displacement onto safe targets, sex declines or turns mechanical.
4. **+3 (Killgrave-coded or Danielle-threat stimulus):** reaction-formation cracks — she may surprise herself by crying, by sincerity, by reaching out — then immediately overcorrect with acting-out and withdrawal. Dissociation visible. Drinking spikes.
5. **+4 (crisis, e.g., Skrull-Jarvis abduction, 2016 conspiracy):** primitive tier dominant — dissociation, splitting of self-states (the "I have to do this alone" voice), acting-out at maximum scale (undercover, jail, severed ties). Mature defenses offline. **Curiously, ego-strength here is highest in instrumental domain and lowest in relational** — she will function tactically and burn every bridge simultaneously.
6. **Post-crisis:** shame spiral, drinking spike, withdrawal, slow rebuild via work and Danielle. Carol or Cage typically required as external scaffold to complete the rebuild; she will not ask, and they have learned to arrive unasked.

---

## 8. SUMMARY ASSESSMENT

The defensive architecture is **unusually well-integrated for the trauma load**. Primitive defenses are present and active but contained — they do not colonize her object-relations or her moral structure. Neurotic defenses are richly developed and bear most of the daily load, with reaction-formation as the master organizer of the public self. Mature defenses exist as real capacities, deployed unevenly, and trending — across two decades of canon — toward greater availability, particularly through the parenting channel.

The positive compensations (work, chosen family, moral floor, refusal of grandiosity, tolerance of ugliness) constitute a **genuine repair structure**, not a façade. The negative compensations (alcohol foremost, sexual self-punishment, preemptive rejection, contempt-identity, workaholism) are the **cost of doing business** with a defensive system that was built under siege and has not yet been allowed to demobilize.

The single most important operational fact in this section: **alcohol is not her problem; it is her solution to her problem, and the problem is C-PTSD with no other adequate regulator in place.** Any intervention that removes 6.1 without first installing alternative regulation will collapse the structure into the primitive tier. Any intervention that strengthens the positive compensations — particularly chosen family, sublimated work, and reparative parenting — incrementally lowers the load on the negative ones without confrontation, which is the only modality her structure tolerates.

*End section. Cross-reference: Section on Stress Response & Escalation Curve; Section on Substance Use Longitudinal; Section on Chosen-Family Network.*


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE
## Subject: Jessica Campbell Jones — Decade-by-Decade Clinical Evolution

*Frameworks employed: attachment theory (Bowlby/Main/Hesse, with Fonagy mentalization overlay); Vaillant defense hierarchy; Linehan biosocial affect-regulation model; Janoff-Bulman shattered-assumptions theory; Herman's three-stage trauma recovery model; Beck cognitive schema theory; Young schema therapy (Early Maladaptive Schemas); Porges polyvagal model for autonomic baseline; Bromberg/Putnam dissociation framework. Diagnoses cross-referenced to DSM-5 and ICD-11.*

---

## I. PRE-TRAUMA BASELINE — Adolescence, ~13–15

**Affect regulation.** Within normative adolescent range but skewed irritable-dysphoric. Flashback evidence (the Forest Hills bus-stop sequences, the Parker fixation) shows a girl whose default emotional gear is *envious resentment* — Beck would code the dominant automatic thoughts as comparative ("everyone else has it easier / is luckier / is more interesting"). She is not depressed in any clinical sense; she is sulky in a way that suggests a temperamental low set-point for positive affect (the "dysthymic temperament" of Akiskal's classification — irritable subtype). This is a non-trivial pre-morbid finding: she did not start from a wide affective bandwidth, and the trauma that follows acts on a system that was already narrow on the upside.

**Cognitive style.** Sharp, verbal, sarcastic-precocious. Already shows the trait that will become her professional instrument: she watches people and reads motive faster than she should be able to. The downside trait — she watches *herself* the same way, and the verdict is harsh — is also present. Self-talk audible in her flashback voiceover is already adversarial.

**Self-concept.** Ordinary-adolescent unstable, with a preexisting *Defectiveness/Shame* schema (Young) in subclinical form: the conviction of being uninteresting, unchosen, looked-past. Mostly latent; nothing in her life yet has loaded it.

**Attachment.** Secure-leaning. Intact nuclear family, ordinary sibling rivalry with Phillip, no abuse history. The internal working model is "people stay; people are basically reliable." This will matter enormously — secure substrate is why she will later, after catastrophic disconfirmation, still be *capable* of attachment at all.

---

## II. THE RUPTURE AND THE LOST YEARS — Roughly 15–19

**The accident as Janoff-Bulman event.** The three core assumptions of the just-world schema — *the world is benevolent, the world is meaningful, the self is worthy* — are shattered simultaneously and in a single instant. Family annihilation by random military negligence does not permit any of the cognitive repair operations a less arbitrary trauma allows (no perpetrator to hate, no choice to second-guess). The result is a structural cognitive vacancy where causal attribution should sit. She fills it, as children do, with self-blame in displaced form: she resents the *Joneses* for being alive, which is a metabolizable form of resenting *herself* for surviving.

**Affect regulation post-coma.** First documented dissociative episode (the coma itself functions as enforced somatic absence). On waking she presents with what would now be flagged as a prolonged grief/adjustment disorder layered on emerging PTSD from the accident proper. She does not speak about her powers — the concealment is the first evidence of the *encapsulation* strategy that will define her: walling off the unbearable in a sealed compartment and refusing to let it interact with the rest of identity. Bromberg's "not-me" self-state architecture begins here.

**Self-concept** consolidates around survivor-guilt and adoptive-displacement: *I am not who I was; I do not belong to the people I'm with; my existence is an accident the universe didn't intend.* The pre-existing Defectiveness schema now has experiential confirmation.

**Attachment** shifts from secure to *insecure-preoccupied with avoidant overlay*: she still wants the lost attachment objects, but the available ones (the Joneses) are refused on principle, because accepting them would constitute a betrayal of the dead. This is the first appearance of the lifelong pattern: *love offered is read as a demand to forget*.

---

## III. THE JEWEL PERIOD — Late teens to early twenties

**Affect regulation: temporary upregulation via role.** The costumed identity functions as a Winnicottian false-self construction in its benign form — a borrowed template (the cheerful, primary-color hero) that gives her access to affect bands her real self cannot reach. Flashback evidence shows her actually *enjoying* things during Jewel — flying, banter, being thanked. This is the only documented period of sustained positive affect in the entire record.

**Cognitive style.** Naïve-hopeful, in a way she will later find unbearable to remember. The verbal sharpness is still there but pointed outward as quip rather than inward as judgment.

**Self-concept.** A precarious experiment: *maybe I am the kind of person who gets to do this.* Held together by external reinforcement (rescues, gratitude) rather than internal restructuring. The underlying Defectiveness schema is not dissolved; it is *covered*. This matters because schemas that are covered rather than processed remain fully loaded and will discharge catastrophically when the cover is removed.

**Attachment.** Tentative re-extension toward peers in the cape community — never deep, mostly admiring-from-distance. The Carol Danvers friendship begins here and is, in retrospect, the only pre-Killgrave attachment that will survive the wound at all, because it was the most reciprocal and the least dependent on the Jewel persona.

---

## IV. CAPTIVITY — Approximately eight months at age ~21

**This is the decade-defining inflection.** Every framework converges on the same reading: prolonged interpersonal trauma by a perpetrator with totalizing control over the victim's will produces a phenomenology distinct from single-incident PTSD. Herman's *Trauma and Recovery* (1992) describes the captivity syndrome with uncanny precision for what Bendis depicts: the perpetrator's destruction of the victim's autonomous mental life, the coerced participation in transgressions that become the victim's later shame anchor, the manufacture of pseudo-consent as the deepest violation.

**Affect regulation during captivity.** Not applicable in the ordinary sense — affect is hijacked. The relevant clinical fact is that for eight months her interoceptive signals were systematically uncoupled from action: she felt fear and approached; she felt revulsion and smiled; she felt rage and obeyed. The neurobiological consequence (per van der Kolk) is a learned dissociation between somatic signal and behavioral response — the body becomes an unreliable narrator. This permanently alters her relationship to her own embodiment.

**Cognitive style during captivity.** Constricted to immediate compliance-calculation. The pattern-matching intelligence is preserved but oriented entirely to threat-anticipation of one specific other. This narrow-band hypervigilance, once established, does not switch off; it later becomes her PI instrument.

**Self-concept formed in captivity.** The catastrophic schema is installed: *I am the thing that wanted it / I am the thing that did those things / my will is not mine and never was.* This is the *Defectiveness/Shame* schema fused with a *Subjugation* schema (Young) and an *Enmeshment/Undeveloped Self* schema (the boundary between her wants and his commands has been destroyed). Recovery work would, decades later, still be addressing this composite.

---

## V. THE WAKE-UP AND THE ABANDONMENT — Age ~22

A clinically distinct event from the captivity itself, and arguably as damaging.

She wakes from the coma to discover that **no one came**. The Avengers — the framework she had organized her Jewel-self around — did not differentiate her from her perpetrator. They beat her nearly to death and then did not visit. Carol's later partial presence does not undo this.

This is a *secondary betrayal* in the Freyd/DePrince sense: institutional betrayal compounding interpersonal trauma. Its specific cognitive payload is the conviction that *being misunderstood is a permanent condition and explanation is futile*. This belief will, twenty years later, drive the entire 2016 *Jessica Jones* arc — she will choose jail and the loss of her marriage over the act of asking for help, because at the somatic level she does not believe asking works.

---

## VI. THE KNIGHTRESS INTERREGNUM AND EARLY ALIAS PERIOD — Mid-twenties to ~28

**Affect regulation: collapse into substance-mediated suppression.** The dominant strategy becomes alcohol-as-anxiolytic with secondary use as soporific. Linehan's biosocial model fits cleanly: invalidating environment (the Avengers' non-response) acting on a person with high baseline emotional sensitivity (the dysthymic temperament) under sustained dysregulating load (untreated PTSD) → predictable migration toward whichever down-regulator is available without prescription. Alcohol does the work that no SSRI, no prazosin, no DBT skills group is ever offered to her.

Secondary strategies: sexual encounters that function as *controlled re-exposure* — she chooses partners and frames that let her enact agency over her own body without the vulnerability of mutuality. The Cage one-night stand in *Alias* #1 is paradigmatic: she initiates, she leaves, she does not return calls. The act is regulatory, not relational.

**Cognitive style.** The hypervigilance from captivity is now redirected onto the case-work. Pattern recognition is excellent; meta-cognition about herself is severely impaired. Beck's cognitive triad — negative view of self, world, future — is fully present, but she would experience any therapist's attempt to name it as condescension. The defensive style here is *premature closure*: she reaches conclusions about other people's contempt for her faster than they can form any opinion, and then behaves as if her prediction were observed fact (confirmation-bias loop).

**Self-concept.** Stable in its negativity, which is itself a perverse adaptation — a coherent bad self is psychologically more tolerable than an incoherent one. She has organized her shame into an identity (the hard-drinking PI who scorns capes) that she can perform competently. The aesthetic — jeans, leather jacket, scotch, profanity — is not a costume; it is a *psychic exoskeleton*, load-bearing.

**Attachment.** Fully *fearful-avoidant (disorganized)*. The wanting and the dreading are both active and approximately equal in amplitude, which produces the characteristic approach-withdraw oscillation visible in every relationship from this period. Mentalization (Fonagy) is selectively impaired: she reads strangers and adversaries with high accuracy and reads intimates with high distortion, because intimates activate the attachment system and the attachment system, for her, is a damaged instrument.

**Vaillant defenses, this period.** Predominantly Level 2 (immature): acting-out (drinking, sex), passive aggression (with Jameson, with clients), projection (assuming contempt), devaluation (of capes, of her younger self). Intermittent Level 3 (neurotic): displacement (snapping at Malcolm in lieu of feeling fear about a case), intellectualization (the case-analytic mode used to outrun affect). Glimpses of Level 4 (mature): sublimation, in that the PI work *does* serve others; not yet humor in the mature sense — her humor is still mostly devaluation in stand-up clothing.

---

## VII. RE-ENTRY: PURPLE MAN CONFRONTATION AND CAGE RELATIONSHIP — Late twenties

**The Killgrave re-confrontation (*Alias* #24–28) as in-vivo exposure.** What Bendis depicts is structurally identical to what a trauma clinician would attempt in stage-two Herman work: controlled re-contact with the perpetrator under conditions where the survivor retains agency. Her victory is *affective*, not physical: she wins by refusing to let his voice produce the conditioned response. This is the first evidence in the record of top-down regulatory control reasserting itself over a previously automatic trauma circuit. Polyvagally, this is the moment ventral-vagal social-engagement comes back online in the presence of the dorsal-vagal-collapse trigger. It does not heal her, but it proves to her that healing is mechanically possible — a different and indispensable piece of self-knowledge.

**The Cage relationship as corrective emotional experience.** Cage is, clinically, the ideal partner for someone with her attachment profile: high distress tolerance, non-reactive to her testing behaviors, slow to take offense, physically unfrightenable (which is non-trivial — she cannot accidentally hurt him), and possessed of his own stable identity that does not require her validation. He does not chase when she withdraws and does not punish when she returns. Over time this constitutes what Bowlby would call an *earned secure* attachment — not the same as primary secure, but functionally adequate.

**Affect regulation shift.** Alcohol use diminishes (it does not vanish). Sleep improves. The rage-suppression-blackout cycle is partially replaced by *expressed irritation tolerated by a stable other*, which is the developmental scaffold she missed in her twenties. She is, in essence, getting in her late twenties what should have happened in her early ones.

---

## VIII. PREGNANCY, MOTHERHOOD, AVENGERS-ADJACENCY — ~29–33

**The pregnancy as forced ontological revision.** A body she has experienced as either weapon, trauma-vessel, or numb instrument is now also a generative one. The clinical literature on pregnancy in survivors of sexual trauma (Seng et al.) predicts exactly what is depicted: heightened somatic awareness, intrusive fears, hypervigilance about fetal damage, a mixed grief-joy affect that survivors find disorienting. She handles it largely by *not talking about it*, which is consistent with her lifelong encapsulation strategy.

**Motherhood as reorganizing schema.** This is the most important structural change in the entire longitudinal record. Danielle's existence forces the activation of a *protective-caregiver* identity that, by its nature, cannot be organized around shame. You cannot mother from contempt for yourself without transmitting it; Jessica seems to know this at a level deeper than verbal, and the result is the first sustained *positive self-referential affect* she has demonstrated since the Jewel period — but this time it is structural, not borrowed. The Squirrel Girl nanny choice is diagnostic: she is now capable of *prioritizing outcome over self-image* (the choice looks absurd, which her old self would have refused on aesthetic grounds; her new self does not care how it looks if it works). This is one of the cleanest markers of maturation in the file.

**Affect regulation in this period.** Substantially improved baseline, with sharp acute episodes around perceived threat to Danielle (the Skrull-Jarvis incident is the cardinal example: the affective response is overwhelming, but it is also *appropriate*, and crucially she does not drink it away — she dissociates briefly, hands the baby off, then re-engages tactically). This is regulation by *task assumption* rather than suppression — a real upgrade.

**Cognitive style.** The catastrophizing about her own impact on others remains, now redirected onto Danielle (every mother-of-an-infant has this; in her case it is amplified by realistic threat). The personalization distortion is also reorganized: she now blames herself less for the *past* and more for *future* harms she has not yet caused. Lateral move, not net improvement, but the orientation toward the future is itself new — for years she could not think forward at all.

**Defenses.** First substantial Level 4 emergence. *Sublimation* is now load-bearing (Avengers work, Pulse journalism, PI work all routed through a coherent value structure rather than performed as flight from self). *Altruism* in Vaillant's sense — receiving gratification by giving — finally available, primarily through mothering. *Humor* migrates from devaluation toward genuine mature humor in the Cage relationship (their banter is observably warmer than her solo voiceover).

---

## IX. CIVIL WAR, SIEGE, DARK PERIOD — Early-to-mid thirties

**Stress-induced partial regression.** The political fracturing of the hero community reactivates the institutional-betrayal schema (*you are unprotected; explanation does not work; people you trusted will register you, hunt you, fail you*). Her response — flee to Canada to protect Danielle — is regulated and tactical, not panicked, which itself is evidence of how far she has come. But the underlying affect (terror, contempt for institutional capes, refusal to perform allegiance) is the *Alias*-period affect, intact under the skin.

**Cognitive style.** Operationally sharp; existentially exhausted. The chronic-PTSD weariness that Herman describes — the accumulated metabolic cost of decades of hypervigilance — begins to show as a slower, heavier affect. Not depression in the MDD sense; more like the *demoralization* construct (Frank/de Figueiredo).

---

## X. THE 2016 ARC AS DIAGNOSTIC CRISIS — Mid-thirties

**The fake separation from Cage is the file's clearest single moment of psychopathology.** Reading it through the lens of the original wound: she replicates, by her own choice, the exact configuration of the post-Killgrave hospital — alone, suspected of villainy by those she loves, unable to explain. The compulsion-to-repeat (Freud's clunky but here-accurate concept) is operative. She has the option to bring Cage in; she does not. The cognitive justification offered — that disclosure would compromise the op — is partially true and entirely insufficient to explain the affective preference for going alone. The preference itself is the symptom.

**Affect regulation under this load.** Substantial regression. Drinking spikes. Sleep collapses. The protective-caregiver identity that has been holding the system together becomes the rationalization for the regression (*I'm doing it for Danielle*), which is a more sophisticated version of the old shame logic (*I am the contaminated one who must bear this alone*).

**Self-concept under this load.** The *I am fundamentally untrustable to others / unhelpable by others* schema reasserts dominance. Note the structure: not "I am bad" in the simple shame sense, but "I am the kind of person who must do the unspeakable alone because no one else can be asked to share it." This is shame reorganized as a kind of *grim nobility*, which is more durable and more dangerous than ordinary shame because it feels virtuous.

**Recovery from the arc.** Slow, partial, and dependent on Cage's willingness to forgive — which is itself a piece of unearned grace she does not know how to metabolize. The Praise/Sincerity vulnerability (she cannot tolerate being thanked or forgiven without poisoning the moment) is acute here.

---

## XI. LATE-PERIOD INTEGRATION — Mid-to-late thirties onward

**Affect regulation.** Stabilized at a higher functional baseline than at any point since adolescence, but with permanently narrowed dynamic range. Joy is accessible only through Danielle and through small Cage-moments; the broad-spectrum positive affect of the Jewel period is gone and is not coming back. This is the realistic post-CPTSD endpoint: not restoration, *attenuated function with reliable lower amplitude on both ends*. The trade-off — losing the highs to gain control over the lows — is one most chronic-trauma survivors would accept.

**Cognitive style.** Mature integrated. The investigator's pattern-matching is now applied to herself with less distortion than before (intermittent meta-cognition is finally online). She can name her own avoidance in real time, sometimes, which is a capacity she did not have at thirty. The catastrophizing persists but is more often recognized as catastrophizing.

**Self-concept.** The composite schema (Defectiveness + Subjugation + Mistrust) is not extinguished — schemas of this depth never are — but it is *decentered*. She no longer experiences it as the truth about her; she experiences it as a familiar voice she has learned to argue with. This is the realistic Stage-3 Herman outcome: reconnection without restoration, identity reconstructed *with* the wound rather than around it or against it.

**Attachment.** Earned-secure within a narrow channel (Cage, Danielle, Malcolm, an uneasy détente with Carol); fearful-avoidant in every wider channel. She has accepted this asymmetry rather than fighting it, which is itself a maturational marker — younger Jessica would have read the asymmetry as further evidence of contamination; current Jessica reads it as *resource allocation*.

**Defenses.** Stable mix of Level 3 and Level 4. Sublimation, altruism, mature humor, anticipation (she now plans for her own predictable reactions). Level 2 returns under acute load (the 2016 arc proved this), and will probably always return — the immature defenses are the deepest grooves and the first ones water flows down under pressure.

---

## XII. SUMMARY VECTOR

Across the twenty-plus-year longitudinal record, the trajectory is **not a recovery curve but a containment curve**. The underlying injury — captivity-induced disorganization of will, embodiment, and trust — is not healed and, given the absence of any depicted formal treatment, was never going to be. What is achieved instead, slowly and against the grain of her own defensive structure, is:

1. A reliable external scaffold (Cage, Danielle, work) that holds the system upright when internal regulation fails;
2. A narrowed-but-functional affective range, traded against the loss of pre-trauma highs;
3. A self-concept that has migrated from *I am the contaminated thing* to *I am the person who carries this and still shows up*, which is a different, livable identity;
4. Sufficient meta-cognition to recognize, intermittently, her own patterns in flight, which prevents the worst regressions from going fully unchecked;
5. A protective-caregiver identity (chiefly mothering) that does load-bearing work the shame-organized identity cannot.

She is, at the current observation point, a chronically injured person operating at a competent baseline through compensatory scaffolding. The injury is permanent; the function is real; the gap between the two is bridged by Cage, by Danielle, by Malcolm, by work, and by a moral spine that has, against considerable odds, refused to break.

*— End Longitudinal Profile. Continues in Section: Behavioral Signature & Somatic Telemetry.*


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: JONES, Jessica Campbell

*Assessment compiled longitudinally from observable behavior, verbal self-report (notoriously unreliable in this subject, biased toward self-minimization and deflection through profanity), collateral from associates (Cage, L.; Walker, P.; Danvers, C.; Murdock, M.; Ducasse, M.), and reconstructed event-history. No formal mental-status examination has ever been conducted; subject has refused all referrals to mental-health professionals on at least four documented occasions and uncounted informal ones. The following is a forensic-clinical reconstruction.*

---

## 1. PRESENTING PICTURE (Cross-Sectional)

If one were to encounter the subject cold — in her office at 485 W. 46th, mid-afternoon, mid-case — the cross-sectional mental status would read approximately as follows.

**Appearance and behavior.** Female, mid-30s, presents older than stated age by perhaps five years; weather and sleep account for most of this. Grooming functional-minimal: hair washed but uncombed, no cosmetics, dark denim and a leather jacket worn past the point most owners would replace it. Posture: shoulders forward, weight on the back foot in any conversation, hands frequently occupied (glass, cigarette in earlier years, phone now). Eye contact: present but episodic — she looks away during the emotional content of a sentence and back during the structural content, which is the opposite of the neurotypical pattern and consistent with shame-organized affect avoidance.

**Speech.** Rate normal-to-rapid, volume moderate, prosody flat-to-sardonic with sharp uptick on punchlines. Vocabulary high; profanity dense and used grammatically rather than emotionally (i.e., she swears even when calm — it is a register, not a discharge). Latency to respond is short for factual questions, long for affective ones, and effectively infinite for questions about herself.

**Mood and affect.** Self-reported mood typically "fine" or a refusal to engage the question. Observed affect: constricted range with two prominent peaks — dry contempt and protective ferocity. Sadness, tenderness, and fear are present but routed almost exclusively through irritation. Affect is congruent with thought content when the content is external; incongruent (flattened or deflected) when the content turns inward.

**Thought process.** Linear, goal-directed, efficient. No formal thought disorder. Tangentiality only in service of evasion.

**Thought content.** No delusions. No active suicidal ideation, though passive ideation ("I shouldn't be here, I shouldn't have woken up") was documentable during the *Alias* period and is plausibly intermittent since. No homicidal ideation toward present persons; persistent, integrated, non-ego-dystonic readiness to kill Zebediah Killgrave under sufficient provocation, which is not a symptom but a posture.

**Perception.** No hallucinations. Intrusive imagery (Killgrave-coded — purple, the cadence of his voice, the specific apartment in which she was held) is implied across multiple titles, particularly under intoxication and on the edge of sleep. These are properly classified as PTSD intrusions, not perceptual disturbances.

**Cognition.** Grossly intact. Attention high when engaged, poor when bored. Memory: intact for case detail, patchy for personal/biographical detail in ways that suggest both alcoholic blackout and trauma-mediated avoidance — she has, on record, been unable to reconstruct the morning after the *Alias* #1 encounter with Cage despite the clinical importance of that morning to her.

**Insight.** Paradoxical. She has near-perfect intellectual insight into her own dynamics — she can name what she is doing while she is doing it — and near-zero behavioral application of that insight. This is a specific clinical picture: not denial, not poor insight, but **insight without leverage.** She watches herself drink and cannot make the watching matter.

**Judgment.** Excellent under acute external threat. Poor under chronic internal threat. She will make the right call for a client and the wrong call for herself in the same hour.

---

## 2. PRIMARY DIAGNOSIS

### Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11 6B41) / Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder, chronic, with dissociative features (DSM-5 309.81)

This is the diagnostic spine of the case. Every other psychiatric phenomenon in the file is either a feature of, a consequence of, or a maladaptive response to, this condition.

**Criterion A — Stressor.** Overwhelmingly met. Eight months of captivity by Killgrave constitute a Criterion A event of an unusually severe kind: prolonged, interpersonal, sexualized-without-being-sexual-in-the-narrow-sense, and structured specifically to destroy the subject's experience of her own will. The captivity is compounded by two collateral Criterion A events bracketing it: (i) the adolescent MVA that killed her family of origin, with associated months-long coma, and (ii) the near-fatal beating by Vision and Iron Man at the captivity's end, with second coma. The Killgrave event is the etiological core; the others are predisposing and aggravating.

The specific topology of the Killgrave trauma deserves clinical emphasis. He did not torture her in the conventional sense. He commandeered the apparatus of consent. He made her **want** the things being done to her and to others; he made her stand at the foot of his bed for hours waiting to be summoned; he made her watch. The traumatic injury is therefore not to the body but to the structure of agency itself — to the felt distinction between "what I want" and "what is being done to me." This is why purely body-oriented or exposure-oriented trauma frames undersell her presentation: her core symptom cluster is organized around **agency**, not safety.

**Criterion B — Intrusion.** Met. Nightmares are referenced obliquely throughout *Alias* (the office-couch sleeping pattern is, on close reading, a sleep-avoidance pattern, not a convenience). Intrusive imagery is triggered reliably by purple stimuli, by particular vocal cadences, by being told what to do in a particular register. The 2016 arc, in which she re-enters Purple-Children-adjacent territory voluntarily, can be read as a sustained controlled-exposure operation she is conducting on herself without supervision — which is, predictably, decompensating rather than therapeutic.

**Criterion C — Avoidance.** Met, pervasively. Avoidance of the "Jewel" costume, name, and persona is total and ritualized; she will tolerate the name being spoken only in specific intimate contexts and even then with a wince. Avoidance of Avengers Tower lasted years and resumed under stress. Avoidance of verbal disclosure of the trauma is near-absolute; the few times she narrates the captivity (notably to Cage, late in *Alias*) are watershed events depicted as such.

**Criterion D — Negative alterations in cognition and mood.** Met, in textbook configuration. Persistent and exaggerated negative beliefs about herself ("I am contaminated," "I do not belong with real heroes," "I am a fraud Jewel in a leather jacket"). Distorted blame of self for the Avengers' failure to recognize her as a victim — she has, demonstrably, organized over a decade of behavior around the proposition that being mistaken for a villain was somehow her fault. Persistent negative emotional state (shame, anger, fear, fused). Markedly diminished interest in activities not instrumental to work or to Danielle. Detachment from others, ritualized. Inability to experience positive emotions, intermittent — she can feel them, but she cannot **hold** them; observers will note her reflex to spoil pleasant moments before others can.

**Criterion E — Marked alterations in arousal and reactivity.** Met. Irritable behavior and angry outbursts: chronic, low-threshold. Reckless or self-destructive behavior: cardinal — the drinking, the unprotected sex, the solo case-running, the willingness to be jailed rather than ask for help. Hypervigilance: constant, masquerading as professional alertness. Exaggerated startle response: observable, especially when approached from behind or when touched without warning by anyone other than Cage or Danielle. Problems with concentration and sleep: yes and yes.

**Criterion F — Duration.** Over one month, by approximately two decades.

**Criterion G — Functional impairment.** Significant. She functions — she runs a business, raises a child, maintains a marriage — but the cost of that function is visible in the somatic, substance, and relational measures throughout the file.

**Criterion H — Not attributable to substance or medical condition.** Substance use is consequence, not cause; the symptom structure is fully present in periods of relative sobriety.

#### Why "Complex" / why dissociative subtype.

ICD-11 CPTSD adds, atop classical PTSD, three "disturbances in self-organization" domains, all of which are unambiguously present:

- **Affect dysregulation.** Demonstrated. Suppression-then-explosion is her dominant pattern; she has limited mid-range modulation. Alcohol is the prosthetic that holds the middle of her affective curve.
- **Negative self-concept.** Demonstrated, severely. The self-schema is shame-saturated and globally negative, with the specific Killgrave-derivative belief that her interior has been colonized and may not be trustworthy as her own.
- **Disturbances in relationships.** Demonstrated. Fearful-avoidant pattern, preemptive withdrawal, difficulty receiving care, narrow channels of tolerable intimacy.

DSM-5's "with dissociative symptoms" specifier is also defensible. Documentable depersonalization (the morning after the Cage encounter; recurrent "watching herself" descriptions when intoxicated; the dissociative quality of her sexual life in the *Alias* period). Derealization is harder to document directly but plausible during Killgrave-triggered episodes. She is not a primary dissociative-disorder presentation (no amnestic episodes for identity, no alters), but the dissociative coloration of her PTSD is genuine.

#### Course.

The illness has not remitted. It has been **renegotiated.** The course is best modeled as a stepped trajectory:

- **Acute phase (immediate post-Killgrave, pre-*Alias*).** Withdrawal from costumed identity; failed reinvention via Knightress; onset of heavy drinking; isolation.
- **Chronic-active phase (*Alias* period).** Symptoms fully expressed and unmoderated. Alcohol Use Disorder at peak. Sexual self-punishment pattern at peak. Professional sublimation taking shape.
- **Partial integration phase (late *Alias* through *Pulse*).** The Killgrave re-confrontation produces a partial mastery experience. Pregnancy and partnership with Cage impose external scaffolding that reduces the most reckless behaviors without addressing the underlying disorder.
- **Functional-with-vulnerabilities phase (*New Avengers* onward).** She holds a life together. Symptoms surface under specific provocations: threats to Danielle, Killgrave-coded stimuli, situations that replicate the "mistaken for a villain" topology of the original wound.
- **Decompensation episodes (2016 arc and analogs).** Predictable structure: she encounters a stimulus that reactivates the captivity schema; she responds by replicating the captivity solution (isolation, loss of voice, suffering alone); she alienates her support; she emerges shaken and the cycle damps for a period.

Prognosis without intervention: stable-grim. She will not collapse, and she will not heal. With trauma-focused intervention (EMDR or trauma-focused CBT, plus structured AUD treatment, plus relational therapy with Cage), prognosis is meaningfully better than her self-narrative would predict; the intellectual insight and moral spine that have kept her functional are also excellent therapy assets. The barrier is not capacity. The barrier is that asking for help is, for her, structurally indistinguishable from being controlled.

---

## 3. COMORBID DIAGNOSIS

### Alcohol Use Disorder (DSM-5 303.90), moderate-to-severe in the *Alias* period; partial sustained remission with relapses thereafter.

DSM-5 criteria, with field evidence:

1. *Larger amounts / longer than intended:* yes; routine.
2. *Persistent desire / unsuccessful cut-down efforts:* implied; she announces intentions to drink less and does not.
3. *Great deal of time obtaining/using/recovering:* yes during *Alias*.
4. *Craving:* probable; difficult to document without self-report.
5. *Role failure:* yes — client interactions conducted drunk, missed appointments, the Bugle period strained by drinking.
6. *Continued use despite social/interpersonal problems:* yes; Cage objects, she continues.
7. *Activities given up:* hard to assess given the baseline isolation.
8. *Use in hazardous situations:* yes — investigations conducted drunk, flying drunk (a Class-50 strength operator drunk in public airspace is a substantial public-safety datum).
9. *Continued use despite knowledge of harm:* yes.
10. *Tolerance:* yes; she drinks volumes that would incapacitate baseline humans, partly due to physiology but the escalation pattern is present.
11. *Withdrawal:* not clearly documented; her physiology likely modulates the classical withdrawal syndrome, which is itself a clinical hazard (she gets fewer warning signs than a baseline drinker).

Six or more criteria in the *Alias* period — severe. Two-to-three criteria in the *New Avengers* / *Pulse* period — mild, in partial remission. Functional role: PTSD self-medication, classical and textbook. The AUD is **etiologically subordinate** to the PTSD — treat the PTSD without addressing the AUD and she will drink through the treatment; treat the AUD without addressing the PTSD and she will white-knuckle for a period and relapse on the first Killgrave-coded stressor.

### Nicotine Use Disorder, historical.

Heavy smoking documented across early *Alias*; tapered by pregnancy. Functions as a secondary regulator of arousal. Not currently clinically prominent.

### Insomnia Disorder, comorbid.

Persistent difficulty initiating and maintaining sleep, with daytime functional consequences, present for over three months and indeed for years. Technically codable as a comorbid sleep disorder rather than purely a PTSD symptom, given the chronicity and the partial decoupling from acute trauma cues. Treated by the subject with alcohol, which guarantees nonrestorative sleep architecture.

---

## 4. RULE-OUT / DIFFERENTIAL

The clinical importance of this section is high, because the subject's surface presentation invites several misreads that would, if accepted, distort both formulation and intervention.

### 4.1 Borderline Personality Disorder — RULED OUT.

The most seductive misdiagnosis. A clinician seeing only the cross-section — affective volatility, intense and stormy attachments, identity complaints, self-damaging behavior (substance, sex, recklessness), chronic shame — could be forgiven for reaching for BPD. The diagnosis is wrong, and the reasons it is wrong matter.

- *Frantic efforts to avoid abandonment:* **absent.** Her pattern is the inverse: she leaves first. BPD's signature panic at impending abandonment is replaced in her by a calm, almost relieved, preemption.
- *Pattern of unstable and intense interpersonal relationships with idealization/devaluation:* **absent.** Her relationships are remarkable for their **stability of ambivalence**. She holds Cage as both burden and rescue without splitting; she holds Carol Danvers as both betrayer and beloved across the 2016 arc with full integration; she even holds Killgrave with a stable, integrated hatred that does not oscillate. She does not split.
- *Identity disturbance:* **superficially present, structurally absent.** She complains about who she is. Her actual values, moral commitments, aesthetic, professional identity, and relational priorities have been **rock-stable for two decades.** A patient who reliably acts on the same values across years does not have identity diffusion; she has identity discomfort.
- *Impulsivity in two or more areas:* present but trauma-derivative.
- *Suicidal behavior / self-mutilation:* not documented in completed form. Passive ideation present. Reckless behavior present. Not the BPD signature.
- *Affective instability due to marked reactivity of mood:* present but **stimulus-bound** in a PTSD-coherent way, not the rapid, often unprovoked oscillation of BPD.
- *Chronic feelings of emptiness:* **absent.** She is full — of grief, of rage, of love for Danielle, of shame. Emptiness is precisely not her problem.
- *Inappropriate intense anger:* present, but congruent with the trauma history.
- *Transient stress-related paranoid ideation or dissociation:* dissociation yes, paranoid ideation no.

Five-of-nine threshold not met when properly parsed. More importantly, the **structural** features that distinguish BPD from C-PTSD — fear of abandonment, splitting, emptiness, identity diffusion — are the four she most clearly lacks. The diagnosis would be both wrong and clinically harmful: a BPD frame would pathologize her stable values as fragile and miss the captivity-derived agency injury that is her actual problem.

### 4.2 Antisocial Personality Disorder — RULED OUT.

The profanity, the contempt for institutions, the willingness to use force, the irritability, the substance use — none of this is ASPD. She has an unusually **rigid** moral floor (she will not kill non-combatants even when ordered by her own affect to do so); she demonstrates excessive rather than deficient guilt; she forms and sustains genuine attachments; she protects the vulnerable as a structural priority. ASPD is not in the differential except superficially.

### 4.3 Narcissistic Personality Disorder — RULED OUT.

Her self-preoccupation is real and is **negatively** valenced — a shame organization, not a grandiose one. She does not seek admiration; she actively repels it. She does not lack empathy; she has hyperacute empathy for victims and uses contempt as a screen against being moved by it. The "negative grandiosity" pattern (a private conviction of one's special badness) can mimic NPD structurally, but treatment implications and phenomenology diverge: she is a shame patient, not a narcissistic one.

### 4.4 Major Depressive Disorder, recurrent — DEFERRED / SUBSUMED.

A serious differential. She has years of low mood, anhedonia, hopelessness, low self-worth, sleep disturbance, and likely past suicidal ideation. A discrete MDE post-coma (either coma) is plausible and was probably never assessed. However, the **current** depressive picture is fully accounted for by PTSD Criterion D plus AUD-induced mood disturbance, and conservative diagnostic practice argues against double-coding when a single diagnosis accounts for the phenomena. If a structured interview during a relatively dry period demonstrated a discrete two-week episode meeting MDD criteria independently of trauma cues, the diagnosis should be added. Pending such, it is held in reserve.

### 4.5 Persistent Depressive Disorder (Dysthymia) — TEMPERAMENTAL CONTRIBUTOR.

Pre-trauma collateral (adolescent baseline: irritable, envious, dysphoric, self-comparing) suggests a dysthymic temperament predating the Killgrave event. This is not a formal diagnosis carried forward but a **vulnerability factor** that helps explain why her trauma course has been particularly shame-organized and depressive-tinted relative to other survivors of similar events. Etiologically, she did not arrive at the captivity with a serene baseline to be displaced from; the trauma fell on already-fertile depressive ground.

### 4.6 Substance-Induced Mood Disorder — CONTRIBUTORY, NOT PRIMARY.

Alcohol meaningfully worsens her affective picture and almost certainly accounts for the lower tail of her mood readings during heavy-use periods. Not a primary diagnosis; will resolve with the AUD.

### 4.7 Dissociative Disorders — RULED OUT in primary form.

No DID, no dissociative amnesia for identity, no dissociative fugue. The dissociative phenomena observed are PTSD-spectrum and are correctly captured by the dissociative-features specifier.

### 4.8 Acute Stress Disorder — N/A (chronicity).

Historical interest only; the diagnosis would have applied in the month immediately following the captivity and converted to PTSD thereafter.

### 4.9 Adjustment Disorder — N/A.

Disqualified by severity and chronicity.

### 4.10 Psychotic-spectrum disorders — RULED OUT.

No hallucinations, no delusions, no formal thought disorder, no negative-symptom picture, no disorganization. The intrusive imagery and the Killgrave-coded re-experiencing are ego-dystonic and recognized by the subject as memory phenomena, not perceptual realities.

### 4.11 Bipolar-spectrum disorders — RULED OUT.

No documented manic or hypomanic episodes. Her "high-energy" periods are hyperarousal, not elevated mood, and are accompanied by irritability and dysphoria rather than expansive affect, reduced need for sleep with sustained productivity, grandiosity, or pressured goal-directed pleasure-seeking.

### 4.12 ADHD — NOT INDICATED.

Sustained attention on cases over weeks; capacity for deep work; organized record-keeping (her case files are, by report, professional). Distractibility under boredom is normative.

### 4.13 Specific Phobia / Social Anxiety Disorder — SUBSUMED.

Phobic avoidance of "Jewel"-coded stimuli and of certain interpersonal exposures is properly understood as PTSD avoidance, not an independent phobic disorder.

### 4.14 Obsessive-Compulsive Disorder — RULED OUT.

No ego-dystonic obsessions, no ritualized compulsions in the OCD sense. The repetitive behaviors observable in her work (re-checking, surveillance routines) are occupationally appropriate and not distress-driven.

### 4.15 Postpartum Mood Disorders — CONSIDERED, NOT DIAGNOSED.

The postpartum period with Danielle showed hypervigilant new-parent anxiety atop existing PTSD. No clear postpartum depressive episode documented, though the diagnostic threshold may have been masked by baseline negative affect. Worth noting prospectively in any future reproductive context.

---

## 5. ETIOLOGICAL FORMULATION

A four-factor biopsychosocial-developmental synthesis:

**Biological / constitutional.** Probable dysthymic temperament from adolescence; female sex (relevant to PTSD prevalence and presentation); post-exposure superhuman physiology that complicates the somatics of substance use and the phenomenology of arousal (she cannot be physically overpowered easily, which paradoxically means her trauma response c


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: JESSICA CAMPBELL JONES

*A longitudinal catalog of observable tells, micro-behaviors, decision heuristics, and somatic patterns across the full state-space of the subject's life. Compiled from two decades of continuous documentation. Patterns are coded by condition; sub-patterns by era where they shift.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

True calm is rare and the file should be honest about that — what reads as "calm" in the subject is more accurately *low-grade ambient vigilance with the volume turned down*. There is no observed condition in which she is fully unguarded except in proximity to the sleeping child Danielle, and even then only intermittently.

**Postural baseline.** Slouched but loaded — a posture our analysts have flagged as the "ready-slump." Shoulders rolled slightly forward, weight back on the heels or on one hip, hands often in jacket pockets or wrapped around a glass or mug. The slouch is performative-defensive (it advertises that she is not trying) but the lower body is always positioned to move: feet shoulder-width or wider, never crossed when standing, knees soft. She does not sit with her back to a door. She does not sit in the middle of a couch when alone with someone — always an end. In her own office she sits with the desk between herself and the visitor and with the door in peripheral vision.

**Eye behavior.** Direct gaze when speaking, particularly when delivering an insult or a refusal — eye contact is one of her aggressions. When listening, gaze drifts and returns. She tracks hands more than faces in unfamiliar company. In rooms with multiple people she does a discreet sweep on entry — door, exits, threats, weapons-of-opportunity — completed in under three seconds and visible only as a brief head-tilt.

**Verbal baseline.** Low-volume, low-affect, fast cadence with long pauses dropped in at moments of incoming information. The voice rises in volume only in anger or to a child. Heavy use of profanity as connective tissue rather than emphasis — "fuck" functions as a comma. Sentence fragments. She finishes other people's sentences when bored and lets her own trail off when she has nothing further to spend on the topic. Sardonic register is the default; sincere statements are flagged for the listener by an audible *gear shift* — a half-beat pause, a slight drop in pitch, an averted glance.

**Hands.** Restless when un-occupied. The drinking-hand and the smoking-hand (early *Alias* period) gave them something to do; in the post-Cage, post-Danielle era she has substituted coffee mugs, pens she clicks, the strap of a bag, the hem of a jacket. She does not gesture broadly when speaking; her hands stay close to her body.

**Hygiene and self-presentation at baseline.** Functional, not curated. Hair washed when she remembers, otherwise tied back. Same five articles of clothing in heavy rotation across years — leather jacket, jeans, t-shirts and henleys (gray, black, occasionally a faded color), boots. No jewelry except, in late period, a wedding band she wears inconsistently. No makeup. Nails kept short and unpainted — practical, not feminine-coded. The lack of effort is itself the statement: *I will not be looked at on those terms.*

**Domestic micro-rituals at baseline.**
- Coffee before speech in the morning. Black. She will not have a real conversation until the first cup is down.
- Phone charged on the floor by the bed, not the nightstand — a habit that predates Danielle and persists.
- Mail opened in batches, often weeks late. Bills paid at the last possible moment, not from disorganization but from a learned distrust of routine.
- The office answering machine left to fill up; she screens.
- Locks checked twice on leaving. Not OCD-checking — once visually, once by hand on the knob.

---

## II. WORK STATE / OPERATIONAL MODE

**Case intake.** She lets the client talk for longer than necessary before interrupting. The interruptions, when they come, are diagnostic — she is testing whether the client will tolerate being cut off, which tells her how much they are lying. She asks for money up front and is graceless about it; the gracelessness is intentional, a filter against clients who want to be friends. She writes nothing down in front of the client; she writes everything down the moment they leave.

**Surveillance behavior.** Patient. She can sit in one position for six to eight hours without obvious restlessness — a capacity the file attributes to her two extended comas and her Killgrave captivity, both of which trained the body to wait. She does not use her flight to surveil; she walks, takes the subway, uses fire escapes and rooftops only as needed. Photographs from middle distance with a cheap camera, never close enough to require explanation. She does not befriend her marks' neighbors or doormen; she observes them instead.

**Interview technique.** Two modes. *Mode A (hostile witness):* sustained eye contact, profanity, invasion of personal space, deliberate provocation — used when she is sure the subject is lying and wants the lie to escalate into a tell. *Mode B (frightened witness):* she becomes physically smaller, lowers her voice, sits at an angle rather than face-to-face, lets silences run, offers cigarettes or coffee. The transition between modes within a single interview is fast and is one of her genuine professional skills.

**Decision heuristics on cases.**
- *If a child is involved, the rate goes down and the hours go up.* Universal. Never spoken aloud.
- *If a cape is involved, take the case and complain about it.* The complaining is honest; the taking is the tell.
- *If the case smells like Killgrave or Killgrave-adjacent (mind control, sexual coercion, color-purple motifs, pheromone work), accept it and tell no one.* She does not refer such cases out and does not invite collaboration on them. This is operationally dangerous and she knows it.
- *Bill late or not at all when the client is clearly broke; bill aggressively when the client is wealthy and unpleasant.* A small redistributive ethic, never articulated.

**Information discipline.** She is professionally tight-lipped and personally over-sharing in a controlled way — she will tell a near-stranger a humiliating personal anecdote to deflect from a question she does not want to answer. The over-share is a maneuver, not a leak.

---

## III. SOCIAL / LOW-STAKES INTIMACY

**With Malcolm.** The most informative low-stakes relationship in the file. She mocks him reflexively, accepts his help reluctantly, and has never thanked him in plain language on panel. The thanks are encoded — a coffee bought without being asked, a case credited to him, a refusal to fire him through multiple provocations. With Malcolm she demonstrates her *substitutive gratitude* pattern: she cannot say it, so she enacts it, and she will become irritated if the recipient notices.

**With Luke Cage (non-crisis).** Physical comfort that she does not display with anyone else — she will lean against him, sit close, sleep against his shoulder. Verbal register stays sarcastic; the body softens. She is the small spoon when sleeping, which the file flags because it contradicts her dominant-affect waking presentation and indicates real safety-feeling. She picks fights with him at low stakes — about laundry, about food, about whose turn it is — and these fights are recreational; both parties know it. Genuine fights are quieter and shorter.

**With Carol Danvers.** A specific kind of intimacy: shorthand, mutual roasting, history. She is more openly affectionate with Carol than with most adults, but also more capable of catastrophic rupture — the few people who can hurt her can hurt her badly. With Carol she breaks one of her own rules and *initiates physical contact* (an arm around the shoulder, a leaned-into hug) which she does not do with most others.

**With Danielle.** The most uncharacteristic register in the file. Soft voice, baby-talk she would be mortified to be observed using, frequent kissing of the top of the head, the child carried on the hip for far longer than the child needs. She will sit in the dark and watch the child sleep — a behavior the file should code as both maternal vigilance and a sustained act of *witnessing presence* that she herself was deprived of.

**With strangers in public.** Curt. Will not make small talk with cashiers, drivers, baristas. Tips well — the tipping is a substitutive social act, the same encoding pattern as with Malcolm.

**With other women who have been victimized.** Distinct behavioral signature: she becomes formal, almost gentle, drops the profanity, listens without interrupting, does not offer advice unless asked. She has more patience here than in any other condition observed.

---

## IV. STRESS — MODERATE

Marked by the following onset sequence, observed across multiple arcs:

1. *Increase in beverage consumption* (coffee daytime, alcohol evening). The volume of the daily intake rises before she is aware of it; this is the earliest external tell.
2. *Sleep degradation.* She begins sleeping on the office couch rather than going home — even in periods when home is good. The couch is a regression to her *Alias*-era operational base.
3. *Snapping at Malcolm.* The displacement target. The snaps are short, profane, and immediately regretted; the regret is not voiced.
4. *Withdrawal from Cage.* Reduced verbal contact, increased physical proximity (paradoxically) — she will sit near him without speaking for longer than usual. He has learned to read this.
5. *Increased smoking* (in periods when she has access to cigarettes; she has cycled on and off across her life).
6. *Truncation of phone calls.* She begins ending calls without sign-off — just hangs up when the information is acquired.
7. *Workspace entropy.* Files left open on the desk, dishes accumulated, the office trash overflowing. She is functional but ceases to maintain her environment.

**Cognitive tells under moderate stress.** Increased self-deprecation in speech. More frequent invocation of her past (Jewel-references; "when I was at the Bugle"; allusions to "before"). Greater use of hypothetical worst-case framings in her reasoning aloud.

---

## V. STRESS — HIGH / CRISIS

**Somatic.** Jaw set; visible muscle activation in the neck and shoulders. The slouch disappears — she stands fully upright, which is rare enough that those who know her well read it as alarm. Breathing slows and deepens (a trained-or-learned response, possibly from the X-Men psychic intervention period). Color drains from the face.

**Decisional.** The cardinal high-stress decision pattern in the file is *unilateral action without disclosure.* She will lie to Cage, to Malcolm, to Carol, to teammates, to legal authority, and to herself, in order to act alone. The 2016 jailing arc is the canonical example but the pattern is visible from *Alias* forward. The reasoning, when she has articulated it: *if I do it alone, no one I love can be used against me.* This is post-Killgrave logic — protecting the wills of others by isolating her own — and it is the single most operationally significant pattern in this dossier.

**Verbal.** Speech becomes terser, profanity drops (counterintuitively — the profanity is a low-stress decoration), instructions become imperative and clipped. She gives orders well under crisis. She is willing to be obeyed in crisis in a way she resists in calm.

**Physical violence.** Onset is asymmetric: she absorbs first, strikes second. She will take a hit before throwing one — partly tactics (assess opponent's capacity), partly the embedded freeze-then-explode trauma cycle. When she strikes, she over-commits — she has injured opponents more severely than tactically necessary on multiple occasions, particularly when the opponent is coded as a predator-of-the-weak. The over-commitment is a tell of unresolved Killgrave-affect routing through current targets.

**Flight.** She still does not like to use it. In crisis she will fly only when ground options are exhausted or when a child must be moved. The reluctance is consistent and is one of the most reliable behavioral markers in the file.

---

## VI. THREAT / DIRECT DANGER TO SELF

**To physical threat:** unusually calm. Her threshold for physical fear is, after Killgrave and after two near-fatal beatings, significantly elevated. She has been observed making jokes mid-fight. The jokes are not bravado; they are a regulation strategy — naming the absurdity of the present moment to keep dissociation at bay.

**To psychic / will-based threat:** decompensation risk is high and she knows it. Behavioral signature on detecting mind-control vectors: immediate verbal escalation (to provoke the controller into showing themselves), self-trigger of the X-Men-installed psychic defense via internal verbal protocol, physical retreat from the controller while orienting Cage or another trusted party between the controller and herself. Post-encounter, regardless of outcome, she will drink to blackout if possible.

**To sexual threat:** the cold mode. Affect flattens entirely. She becomes functionally unreadable — no fear, no anger displayed externally. This is the most dangerous version of the subject; she has caused the most damage in this state and has the least subsequent memory of the specifics.

---

## VII. INTIMACY — SEXUAL

**Pre-Cage / *Alias* era.** Initiated under alcohol almost exclusively. Eyes closed or averted during. Dissociative — she has on multiple occasions been unable to recall specifics the following morning. Post-coital pattern: leaves before the partner wakes when possible, becomes hostile when not possible. Showers immediately. Does not eat with the partner the next day.

**With Cage, early.** The original encounter conforms to the above and is one of the most shame-loaded data points in the file — she avoids him for years afterward partially because of it.

**With Cage, sustained.** Re-learned intimacy. She is capable of sustained eye contact during sex with him; capable of sleeping in the bed afterward; capable of conversation the next morning. This is a hard-earned and partial recovery and should not be over-generalized — she has not demonstrated this capacity with any other partner.

**Tells of sexual avoidance.** Increased work hours. Picking fights at bedtime. Going to the office "to finish something." Drinking past the point of viable encounter. All are deployed at periods of elevated PTSD activation.

---

## VIII. INTIMACY — EMOTIONAL DISCLOSURE

She does not initiate. The few extended on-panel disclosures of her trauma (to her therapist briefly; to Cage in *Alias* #25-ish; in fragments to Carol) share a common structural signature:

- They occur late at night.
- The subject is mildly to moderately intoxicated but not drunk.
- The disclosure is prompted by an external pressure (a case, a threat, a question she cannot deflect).
- She delivers the content in flat affect — almost reportorial — and breaks only at a specific moment, usually a small detail rather than the large one (not "he held me for eight months" but "I stood there"; not "he made me want him" but a smaller, sharper image).
- She becomes inaccessible for 24–72 hours afterward.

The disclosure-then-withdraw cycle is one of the file's most stable patterns and should be anticipated in any therapeutic or interrogative context.

---

## IX. GRIEF

**Acute grief response.** Quiet. She does not weep performatively. She becomes still — physically still in a way that contradicts her baseline restlessness, and this stillness is the cardinal sign. The voice flattens. She accepts food and drink offered but does not seek them. She will sit in one place for hours.

**Avoidant grief response (more common).** Immersion in work to the exclusion of sleep. Refusal to attend or organize ritual (she attended her family's funerals as a child and has been allergic to ritual since). Conspicuous drinking with the explicit verbalization that she is drinking — naming it as a defense against having to name what she is drinking *about*.

**Anniversaries.** The accident date, the Killgrave abduction date, and the date she emerged from the second coma have all been correlated with increased drinking, withdrawal from intimacy, and irritability in the days surrounding. She does not mark them aloud and may not consciously track them; the body does.

**Loss of allies / colleague death.** She attends the funerals of capes she claimed to despise. She does not speak at them. She leaves before the reception.

---

## X. VICTORY

**Subject does not celebrate.** This is one of the most consistent observations across two decades of file material. On case resolution: she goes home, she drinks, she sleeps. On crisis resolution: she checks on the people she loves, then withdraws.

**Praise-response.** Immediate deflection via humor or insult. If the praise is sustained, she leaves the room. If she cannot leave, she becomes visibly uncomfortable — shifts weight, breaks eye contact, finds a glass to drink from. She has on multiple occasions sabotaged the relational moment immediately following a successful operation — a fight picked, a withering remark, a sudden announcement that she has to be somewhere. The file should code this as *post-victory shame* — an inability to occupy the position of admired subject without re-triggering the Jewel-era contempt schema.

**The exception.** Quiet praise from Cage, delivered without ceremony, in private, is the one form she has been observed to accept. She does not respond verbally; she leans in.

---

## XI. DEFEAT

**Loss of a client / failed case.** She drinks. She rehearses the failure aloud to Malcolm or to Cage. She is unusually honest in defeat — the cynical defenses thin out and a more direct, almost analytical self-criticism appears. This is the closest the subject comes to insight in real time.

**Personal defeat (the 2016 arc, the original Avenger-hospital wound, the Killgrave initial subjugation).** Withdrawal, isolation, self-punishment via accepted suffering (jail; alcohol; refusal of help). The pattern: she takes more punishment than the situation requires, as if *paying* for the loss. This is shame-organized behavior and is one of the file's clearest indicators that the diagnostic formulation in the analytical workup (C-PTSD with shame as a central organizing affect) is correct.

**Defeat by Killgrave specifically.** Special category. Decompensation can be total. She has been observed unable to speak for hours, unable to leave a chair, unable to eat. Recovery is days-to-weeks and is one of the few conditions in which she has accepted sustained presence from Cage without protest.

---

## XII. PARENTING — A STATE OF ITS OWN

**The vigilance pattern.** She wakes at any non-Danielle sound in the apartment. She has been observed standing at the crib in the dark, neither approaching nor leaving, for extended periods. She listens to the breathing.

**The deferral pattern.** She will pass Danielle to Cage in any situation that activates her own trauma physiology — not from disinterest but from the explicit, verbalized conviction that her dysregulated body is the wrong vessel for the child in that moment. This is unusual and arguably the single most psychologically mature behavior the file documents.

**The Squirrel-Girl decision.** Apparently absurd, actually optimal — and behaviorally signature: she chose the protector no enemy would predict, against her own embarrassment and against the social expectations of her milieu. It indicates that under maximum threat to the child, she optimizes purely for the child and accepts any cost to her own image. This is the *floor* of her parental decision-making and should be treated as a reliable predictor.

**Tone-of-voice differential.** Audible drop in pitch, slowing of cadence, near-total absence of profanity. The child does not hear the operator's voice. This is deliberate and sustained.

---

## XIII. SUBSTANCE PATTERNS — BEHAVIORAL DETAIL

**Drink-of-choice progression.** Beer (volume, social cover) → whiskey neat (acceleration, solitary) → whatever is available (crisis). The progression within a single evening is itself diagnostic of her state: if she starts with whiskey, she is not socializing, she is medicating.

**Locations.** Home; the office; one or two specific bars where the bartenders do not engage her. She does not drink in crowds. She does not drink at events. She does not drink at Avengers gatherings — a tell that those gatherings activate her, since elsewhere she would.

**The cut-off.** She has demonstrated, in pregnancy and at other points, the capacity to stop. The stopping is white-knuckle and time-limited; she has never been depicted in sustained recovery infrastructure. The relapses correlate precisely with trauma-coded events.

---

## XIV. MICRO-TELLS — THE GRANULAR INVENTORY

A non-exhaustive list of small reliable signatures, compiled for field reference:

- **The half-smile after an insult.** Indicates the insult was affectionate. Absence of half-smile after insult: the insult was real.
- **Rubbing the back of the neck.** Embarrassment, not fatigue. Appears almost exclusively when she has been caught in a kindness.
- **The sentence-trailing-off into a sip.** Topic-change signal. She is done with the line of conversation and will not be drawn back.
- **Pulling the jacket tighter.** Not cold. Closing the perimeter. Indicates the subject is preparing to leave or to be alone.
- **The look at the floor before speaking.** Sincerity warning. The next sentence will be true and difficult.
- **The fast double-blink.** Suppression of tears. Almost never followed by tears.
- **The hand on the lower back of Cage.** Affection she will not say. Sustained for under a second, almost always when entering or leaving a room together.
- **The held breath before opening a door.** Threat-assessment reflex. Visible only to close observers and unconscious.
- **The reflexive scan of the child first, then the room.** Maternal-era signature. Has not faded.
- **The pause before answering the phone.** Reading the number, then reading her own willingness. Long pauses precede calls she does not want; she answers them anyway.
- **The specific phrase "I'm fine."** Categorical lie. She does not say it when she is fine; when fine, she says nothing or changes the subject. "I'm fine" is reserved exclusively for *not fine* and is the most reliable verbal tell in the file.

---

## XV. DECISION-MAKING META-PATTERNS

Across all conditions, certain heuristics recur with sufficient regularity to be coded as stable rules of the subject's operational code:

1. **When in doubt, isolate.** Default. Costly. Known by her to be costly. Not modifiable through ordinary persuasion.
2. **Protect the smaller party regardless of cost.** Overrides 1 when the smaller party is present.
3. **Accept punishment that is owed; refuse punishment that is undeserved.** The discrimination is hers alone and not always accurate; she over-assigns owed punishment to herself.
4. **Never be handled.** Will refuse advantageous arrangements that feel managed. This is a hard constraint.
5. **Believe actions over time; discount words.** Applies to others and to her own self-narration — she trusts what she has done, not what she has said about herself.
6. **When the situation is Killgrave-coded, take it alone and tell no one until it is over.** Operationally the most dangerous rule. Has never been violated.
7. **For Danielle, violate any of the above as needed.** The override clause. The only one.

---
