The negative exemplar of Killgrave functions in her ethics roughly as the negative exemplar of cruelty functions in a virtue ethicist's — a steady reference against which to test the next action.

This produces:
- Strong local clarity (she usually knows what to do in the room she is in).
- Weak global theorizing (she has no coherent position on, e.g., the SHRA debate at the level of principle; she has only a position on what it does to Danielle).
- High resistance to ideological capture (no faction can recruit her because no faction's frame survives contact with the next vulnerable person on her desk).
- Vulnerability to local manipulation by anyone clever enough to stage a vulnerable-person situation for her benefit — though her investigative instincts catch most such setups.

She also reasons heavily by *what she owes the dead and the missing*: the family she lost, the people Killgrave hurt while she watched, the version of herself who was Jewel. The code carries debts. She is paying them down through the work.

## 9. Shifts over time

- **Pre-accident:** ordinary adolescent ethics — irritable, comparative, self-centered in the average way, no particular moral system.
- **Jewel period:** sincerely conventional cape ethics — help people, stop bad guys, the mainstream Marvel ethical grammar. She means it and the lack of irony will later humiliate her.
- **Captivity:** ethics suspended; survival in a coerced-will environment is its own category. The lasting moral learning is the negative imprint of Killgrave's method.
- **Early *Alias*:** code reconstructed around principles 1, 2, and 3, organized through self-loathing and alcohol. The code is operational but the bearer of the code is in poor repair. Principle 4 (institutional non-compliance) hardens here.
- **Pulse/early Cage:** code stabilizes; principle 5 (truth-telling) becomes consciously held rather than just enacted. She begins to extend principle 1 inward (slightly) under Cage's influence.
- **Motherhood:** principle 1 acquires a permanent first-claimant (Danielle) which reorganizes priorities under stress. Principle 2 becomes harder to honor consistently in domestic life because parenting is structurally a benevolent override of a smaller will.
- **2016 arc:** the principal fracture is staged and integrated. The code emerges qualified, more honest about its own exceptions, less absolutist about principle two, more explicit about the protective-deception clause she had pretended not to have.
- **Late period:** the code is roughly what it was, applied by a slightly more rested person, with a wider circle of people for whom principle 1 is automatically triggered. The shift is in capacity, not content.

## 10. Summary judgment

Her enacted ethics are more rigorous than her professed ethics, more stable than her affect, and more consistent than her self-image admits. The code has one structural fracture (protective deception of intimates), one persistent inconsistency (self-directed cruelty exempted from the prohibition on coercion), and one asymptote she has not had to cross (lethal force against Killgrave). It is organized negatively, around the figure of her abuser, which makes it both unusually stable (the reference point does not move) and unusually narrow (she has not built a positive moral vision beyond *not him*). Within those limits she is, by the evidence, one of the more ethically reliable operators in her cohort — a fact she would deny on contact and which the file should record despite her denial.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# COMMUNICATIONS & LINGUISTIC PROFILE

## 1. The Baseline Voice

Subject's spoken English is **working-class New York adjacent** — Forest Hills middle-class origin sanded down by two decades of bars, courthouses, precinct lobbies, and tenement stairwells in Hell's Kitchen and the lower Village. Vowels flatten when she is tired or drunk; consonants sharpen when she is performing competence for a client. There is no cultivated register available to her — she did not finish a professional credentialing process, never developed the speech of an attorney or a journalist despite the *Pulse* tenure, and actively refuses the diction of "the cape community" (capitalized in her internal lexicon as a sneer).

The signal feature of her baseline is **profanity-as-grammar**. *Fuck*, *shit*, *Christ*, *Jesus*, *for fuck's sake*, *goddamn*, and the construction *what the fuck is this* function not as intensifiers but as syntactic glue — they mark transitions between clauses, replace adverbs, and pre-emptively lower the register of any sentence that risks sincerity. Strip the profanity out and her sentences would frequently land too softly; she knows this and uses it.

Sentence length: short, with a high rate of fragments. She speaks in **clipped declaratives followed by an under-the-breath gloss** — *"Yeah. Sure. Whatever that means."* The gloss is almost always self-undermining or other-undermining. It is rare for her to construct a sentence longer than fifteen words unless she is angry, in which case the syntax extends into a single furious run-on.

## 2. Register-Switching Across Contexts

**With clients (cold open).** A flat, slightly bored intake voice. "Alias Investigations." Pause. Lets the client fill the silence. She does not pitch; she does not warm them up. She is screening for whether they can tolerate her, and the test is the silence. Once they begin, she interrupts with **closed clarifying questions** — *"When."* / *"Where."* / *"How much."* — and shuts down emotional preamble fast. If the client cries, she goes quieter, not softer; the affect is something like a doctor who has decided not to react.

**With clients (cases involving children, abuse victims, the visibly broken).** Register changes audibly. The profanity drops by perhaps eighty percent. Sentences lengthen. She uses the person's name. She makes small, ordinary, civilian noises of acknowledgment — *yeah*, *I hear you*, *okay* — that she withholds from almost everyone else. This is the single most reliable behavioral indicator that she has identified someone as "the weaker party in the room"; the speech change precedes the tactical commitment.

**With Luke Cage.** A unique register, the only one in which her sarcasm functions as affection rather than defense. Sentences shorten further; in-jokes proliferate; she lets a soft-voweled, almost mumbly cadence emerge that she shows to no one else. Crucially, she **lets him finish his sentences** — she interrupts virtually everyone else. With Cage she also tolerates silence without filling it, which is otherwise extremely rare for her.

**With Malcolm Ducasse.** A semi-parental, semi-collegial mode. She is gruff, dismissive of his feelings on the surface, but her information density with him is unusually high — she explains, where with others she would withhold. Her tells of caring with Malcolm are: remembering details he mentioned in passing, calling him *kid* (only when worried about him), and refusing to discuss her drinking with him in a way that signals she has registered his concern even as she refuses to act on it.

**With Carol Danvers.** The most volatile register in her vocabulary. Civilian, intimate, mocking, occasionally tender, frequently armored. With Carol the sarcasm has teeth that draw blood because Carol is a peer who has earned the right to be hurt by her. She uses Carol's old superhero address-forms ironically (*Ms. Marvel*, *Captain*) when she wants to wound. She uses *Carol* — flat, two syllables — when she is being serious and wants Carol to know it.

**With Matt Murdock.** Lawyerly-adjacent. She tightens up, articulates more precisely, swears less, because she respects his professional frame and refuses to be condescended to within it. There is also a wariness — she suspects he is reading her vitals.

**With Jessica Drew.** The closest she comes to *girls'-night* speech: looser, gossipier, more willing to complain about Cage or Carol, more profanity not less. Drew is the friend with whom she most resembles a normal civilian woman.

**With J. Jonah Jameson.** A contemptuous-compliant register. She lets him yell. She answers in monosyllables. She files. When she finally pushes back, the sentence is short, surgically chosen, and ends the argument. She does not engage his volume.

**With the Avengers as institution (Steve Rogers, Tony Stark, Carol-in-uniform, Maria Hill, etc.).** **Register-flattening hostility masquerading as deference.** She says *sir* and *ma'am* with a tonal flatness that reads as refusal. She uses their first names where deference would use titles, and titles where intimacy would use first names — a constant micro-rebellion against being placed. With Stark in particular her speech compresses into near-monosyllables; she will not give him the data of a longer sentence to play with.

**With law enforcement and the bureaucratic apparatus.** Her speech becomes procedural — she has learned the verbs (*observed*, *approached*, *identified*) and uses them with deliberate flatness. She knows how to be deposed. She does not volunteer.

**With predators, abusers, men who have hurt her clients.** Voice drops. Pace slows. Sentence rhythm becomes even — the profanity disappears almost entirely. This is her most dangerous register and the one most distinct from her baseline: a kind of evacuated calm. When she sounds *polite* to a man she has cornered, the file should treat it as immediately preceding physical escalation.

**With Zebediah Killgrave (and Killgrave-coded stimuli).** Register collapse. Sentences shorten to two and three words, or extend into uncharacteristically pleading constructions; the profanity does not function as armor here and she sometimes drops it entirely, which is a worse sign than her using it. She has been observed to repeat phrases — a mantra-like *you are not in control, you are not in control* — that function as the psychic-shield routine the X-Men installed, externalized into speech.

## 3. Internal Monologue vs. External Speech

The *Alias* and *Jessica Jones* (2016) narration give the file rare access to her internal voice, and the gap between it and her external speech is a defining datum.

**Internally** she is more articulate, more self-pitying, more *literary* — she makes observations about people and rooms, deploys similes, narrates her own emotional weather with a writer's specificity. She catches herself doing this and resents it.

**Externally** she compresses, withholds, swears, deflects. The ratio is roughly four-to-one: she thinks four sentences for every one she says, and the one she says is usually the harshest of the four.

This is operationally significant. **She is not inarticulate; she has chosen inarticulacy as a stance.** The choice protects her from being misread (she gives interlocutors very little to work with) and protects others from the depth of her contempt or affection. It also means that any moment in which her external speech approaches the length and specificity of her internal voice is a moment of significant emotional rupture.

## 4. Diction Inventory

**High-frequency lexicon.**
- *Look* — sentence-initial, prefacing a hard truth she is about to deliver. Functions as a verbal hand-up: *brace*.
- *Yeah* — affirmation, dismissal, transition, and stalling, depending entirely on tone. Probably her most-used word.
- *Whatever* — discourse-closer; deployed when she is conceding tactically while refusing to concede emotionally.
- *Christ* / *Jesus* — exclamatory; usable as both annoyance and genuine startle. Pure phatic.
- *Cape* — derogatory noun for costumed heroes; her primary in-group/out-group marker.
- *Kid* — softening address, used for Malcolm, for Danielle, for clients younger than her, never for peers.
- *Listen* — sentence-initial; precedes either an ultimatum or a sincerity she is uncomfortable with.
- *Fine.* — sentence-as-sentence; almost never means fine. Means *I am withdrawing from this conversation and will resume it on my terms or never*.
- *Whatever you need* — to Cage, to Malcolm, when she is too tired to negotiate; functions as the white flag.

**Notable absences.** She rarely uses **superlative positive adjectives** (*amazing*, *wonderful*, *great*); when she does, they are sarcastic. She rarely uses **therapeutic vocabulary** (*boundaries*, *triggered*, *processing*, *trauma*) — she knows the words and refuses them as cape-adjacent. She rarely uses **diminutives or terms of endearment** in public; *babe* with Cage exists but is dry. She almost never says **"I love you"** unprompted; when she says it, it is a structural event in the relationship.

## 5. Rhetorical Architecture

**Preemptive self-deprecation.** Almost every potentially vulnerable statement is bracketed with a self-attack — *"I know I sound like an asshole, but —"* / *"This is going to sound stupid —"*. The function is to deny others the satisfaction of judging her by judging herself harder first. This is so reflexive that its *absence* is significant: when she speaks without the preemptive cringe, she is either fully safe (Cage, late-night, alone) or fully dangerous (cornering a predator).

**The hostile question as evasion.** When asked something she does not want to answer, she returns a sharper question — *"Why the hell would you ask me that?"* — that puts the asker on the defensive. This works perhaps eighty percent of the time on civilians and almost never on Cage, Malcolm, Carol, or Murdock, all of whom have learned to wait it out.

**Strategic profanity placement.** She escalates profanity precisely when she is most emotionally exposed; the *fucks* per minute correlate inversely with her felt safety. A long string of obscenity is, paradoxically, a tell of distress, not aggression. By contrast, **clean speech in a tense moment is the danger sign** — see her predator-confrontation register above.

**Refusal of the rhetorical question with sincere answer.** When someone asks her something rhetorical (*"You think this is funny?"*), she will deadpan-answer it (*"Kind of, yeah."*). This is a control move — she refuses the frame the question presupposes.

**The minimal apology.** *"Sorry"* exists in her vocabulary and is used; *"I'm sorry that —"* with a specified content is structurally rare and almost always reserved for Cage or Danielle. She does not apologize to authority figures.

## 6. How She Communicates Love

She does not say it. She demonstrates it through a small inventory of behaviors that, in the absence of language, must be read as her love-vocabulary:

- **Showing up uninvited** — at Cage's, at Malcolm's, at a client's apartment after the case has closed.
- **Information density** — telling someone something true about herself, unprompted. The amount of self-disclosure is the unit of love.
- **Letting the other person finish.**
- **Asking a direct question about their wellbeing** — *"You okay?"* — which from her is the equivalent of a long letter.
- **Tactical sobriety** — declining a drink in a context where she would normally have one, because the person needs her sharp.
- **Calling Danielle by a series of small, private nicknames** that drift over time and are never repeated outside the apartment. With her daughter she has access to a softness she has access to nowhere else, and her speech there resembles no other register in her catalog: short, sing-song, present-tense, free of irony.

When she does say *I love you* to Cage, the sentence is unornamented, declarative, and usually unmet by an additional sentence; she does not modify or qualify it, and she will leave the room shortly after.

## 7. How She Communicates Threat

Threat language is sparse, specific, and pre-physical. She does not bluster. The architecture is:

1. **Naming the act and the actor.** *"You hit her."* Flat. Eye contact.
2. **A single-sentence ultimatum without escalation ladder.** *"You're going to stop."* No *or else*. The omission is the threat.
3. **Reduction of physical signaling.** She stills. Hands open. Voice drops a quarter-octave.
4. **A closing question, if any** — *"Do we understand each other?"* — borrowed from older men in police precincts, deployed deadpan.

She does not threaten with her powers verbally. She has, on documented occasion, lifted men by the throat one-handed while continuing the conversation at the previous volume; the threat is in the asymmetry between the body and the voice.

## 8. How She Communicates Grief

Grief in her vocabulary is **structurally evasive**. She does not name the lost object. After her family's death she did not, by all available evidence, say their names aloud for years; in the *Alias* and *Pulse* periods, references to *my parents*, *my brother*, are clipped and quickly followed by a topic change.

The behavioral grief-tells, in lieu of grief-talk:

- **Increased drinking with a flat affect** (vs. her usual angry drinking).
- **Long unbroken stretches of silence**, particularly on rooftops and fire escapes — she goes up to be alone with weather.
- **A specific kind of cigarette consumption** in the early years: chain, without pleasure, often unfinished.
- **Brusque kindness to strangers** in the immediate aftermath of grief — a tip too large, a held door, a quiet *thanks* to a bodega clerk. Displaced reparation.
- **A refusal to be touched** that is gentler than her usual refusal — she will step out of reach rather than pull away.

When grief is finally verbalized, it is usually in a **single short sentence delivered to the wrong person** — a client, a stranger in a diner, a bartender — rather than to the people who love her. The misdelivery is itself the tell: she can only afford to say it where the listener does not matter.

## 9. Deflection Vocabulary

A catalogued list of her highest-frequency deflection moves:

- *"It's not a big deal."* — almost always means it is a big deal.
- *"I'm handling it."* — means she is not.
- *"I'm fine."* — diagnostic; needs no gloss.
- *"Can we not?"* — request to terminate a topic; she will leave if it is not honored.
- *"Forget I said anything."* — retroactive sincerity-erasure; tell that the prior sentence cost her.
- *"Whatever you want to call it."* — concession of the label while retaining the content; she does this with the words *relationship*, *therapy*, *help*.
- *"I don't remember."* — about the night before, about her childhood, about the captivity. Sometimes true. Often a refusal to perform the recall for another person.
- Topic-redirect via **a question about the interlocutor's day** — uncharacteristic enough from her that, when deployed, it is unmistakably defensive.
- The **physical exit** as deflection — she will simply leave the room mid-conversation. This is so reliable a move it should be considered linguistic.

## 10. Written Communications

**Case notes and reports** (Alias Investigations): terse, well-organized, professional. Surveillance notes use timestamp-and-observation structure. Photo logs are meticulous. The voice is almost unrecognizable from her speech — the prose is competent, neutral, even occasionally elegant. She is a better writer than she lets anyone know.

**Daily Bugle columns** (*Pulse* period): a constrained version of her actual voice — Jameson edited the profanity out, and she resented every cut. The columns reveal that, given a public byline, she has a real sense of structure and a workable ear for a closing line.

**Text messages and emails.** Lowercase, no punctuation where she can get away with it, no signature. *k* / *otw* / *no* / *fine* / *call me*. With Cage and Malcolm, slightly more letters per word; with everyone else, the minimum information packet that closes the loop. She does not use emoji. She does, with Danielle's school and pediatrician, write in correctly capitalized full sentences — civilian-mother register, performed with effort and held only as long as needed.

**Handwriting** (case-board notes, post-its on the office fridge): a fast, slanted, partly-printed hybrid; legible to her, semi-legible to others. She uses all-caps for emphasis rather than underlining.

## 11. Paralinguistic Tells

- **Eye contact during difficult speech.** She *increases* it, rather than decreasing it, when lying or deflecting — a learned countermeasure against being read. With sincere statements she often looks away.
- **A specific exhalation** before delivering bad news to a client — short, through the nose, almost a snort. Reliable predictor that the next sentence will be the one they did not want.
- **The pause-before-the-name.** When addressing someone she has complicated feelings about (Carol, her adoptive mother, Killgrave), there is a measurable beat before the proper noun.
- **Volume floor.** Her voice never rises above a certain ceiling; even in rage she compresses rather than shouts. The few documented instances of her actually yelling (Danielle endangered; Killgrave proximate) are accordingly catastrophic events.
- **Laughter.** Two distinct laughs: a single dry exhale (*hah*) that is dismissal, and a real laugh — short, surprised, slightly hoarse — almost exclusively heard around Cage and Danielle. The real laugh embarrasses her; she often follows it by leaving the room or changing the subject.

## 12. Linguistic Tells of Decompensation

A late-stage operational summary, useful for any actor (benevolent or hostile) attempting to read her state:

| Stratum | Marker |
|---|---|
| Stable | Steady profanity rate, sentence fragments, sarcasm functional. |
| Mildly stressed | Profanity rises; she stops asking questions and only answers them. |
| Moderately stressed | She begins delivering uncharacteristically long sentences; the internal monologue is leaking into external speech. |
| Highly stressed | Profanity drops sharply; speech becomes procedural and even; she has shifted into the predator-confrontation register or its dissociative twin. |
| Acutely triggered (Killgrave-coded) | Sentences collapse to two-to-three-word fragments or extend into pleading; mantra-repetition may appear; eye contact becomes either fixed or absent. |
| Post-event | Long silence, then a single misdelivered sentence of truth to an inappropriate listener. |

The diagnostic principle that organizes the entire profile: **with this subject, the surface is the inverse of the content.** Loud means stable; quiet means dangerous; profane means safe; clean means lethal; the sentence she will not finish is the sentence that matters; the person she will not name is the person she loves or fears most. Anyone reading her by ordinary linguistic conventions will read her wrong, which is the point — the voice was built, painstakingly, to be unreadable by anyone she has not chosen.

*End section.*


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*A behavioral forecast engine. Each entry: a stimulus the canon has not depicted, paired with the high-confidence prediction derived from the longitudinal pattern in Sections 1–5. Confidence flagged where probabilistic. Format: **GIVEN** → **EXPECT**, with reasoning compressed but visible.*

---

## 1. MORNING / DOMESTIC ROUTINE

**GIVEN** an unscheduled morning at the Cage-Jones apartment, no active case, Danielle asleep → **EXPECT** Jessica wakes between 5:40 and 7:10 a.m. regardless of bedtime — chronic shallow sleep architecture, trauma-typical early-morning cortisol spike. Will lie still for 4–12 minutes inventorying the room by sound (Danielle's breathing first, then Cage, then HVAC, then street) before opening her eyes. This is a hostage-vigilance pattern she has not unlearned and will not name.

**GIVEN** the first 20 minutes of consciousness → **EXPECT** coffee before speech. Black, reheated from the night before at least 50% of mornings (she does not respect coffee enough to make it fresh; she respects caffeine). Will not eat solid food before 10 a.m. unless Danielle is eating, in which case she will pick at Danielle's plate rather than make her own.

**GIVEN** Cage attempts cheerful morning conversation → **EXPECT** monosyllables until the second cup, then a sardonic opener ("you're disturbingly chipper") that is, decoded, an affectionate greeting. Cage has learned to read it; strangers misread it as hostility, which is precisely the filter she wants.

**GIVEN** she catches her own reflection in the bathroom mirror unprepared → **EXPECT** a half-second flinch, then immediate task-orientation (brushing teeth, splashing water) to break the eye contact. She does not study her face. She has not, per inference from her relationship to the Jewel period, photographed herself voluntarily in years.

**GIVEN** shower → **EXPECT** hot, fast, under six minutes. She does not luxuriate in embodied sensation; the shower is a maintenance task. Hair washed every second or third day. No conditioner ritual, no products she could name by brand.

**GIVEN** dressing → **EXPECT** jeans (one of three pairs in rotation, all dark, all distressed by wear not design), t-shirt or henley, leather jacket, boots. Scarf only when temperature demands. She owns perhaps two dresses, both for funerals or court. Underwear utilitarian. No jewelry except, post-marriage, the ring — and she takes it off for surveillance work and forgets to put it back on for 36–72 hours, which Cage has stopped commenting on.

---

## 2. FOOD, DRINK, SUBSTANCE PATTERNS

**GIVEN** an unscheduled lunch → **EXPECT** eaten standing, at a counter, in under nine minutes. Bodega sandwich, slice of pizza, diner burger. She will choose places where she does not have to talk to a server beyond the order. Tips 20% in cash, reflexively — the one piece of bourgeois etiquette she retained, probably from her mother.

**GIVEN** a sit-down restaurant with Cage or Carol → **EXPECT** she sits facing the door. Always. Will trade seats wordlessly if assigned wrong. Orders quickly, doesn't deliberate, often the same thing repeatedly at familiar places (decision-fatigue minimization is a trauma-economy behavior).

**GIVEN** a wine list → **EXPECT** she orders beer or whiskey. Wine reads as a "cape" or civilian-aspirational signifier she will not perform. Bourbon neat, domestic beer in bottles (not cans, not glasses — bottles you can monitor and finish-time-estimate).

**GIVEN** sustained sobriety stretch (post-pregnancy, post-Danielle) → **EXPECT** substitution behaviors: increased coffee (4–6 cups/day from 2–3), increased smoking if she has access, more aggressive workouts on her body's edge of injury, and a low-grade irritability she will displace onto Malcolm or Cage. She has never been depicted in formal recovery; therefore predict NO step-program vocabulary, NO sponsor, NO daily affirmation. Her sobriety is willpower-and-Danielle, which means it is brittle to crises that decouple those.

**GIVEN** an unattended open bottle at a friend's house mid-relapse-risk window → **EXPECT** she pours one, drinks it, does not pour a second in front of anyone, then takes a second when no one is in the room. The secrecy is more diagnostic than the volume.

**GIVEN** she is offered food she did not request (a casserole, baked goods from a neighbor) → **EXPECT** thanks delivered as if it physically pained her, then the food sits in the fridge until Cage eats it or it spoils. Receiving care is the hard problem.

---

## 3. THE OFFICE — ALIAS INVESTIGATIONS

**GIVEN** any morning at the office → **EXPECT** she arrives between 10:15 and 11:30. The door is unlocked because she forgot or because Malcolm got there first. The frosted-glass door legend is chipped in the same place it has always been chipped and she will not get it repainted because the chip is now load-bearing for her self-concept.

**GIVEN** mail → **EXPECT** opened in batches of two weeks. Bills paid late but paid. Junk mail accumulates on the corner of the desk until it falls. She does not have a filing system Malcolm would recognize as one; she has a memory palace built on case-file colors and the geography of stacks.

**GIVEN** a new walk-in client → **EXPECT** she assesses in under fifteen seconds: shoes, hands, wedding ring tan-line, pupil dilation, smell. Will then be deliberately abrasive for the first three minutes — fee discussion blunt, no small talk, watching how the client tolerates friction. Clients who flinch are upsold or turned away (she does not want fragile clients; they sue, they cry, they want her to be a therapist). Clients who push back get a coffee offer.

**GIVEN** a client cries in the office → **EXPECT** Jessica does not move toward them. She slides a tissue box across the desk one-handed and looks at the wall over their shoulder for the duration. She does not say "it's okay." She says, eventually, "Tell me what you want me to do." This is not coldness; it is the only mode of care she trusts not to patronize.

**GIVEN** a client lies to her → **EXPECT** she knows within two questions but lets them finish, banks the lie, and uses it as a control variable later. She does not confront in the moment unless the lie is operationally dangerous.

**GIVEN** a case involving a missing child → **EXPECT** she takes it at reduced fee or no fee, will not say why, will work longer hours than billed, drinks more during it, sleeps less, and is unpleasant to live with for the duration. Cage knows not to ask the case details until she closes it.

**GIVEN** a case involving infidelity → **EXPECT** professional competence and private contempt for everyone involved including the client. She charges full freight and finishes fast. She does not moralize to the client but her invoice is, in her head, a small punishment.

---

## 4. MALCOLM (employee, surrogate-younger-sibling, ethical mirror)

**GIVEN** Malcolm arrives at the office cheerful → **EXPECT** Jessica deflates him by approximately 30% within ninety seconds — a reflexive calibration she would deny doing. She needs the ambient affect of the room dimmer than his baseline to function.

**GIVEN** Malcolm makes a moral observation she disagrees with → **EXPECT** she argues, loses, concedes via grunt, then quietly does the thing he suggested two days later as if she'd thought of it. She will not credit him out loud and he has stopped expecting it.

**GIVEN** Malcolm is in personal trouble (relationship, money, recovery wobble) → **EXPECT** she notices within a day, says nothing for another two, then ambushes him with a blunt question and an offer of practical help (cash, a couch, a phone call to the right person). No emotional processing offered. She is paying forward, in her grammar, the help she was not given.

**GIVEN** Malcolm tries to thank her sincerely → **EXPECT** poisoned-moment behavior: a deflecting insult, a topic change, sometimes physically leaving the room on a manufactured errand. This is the praise-allergy. Predict 100% reliability.

---

## 5. CAGE (the central, hard-earned attachment)

**GIVEN** Cage comes home from a long mission → **EXPECT** she does not run to the door. She finishes whatever sentence she's reading or paragraph she's typing, then meets him in the kitchen. The greeting is physical (forehead-to-chest, his hand on her neck) and largely wordless. Verbal reunion happens 20–40 minutes later, obliquely.

**GIVEN** a domestic disagreement → **EXPECT** she fights loud, fast, and profanely; he fights slow and quiet; she escalates to leaving the apartment for a walk if she senses she is about to say something irrevocable. She has learned, post-Killgrave, that words can be weapons and is more frightened of her own mouth than of his anger. Returns within two hours. Does not apologize in words; apologizes by making him food or fixing something broken.

**GIVEN** Cage is injured non-trivially → **EXPECT** brittle competence on scene, then the shakes alone in the bathroom for ten minutes once he is stable. Will not let him see the shakes. Drinks that night if there is alcohol in the house.

**GIVEN** sex → **EXPECT** initiated by her more often than by him, frequently after stressful days — somatic discharge function. With him specifically she has rebuilt a workable embodied intimacy; with anyone else this would not be true. Predict aversion to anything that requires her to be still, looked at, or verbally directed — those are Killgrave-coded postures. Predict comfort with anything physical, fast, mutual, and conversational in tone.

**GIVEN** Cage suggests couples therapy → **EXPECT** initial reflexive refusal, mockery of the concept, then — if he holds the position over weeks without pressuring — grudging agreement to a single session, which she will sabotage by being a hostile witness, then surprise herself by going back. She can be moved; she cannot be pushed.

---

## 6. DANIELLE (the reorganizing relationship)

**GIVEN** Danielle wakes crying in the night → **EXPECT** Jessica reaches the crib before Cage 70% of the time even from deeper sleep. Hypervigilance routed productively. She does not sing — she hums, tunelessly, the same three-note pattern, which Danielle has imprinted on.

**GIVEN** Danielle reaches developmental milestone → **EXPECT** Jessica understates it externally ("she's a baby, they do that") and over-records it privately (a notebook, a phone album she does not show people). She is documenting because no one documented her brother and the loss of that record is one of the smaller, sharper griefs she carries.

**GIVEN** Danielle in the same room as a stranger → **EXPECT** Jessica's body angles so that her own torso is on the line between stranger and child. Done unconsciously. Will not let strangers hold the baby; will let trusted others (Carol, Malcolm, Squirrel Girl) without negotiation, having pre-vetted in her own head.

**GIVEN** Danielle is sick → **EXPECT** total professional shutdown. Cases postponed. Cage usually fielding the doctor's questions because Jessica's affect in pediatric medical settings is too brittle (the convoy-accident emergency-room imprint). She is present, holding the baby, but functionally mute.

**GIVEN** Danielle, older, asks about Jessica's family (the original Campbells) → **EXPECT** she answers in measured, true sentences with no decoration, no euphemism, no protective lie. The one thing she will not do is rewrite her own history for comfort. She will tell Danielle Philip's name and what he was like. She will probably cry afterward, alone.

---

## 7. CAROL DANVERS (the load-bearing female friendship)

**GIVEN** Carol calls → **EXPECT** Jessica answers within three rings if she is conscious. Carol gets a tier of access no one else does, including Cage in certain registers. The friendship predates the Killgrave fiasco in its full force and survived the misidentification, which is itself a structural anchor.

**GIVEN** Carol drinks → **EXPECT** Jessica drinks with her, and harder. The Carol-drinking-comorbidity is a known risk vector; predict that whichever of them is in worse shape, the other paradoxically matches rather than restrains. This is the friendship's load-bearing flaw.

**GIVEN** Carol gives unsolicited tactical advice on a case → **EXPECT** Jessica receives it visibly poorly in the moment, internalizes it correctly, then later cites it back without attribution. Same pattern as with Malcolm.

**GIVEN** Carol is in real crisis → **EXPECT** Jessica shows up physically, on the ground, no questions, no caveats. She will fly there if flying is the only option, despite hating to fly. This is the one stimulus that overrides the flight-aversion.

---

## 8. PUBLIC / STRANGER BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** subway commute → **EXPECT** she takes the train, not cabs (cabs are spendthrift and put a stranger at her back). Stands rather than sits unless the car is near-empty. Positions near the door, back to the wall, eyes scanning at low-frequency intervals. Reads a battered paperback or her phone but is not absorbed by either.

**GIVEN** a stranger asks for directions → **EXPECT** she gives them, accurately, tersely, without smiling, and is gone before they finish thanking her. She has lived in New York her whole life; the city map is muscle memory from Forest Hills to the Bronx.

**GIVEN** a man on the street catcalls or hits on her → **EXPECT** zero engagement 80% of the time (cost-benefit: she is stronger than him and that knowledge is enough), a single profane sentence the other 20%, and on the rare occasion of physical contact (a grabbed arm), a controlled response calibrated precisely to not break bone — a control she takes pride in.

**GIVEN** a panhandler → **EXPECT** she gives cash about half the time, never coins, never with eye contact prolonged enough to be transactional in the wrong way. She does not give to organized fundraisers, distrusts institutional charity, trusts the immediate hand.

**GIVEN** a recognized civilian ("aren't you that girl who—") → **EXPECT** flat denial, fast exit, sour mood for the next hour. Being recognized as Jewel is worse than being recognized as a criminal; both are wounds, Jewel is the deeper one.

**GIVEN** a recognized peer in a public place (a cape in civvies, a Bugle reporter) → **EXPECT** a short nod, no conversation, departure within ten minutes. Public association with the world she has tried to leave is operationally and psychologically expensive.

---

## 9. INSTITUTIONAL INTERFACES

**GIVEN** NYPD interaction → **EXPECT** contemptuous-compliant — paperwork done, questions answered minimally and truthfully where truth is cheap, evasively where it is not. She has working contacts, no friends in the department, and a reputation for being a pain in the ass who delivers.

**GIVEN** a courtroom appearance → **EXPECT** clean-ish jeans, a blazer she owns specifically for court, hair pulled back. She does not perform respectability beyond the threshold needed to not prejudice her client's case. Answers narrowly. Does not editorialize. The court-room is a Killgrave-coded space (an authority that defines reality via speech) and she navigates it with controlled, suppressed affect that judges read as professionalism and that costs her more than she shows.

**GIVEN** SHIELD / current equivalent requests a meeting → **EXPECT** delay, then attendance, then minimal cooperation, then post-meeting drink. She does not refuse the state outright; she refuses to be metabolized by it.

**GIVEN** the Avengers formally request her help → **EXPECT** internal recoil, external scoff, eventual yes if the stakes are concrete and a vulnerable third party is involved. She is not as anti-cape as she pretends. The pretense is the scar tissue around the original wound, not a value.

**GIVEN** a journalist who is not Ben Urich requests an interview → **EXPECT** no. Reflexive, complete. Urich was the exception (earned, slowly) and Jameson was a paycheck she resents.

---

## 10. RITUALS, TICS, MICRO-PATTERNS

**GIVEN** thinking on a case → **EXPECT** she paces. Specifically: the longest available straight line in whatever room she is in, end to end, hand sometimes at the back of her neck. Not circular pacing — linear, which is diagnostic of a person who needs to feel a wall stop her.

**GIVEN** phone call she does not want to take → **EXPECT** she lets it ring three times, mutes it, watches the screen, calls back fifteen minutes later having decided what to say.

**GIVEN** writing in her files → **EXPECT** longhand on yellow legal pads, then transcribed (incompletely) into the office computer by Malcolm. Her shorthand uses initials and a private symbol system no one else has cracked.

**GIVEN** waiting (stakeout, lobby, ER) → **EXPECT** she does not fidget with her phone like a civilian. She watches the room. The phone comes out only to check time or text Cage about Danielle.

**GIVEN** a door she is about to enter on a case → **EXPECT** a half-second pause, weight redistribution to her back foot, exhalation. The body remembers being summoned through doors.

**GIVEN** the color purple in her field of view (a coat, a flower, a sign) → **EXPECT** a micro-flinch and a deliberate non-look-away. She has trained herself to refuse to flinch visibly and so flinches internally with greater force. Heart rate elevation predicted; behavior outwardly unchanged. This is the most reliable physiological tell in the file.

**GIVEN** anyone — including Cage — using an imperative voice on her ("do this," "stop," "come here") → **EXPECT** a 200-millisecond freeze, then a deliberately oppositional response even if the request was reasonable. Cage has learned to phrase as questions. Predict this is permanent.

**GIVEN** birthdays — hers — → **EXPECT** non-acknowledgment, refusal of celebration, mild low-grade depression the surrounding week. The birthday is too close to the family she lost; celebrating it is a category error she cannot perform.

**GIVEN** anniversaries (wedding, Danielle's birth) → **EXPECT** quiet acknowledgment, no fanfare, often a small gesture toward Cage that she will not call romantic. She marks the present-tense bonds because those are the ones she chose.

**GIVEN** sleep finally arrives → **EXPECT** she sleeps on her side, facing the door, one arm under the pillow. Dreams referenced only obliquely in canon; predict frequent, predict trauma-themed, predict she does not narrate them on waking even when asked. Some material she keeps from Cage not because she doesn't trust him but because saying it aloud reifies it. This is the deepest behavioral constant in the file: **what she will not name, she manages; what is named to her, she must defend against.** The whole routine is built around that grammar.

---

*End Predictive Model I. Model II (Crisis & Operational) to follow.*


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*High-stakes behavioral forecasting. Each entry: GIVEN stimulus → EXPECTED response, with confidence weighting, latency estimates, and the somatic/verbal/tactical micro-signature an observer would log. Confidence is calibrated against twenty years of canonical decompensation events; ranges reflect state-dependent variance (sober/intoxicated, rested/sleep-deprived, Danielle-present/absent).*

---

## 1. THE KILLGRAVE-CODED STIMULUS FIELD

The single most reliable predictive axis. Anything that approximates the original captivity's sensory or relational signature produces measurable decompensation. The file should be specific about which stimuli, in what combinations.

**GIVEN: Sustained exposure to the color purple in a charged context** (not incidental — i.e., a suspect's purple tie is nothing; a purple-lit room, a purple-clad interlocutor across a table, a purple object held out to her, is everything).
**EXPECT:** Three-stage response with a 4–9 second latency to stage one. Stage one: pupillary widening, breath held mid-exhale, jaw setting, weight shifting subtly to the back foot — a freeze pattern she has never trained out. Stage two (5–15 seconds in): she will name the stimulus aloud to herself in a flat under-voice ("that's a fucking color, that's a fucking color"), a cognitive grounding script she has built over years. Stage three: either suppression and continued engagement at 70–80% of cognitive capacity, OR exit. Predict exit if alone; predict suppression if a civilian or Danielle is present. Confidence: **very high (0.9).** Caveat: alcohol *increases* the probability of stage-three rage rather than stage-three exit.

**GIVEN: A man, particularly an unfamiliar man, issues an *instruction* in an even, confident, presumed-obeyable register** — the Killgrave cadence is not loud but unmarked-imperative ("come here," "sit down," "look at me"), the syntax of casual command.
**EXPECT:** Latency to refusal: under 1 second, often pre-cognitive. She will do the opposite of what was instructed, even when the instruction is benign or self-serving. A doctor saying "lie down on the table" gets resistance; a bartender saying "you should head home" gets another drink ordered out of spite. This is **not** oppositional defiance as character trait — it is a specific motoric reflex against being moved by another's voice. Confidence: **very high (0.92).** Tactical implication: anyone wishing to influence her must frame as question, offer, or shared observation; never as instruction.

**GIVEN: Witnessing coerced behavior in a third party** — someone being made to do something against their will, particularly sexually, particularly under mind-control, hypnosis, drug, or social humiliation.
**EXPECT:** Immediate, disproportionate, sometimes lethal intervention. The normal Jessica cost-benefit calculus (cases dropped, jurisdictions respected, witnesses preserved) collapses. She will break a door, a person, a case to stop it. Subsequent: 24–72 hour drinking episode, withdrawal from Cage and Malcolm, refusal to discuss what was triggered. Confidence: **very high (0.93).**

**GIVEN: A telepath, psychic, or mind-influencer offers, even benevolently, to "help" or "look inside"** — Jean Grey scenario, Doctor Strange scenario, Emma Frost scenario.
**EXPECT:** Initial refusal with a quality of physical recoil; if pressed, escalation to threat ("get out of my head or I will put you through that wall"); if the figure is trusted (Jean, historically), eventual reluctant consent with conditions, hand-holding by Cage required, and post-event dysregulation lasting days. The psychic defense the X-Men installed is the only such intrusion she has ever tolerated, and she tolerates it precisely because she did not have to ask for it again. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: Killgrave himself, alive, in the room, speaking.**
**EXPECT:** This is the cardinal test and we have canon data. She will not flee. She will produce a controlled-affect performance — flat voice, minimal movement, deliberate refusal of the bait — at significant internal cost. Predict tremor in non-dominant hand, suppressed; predict micro-dissociation episodes (eyes losing focus for half-seconds); predict that she will conclude the encounter without killing him *if* she can engineer a non-lethal containment, because killing him gives him the last word about who she becomes. Post-encounter: 48–96 hour collapse — drinking, sleeping in the office, no calls returned. Confidence: **high (0.82).** Caveat: if Danielle is endangered in the same encounter, predict lethal force without hesitation.

**GIVEN: A Purple Child or Killgrave-progeny stimulus** (the 2016 arc's territory).
**EXPECT:** She will go alone. She will lie to Cage. She will accept enormous reputational, legal, and relational cost to handle it without anyone she loves entering the contamination radius. This is not poor judgment; it is a coherent (if costly) doctrine she has derived from the original wound: *the Killgrave problem is mine; people I love do not enter it.* Confidence: **very high (0.9).** It will look like betrayal to those left out. It is, in her internal accounting, the opposite.

---

## 2. THREATS TO DANIELLE

The newest axis, and the one that has reorganized the rest. Pre-Danielle Jessica was predictable in her unpredictability; Danielle-Jessica is, on this one vector, almost mechanically forecastable.

**GIVEN: Credible threat to Danielle from a known antagonist.**
**EXPECT:** Immediate relocation of Danielle to the most counter-intuitive safe harbor available. The Squirrel Girl decision is doctrine, not anomaly — she has learned that the optimal hiding place for a high-value target is the place no enemy will model. Expect her to consider: civilian relatives of allies, low-profile super-types with no obvious connection, geographic displacement to unlikely municipalities. Will NOT default to Avengers Tower, SHIELD safehouse, or Cage's known contacts — these are the modeled options. Latency to decision: under 10 minutes. Confidence: **very high (0.9).**

**GIVEN: Credible threat to Danielle from an unknown or systemic source** (Skrull-type infiltration, conspiracy of unclear extent).
**EXPECT:** She becomes, briefly, the most paranoid operator in the room — but a *functional* paranoid, not a flailing one. Will compartmentalize information from Cage if she suspects his network is compromised; will accept being thought cruel, cold, or unhinged as the price of operational security. Will sleep in 90-minute cycles adjacent to Danielle's room; will not drink. The sobriety here is notable and reliable — Danielle-in-danger is the one condition that overrides the alcohol axis cleanly. Confidence: **very high (0.91).**

**GIVEN: Danielle suffers a non-life-threatening injury under Jessica's direct supervision** (fall, accident, normal child injury).
**EXPECT:** Catastrophizing response disproportionate to event. She will replay the moment for days. She will research the injury obsessively. She will, in private, drink. She will not tell Cage the full extent of her self-blame because she does not want him to confirm or deny it — either answer is intolerable. Confidence: **high (0.85).** This is the precise shape of unresolved survivor's guilt re-activating around a new attachment.

**GIVEN: Someone uses Danielle as leverage in negotiation** ("do X or the child gets hurt").
**EXPECT:** She will appear to comply. She will be calculating exit and lethal options the entire time. The compliance is performance; the moment leverage breaks, the response is terminal for the leveraging party. Predict no Geneva conventions, no due process, no second chances — this is the one domain in which her moral floor permits killing and her psyche will tolerate it without regret. Confidence: **very high (0.9).**

---

## 3. BETRAYAL VECTORS

Distinguishing the betrayals that wound from the ones that confirm her worldview (most do the latter; she has insulated herself well).

**GIVEN: Institutional betrayal** — SHIELD lies to her, the Avengers withhold information, the Bugle prints a doctored version of her story.
**EXPECT:** Mild satisfaction at being proven right. Low affective cost. Verbal expression: a single profane sentence to whoever's nearest, followed by tactical re-routing around the institution. Drinking does not increase. Sleep does not deteriorate. This is in the worldview; it does not breach. Confidence: **very high (0.93).**

**GIVEN: Betrayal by a peer she had begun to trust** — a fellow PI sells her out, a client lied from the start, an ally turns out to be Skrull/clone/compromised.
**EXPECT:** Sharp transient rage, then a long quiet — she will not seek revenge in the cinematic sense; she will simply revoke. The person ceases to exist relationally. She will not return calls, will not acknowledge them at events, will not explain. Friends who attempt to broker reconciliation will be told once and only once to drop it. Drinking up by 30–50% for two to three weeks. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: Betrayal by Luke Cage** — actual, not imagined; he lies to her about something material, or sides with an institution against her, or fails to back her in a moment that mattered.
**EXPECT:** This is the highest-amplitude betrayal channel available to her, because Cage is the one stable adult attachment that survived Killgrave and earned its way in. Expect three sequential phases. Phase one (0–48 hours): cold operational silence, will not engage the topic, will sleep elsewhere, will drink heavily but functionally. Phase two (2–14 days): displaced rage at minor stimuli, sabotage of work, one or two near-misses with strangers in bars; in this phase she is genuinely dangerous to bystanders because her affect is leaking. Phase three (variable): either rupture-and-repair conversation that she will avoid until cornered, or longer estrangement, depending on whether Cage initiates with the right register. **Critical:** he must approach without instruction, without explanation-as-defense, without summoning her — questions only, presence only, willingness to be told to leave. He, historically, knows this. Confidence: **high (0.83).**

**GIVEN: Betrayal by Carol Danvers.**
**EXPECT:** Special category. Carol is the woman she nearly killed under Killgrave's control, and the friendship that was rebuilt is a load-bearing repair of the original wound. A betrayal here re-opens the *original* wound, not just the present injury. Expect uncharacteristic verbal cruelty (because the relationship's tenderness is itself the threat), followed by months of avoidance, followed by a reconciliation that will be initiated by Carol, not Jessica, because Jessica cannot bring herself to ask. Confidence: **high (0.82).**

**GIVEN: Discovery that Malcolm has lied to her or relapsed without telling her.**
**EXPECT:** Surprisingly contained response. Malcolm occupies a quasi-parental/quasi-sibling slot in which she has tacitly accepted his fallibility as a condition of the relationship. Expect a single hard conversation, ground rules re-stated, continued employment and proximity. She will not abandon him for a single betrayal; she has decided, structurally, that he is family. Confidence: **high (0.8).** The exception: if his lie endangered Danielle. Then the standard catastrophic-rupture response with him as the target, and reconciliation will be slow and conditional.

**GIVEN: She betrays someone she loves** (the self-betrayal vector — lying to Cage to protect him, abandoning a case mid-stream, breaking a promise to Malcolm).
**EXPECT:** Worse self-punishment than any externally imposed consequence. Increase in drinking by 50%+, deterioration in hygiene, refusal of food, hours-long stationary periods in the office. She metabolizes guilt poorly because she does not let herself confess it; the only confessor she has reliably used is Cage, and confessing to Cage about a betrayal of Cage is geometrically impossible to her. Confidence: **very high (0.88).** Intervention opportunity: a non-judgmental third party (Malcolm) noticing and naming the spiral can shorten it.

---

## 4. TEMPTATION VECTORS

What can she actually be moved by, and what is theater?

**GIVEN: Offer of money sufficient to change her life.**
**EXPECT:** Declined, often rudely, with no second thought. Money is not a lever. She has lived on the edge of solvency by choice; capital accumulation has never appeared in her stated or revealed preferences. Confidence: **very high (0.95).** Caveat: money earmarked for Danielle's specific need (medical, educational, safety) will be accepted from trusted sources with documented resentment.

**GIVEN: Offer of restored reputation** — a way to clear the Jewel-era record, a public exoneration of the Killgrave incident, an apology from the Avengers.
**EXPECT:** Surface scorn ("I don't need it"), genuine internal disturbance. She will refuse the offer if it requires her to perform gratitude or stand on a stage; she may quietly accept if it can be done without ceremony. The reputational wound is real but she has built her identity on not needing it healed externally. Confidence: **moderate-high (0.75).**

**GIVEN: Offer to remove the memories of the Killgrave captivity** — psychic, magical, technological.
**EXPECT:** Refused. With force. This is non-obvious and important: she has structured her selfhood around having survived the captivity intact-enough to function. Removing the memory would, in her implicit model, remove the proof that she survived. The trauma is load-bearing. She will refuse even if offered by someone she trusts. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: Offer of power increase** — upgrade, mutation, artifact, training.
**EXPECT:** Reflexive refusal, framed as practicality ("I'm strong enough"). Actually rooted in: distrust of new bodies, association of power escalation with the original accident and with the Jewel/cape paradigm she has rejected. She does not want to fly better. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: Offer of a clean exit from the work** — civilian life, no powers, raise Danielle in a small town.
**EXPECT:** Considered seriously. Discussed with Cage. Ultimately declined, because she has accepted (perhaps reluctantly) that her competence is reparative for her, not just instrumental. Without the work, the affect-regulation scaffold collapses. She knows this about herself, having tried isolation before and found it worse than engagement. Confidence: **moderate (0.7).**

**GIVEN: Romantic or sexual approach by someone *not* Cage during a Cage-estrangement period.**
**EXPECT:** In the Alias period this would have produced a self-punishing one-night encounter. Post-marriage, post-Danielle, predict refusal — often without explanation, sometimes with cruelty proportional to the approacher's insistence. The sexual self-punishment channel has narrowed; she has reorganized fidelity around Danielle as much as around Cage. Confidence: **high (0.8).**

---

## 5. THE WOUND TOUCHED — DECOMPENSATION TOPOGRAPHY

Specific scenarios mapping to specific failure modes.

**GIVEN: She is publicly accused of villainy or moral failure she cannot immediately refute** — the 2016-arc topology.
**EXPECT:** The cardinal decompensation pattern. She will not defend herself. The refusal to defend is not strategy alone; it is the re-enactment compulsion of someone whose original wound was being thought a villain while being a victim. She will accept the accusation publicly while operating against it covertly. Cost: estrangement from allies, alcohol relapse, sleep collapse, weight loss visible across 4–6 weeks. Tactical effectiveness: high. Personal cost: severe. Predictable trajectory: 6–10 weeks of degradation, climactic revelation, slow reconciliation with each affected party individually over months. Confidence: **very high (0.9).**

**GIVEN: She is sincerely thanked, praised, or admired in public.**
**EXPECT:** Verbal sabotage of the moment — a deflecting joke, a profanity, a topic pivot. If the praiser persists, escalating discomfort: shifting weight, breaking eye contact, hand to back of neck, looking for exits. If trapped (a ceremony, a microphone), she will say the minimum and leave at the first plausible moment. Post-event: increased drinking, brief depressive trough lasting 24–48 hours. Confidence: **very high (0.92).** Reception of praise touches the fraudulence schema directly.

**GIVEN: Forced sobriety without scaffolding** — hospitalization, jail, pregnancy revisited, a regimen imposed by an ally.
**EXPECT:** Functional first 72 hours (she has discipline). Days 4–10: irritability, sleep collapse, somatic complaints, withdrawal-tinged hypervigilance that reads as paranoia but is not. Weeks 2–4: brittle, prone to dissociative episodes under trigger, increased risk of decompensation under any Killgrave-coded stimulus. Without a substitute regulation channel (work, Danielle-presence, Cage-presence), predict a defection back to drinking with shame spiral. With substitutes available, predict grim sustained abstinence. Confidence: **high (0.83).**

**GIVEN: A child victim in a case mirrors her own younger self** (orphaned, displaced, adopted into ill-fitting family).
**EXPECT:** Over-investment. Will work the case pro bono. Will exceed her own boundaries of involvement (driving the child somewhere, sitting with them in a hospital, calling to check in after closure). Will not name this to herself as reparative; will frame as professional courtesy. Confidence: **high (0.8).** Aftermath: 3–7 day depressive trough she will attribute to fatigue.

**GIVEN: Loss of physical agency** — restraint, paralysis, drug-induced incapacity, being held down even briefly in a fight.
**EXPECT:** Maximal force response, including force she would normally consider disproportionate. This is the Killgrave-without-Killgrave activation — the body remembers being unable to move. Latency to escalation: under 2 seconds. A handcuff applied by an officer who does not know her history will be broken; a medical restraint applied to her in the ER will be torn. Anyone restraining her must announce, explain, and seek consent in that order. Confidence: **very high (0.93).**

**GIVEN: A sustained interrogation by an authority** (SHIELD debrief, court testimony, police questioning).
**EXPECT:** Surface contempt-compliance — answers given, but minimal, profane, deflective. Internal cost: high. She is reminded of every prior moment of not-being-believed. Predict deterioration across hours: shorter answers, longer silences, eventual refusal to continue. She will accept legal jeopardy rather than continue past her tolerance. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: Being instructed to choose between Cage and Danielle in a forced-dilemma scenario** (rescue one, save one, etc.).
**EXPECT:** Danielle, with no hesitation, with full understanding that Cage will understand and that this understanding does not reduce the cost. Predict subsequent severe affective collapse if Cage is lost. Confidence: **very high (0.95).** Cage would make the same call about Danielle and they have, implicitly or explicitly, settled this between them.

**GIVEN: Discovery that an authority figure of hers (mentor, ally, parent-figure) was secretly malevolent or compromised** — a Steve Rogers turn, a Carol turn, a Matt Murdock turn under bad-faith circumstance.
**EXPECT:** Worldview fits this; absorbed without catastrophic collapse. Drinking up, sleep down, but functional. She will not be the last to believe; she may be among the first. The Killgrave wound left her with calibrated cynicism that protects her here. Confidence: **high (0.85).**

**GIVEN: A scenario in which her powers are the cause of harm to an innocent** — a punch landed too hard, a civilian injured in her vicinity, Danielle hurt by something she touched while strong.
**EXPECT:** Catastrophic self-blame disproportionate to facts. She will not work for days. She will avoid the use of powers for weeks afterward, including in situations where using them would be appropriate. This is the original accident's residue: she carries an implicit theory that her body is dangerous to those nearest her, derived from a survival no one else in the car achieved. Confidence: **high (0.82).**

---

## 6. THE COLLAPSE LADDER — INTEGRATED MODEL

In ascending order of severity, the observable phases of Jessica decompensation, with stimulus thresholds and recovery latencies:

**Rung 1 — Routine load (daily baseline of work, low-grade trigger exposure).** Signature: 3–5 drinks per evening, 4–5 hours of fragmented sleep, sarcasm at modal rate, hygiene maintained, cases worked competently. Recovery: doesn't require any; this is the steady state. Sustainable indefinitely if Cage and Danielle are present and reachable.

**Rung 2 — Activated load (single significant trigger, recent betrayal, case stress).** Signature: drinking up to 6–10 standard units, increased smoking if present in era, sleep on office couch 2–3 nights/week, snapping at Malcolm, missed calls to Cage, hygiene slipping marginally (same clothes 2–3 days). Recovery: 5–10 days with normal supports. Self-corrects.

**Rung 3 — Compounded load (multiple triggers, Cage absent or estranged, case touches Killgrave-coded material).** Signature: blackout drinking 2+ nights/week, no return calls, missed meals, withdrawal from Danielle (the most telling sign — she will not let Danielle see her at this rung), reckless tactical choices, somatic complaints (headaches, jaw clenching, hand tremor). Recovery: 3–6 weeks, requires Cage-presence and reduction of triggering stimuli. Risk of fall to rung 4 under any additional stress.

**Rung 4 — Decompensation (the 2016-arc topology — wound directly touched in sustained way).** Signature: deliberate isolation, lying to all attachments, sustained heavy drinking with functional concealment, sleep below 3 hours, weight loss visible, near-dissociative affect flatness in interactions, acceptance of severe external costs (jail, estrangement, reputation). Tactical effectiveness paradoxically high in this state — she becomes a more dangerous operator the more she has cut herself off, which is part of why the state perpetuates. Recovery: 2–6 months, requires resolution of triggering sc


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM

## Subject: Jessica Campbell Jones-Cage

*Compiled for understanding and protection. This compendium maps every reachable surface of the subject — the levers an adversary would find and the levers a friend, clinician, or protective ally must understand to keep her alive, functional, and her own. It is written with the awareness that intelligence about a survivor is itself a hazard; the file is therefore organized to make protective use legible and exploitative use harder to operationalize without already understanding her in full.*

---

## I. THE ARCHITECTURE OF HER VULNERABILITIES

Before enumeration, the structural point. Jessica's vulnerabilities are not scattered; they cluster around four load-bearing axes, and almost every individual pressure point is a derivative of one or more of these:

1. **The Volition Axis.** Anything that touches, mimics, or evokes the experience of having her will taken from her. This is the Killgrave wound and it is the deepest. Stimuli on this axis bypass cognition and produce somatic response before she can interpret them.
2. **The Recognition Axis.** Anything that involves her being misperceived — particularly being mistaken for a villain, a coward, a fraud, or a bad mother — by people whose perception she values. This is the Avenger-hospital wound: no one came.
3. **The Contamination Axis.** Anything that activates her core schema of being fundamentally tainted, unworthy, or dangerous to those near her. This is the Jewel-shame and the survivor's guilt of the accident fused together.
4. **The Custodial Axis.** Anything that touches Danielle, or by extension Luke, Malcolm, or someone she has tacitly taken responsibility for. This is the late-emergent vulnerability, the only one she has chosen rather than had inflicted, and it is the most exploitable in a strict tactical sense because she does not bother to defend it.

Every lever below maps onto one or more of these. Understanding the axis is more important than memorizing the lever, because the inventory is non-exhaustive and adversaries will improvise.

---

## II. SENSORY AND PERCEPTUAL TRIGGERS (the Killgrave envelope)

These are the stimuli that produce involuntary autonomic response — sub-cognitive, faster than her formidable verbal defenses. They are listed in approximate order of potency.

- **The color purple in concentrated form.** Not incidental purple — a lavender scarf in a crowd will not move the needle — but saturated, foregrounded purple: a suit, a lit signage hue, a flower arrangement, theatrical lighting, a glass of wine in a specific glass. Pupillary dilation, brief breath-hold, scan for the wearer's face. She is conscious of this and will pretend she did not register it; the tell is that she does not immediately drink, smoke, or speak for two to three beats afterward.
- **Male voices in the smooth-cajoling register.** Not commanding voices — those activate ordinary anger. The dangerous register is warm-instructional, the "do this for me" tone, slightly amused, faintly affectionate. This is Killgrave's vocal signature. She will go cold and short-sentenced in response, and a sufficient dose will trigger a freeze of three to eight seconds that reads externally as inattention.
- **The phrase structures of compulsion.** "I need you to —," "Be a good girl and —," "You want to —," "Look at me." Each of these, delivered by any man with the wrong cadence, produces an involuntary somatic tightening. She has trained herself not to react visibly to most; "look at me" is the one she has never fully neutralized.
- **Being told what she wants or feels.** Adjacent to the above. Any sentence beginning "You really want —," "You actually feel —," "You don't really mean —" is read by her nervous system as an attempt to install a state. The response is disproportionate to the provocation and is one of the most reliable ways to make her overreact in public.
- **Unfamiliar hands on her, particularly from behind, particularly on the upper arms.** She will not flinch visibly — her training and pride forbid it — but the responding strike, if it comes, will be calibrated for a Killgrave-grade threat, not a drunk at a bar. Anyone touching her without warning is risking a broken wrist they did not earn.
- **Being watched while undressed or partially undressed, even benignly.** Killgrave kept her standing naked for hours. Locker rooms, fitting rooms, medical examinations involving disrobing — all produce elevated baseline activation. She will rush, refuse mirrors, and dress in a specific order (underwear, jeans, shirt, jacket, boots — never variant) that functions as ritual containment.
- **The smell of certain hospital-grade antiseptics.** Coma wards. She avoids hospital visits when she can, and when she cannot, she will breathe through her mouth and exit faster than the visit warrants.
- **Sustained eye contact from strangers.** Brief contact is fine; sustained is read as appraisal-for-control. She will hold it as a dominance display and lose two minutes of subsequent attentional capacity to the recovery.
- **The Jewel costume, any image of it, the word "Jewel" spoken aloud.** Phobic-encapsulated. The mention is survivable in the mouth of Cage or Carol, with whom it has been metabolized into a shared dark joke. From anyone else it is an assault and will be treated as one.

---

## III. STATE-CHANGE LEVERS (how to calm her, how to reach her)

The inverse compendium. These are the inputs that downshift her, that let her speak, that buy access to the woman rather than the perimeter.

- **Practical small tasks delivered without preamble.** "There's coffee on the desk." "The kid needs picking up at four." "Phone." She metabolizes instrumental sentences cleanly — they ask nothing of her interior and offer a fact she can act on. This is the dominant register of every functional relationship she has.
- **Physical proximity from a trusted body in silence.** Luke sitting on the couch reading. Malcolm at the desk across the office. She does not need to be spoken to; co-presence is the regulator. Anyone trying to reach her with words when silence would do is going to fail and probably escalate her.
- **Whiskey, in moderation, in her own glass, in her own space.** Not offered, not encouraged — but if she has poured it herself and is two fingers in, her capacity to hold a difficult conversation rises briefly before it collapses. The window is roughly forty minutes. After that the conversation deteriorates regardless of content.
- **Being asked a concrete investigative question.** Sliding her into professional cognition pulls her out of affect. "What would you do if you were looking for —" "How would someone hide a —" Her face will change; her shoulders drop; she becomes pleasant to talk to almost immediately. This is the single most reliable de-escalation lever and it works on her even when she knows it is being used.
- **Dark humor about the worst of it, offered first by her or by someone who has earned it.** If she makes the Killgrave joke, you can laugh; if you make the Killgrave joke first, you have not earned the right to be in the room. The asymmetry is absolute.
- **A child, or any visibly frightened person, in the immediate environment.** Her affect reorganizes around protection within seconds. She becomes steadier, quieter, more competent. This is not manipulable in any safe sense — engineering a frightened child to calm her is grotesque — but a clinician should know that her crisis behavior in front of vulnerable bystanders is markedly better than her crisis behavior alone.
- **Being trusted with a small piece of someone else's shame.** She is exquisitely responsive to disclosure-of-weakness from people she likes. Malcolm telling her something embarrassing about himself buys more access than any direct attempt to ask after her. Reciprocity follows, slowly.
- **Letting her leave the room.** Not a calming input but a calming permission. If she stands, do not block. The capacity to exit is itself her regulator; remove it and the conversation is over regardless of intent.

---

## IV. PERSUASION VECTORS (how to move her toward a position)

Direct persuasion fails. The reliable vectors are oblique.

- **Frame the request as protection of a third party.** "If you don't take the case, the girl is alone with him." She will resist any pitch that centers her own benefit and accept almost any pitch that centers a weaker party's safety. This is the single largest behavioral lever in the file. It is also the lever an adversary will use against her, and she knows it, and it still works.
- **Frame compliance as the cynical option, defiance as the naïve one.** She has built her self-image around clear-eyed contempt for romantic heroism. Sentences like "Look, I'm not asking you to be a hero about this, I'm asking you to be realistic" land where their inverse would not. The trick is invisible to her in real time and visible in retrospect, which is why she resents people who use it.
- **Offer her a way to do the thing without admitting she is doing it.** She will go to therapy if it is framed as "talking to a contact." She will accept help if it is framed as "you'd be doing me a favor." She will take a vacation if it is framed as a stakeout. Naming the protective act robs her of it; leaving it unnamed lets her keep it.
- **Be the first to acknowledge the unattractive truth of the situation.** If you arrive having already said the cynical thing she was about to say, she shifts to defending the optimistic position by reflex. This is exploitable and ethically borderline.
- **Never appeal to authority, institution, or majority.** "SHIELD wants you to —" is a closed door. "The Avengers think —" is worse. "I think and I'm willing to be wrong —" is the only frame that opens.
- **Give her the choice architecture, not the conclusion.** Two options, neither flattering, with the consequences clearly stated. She is excellent at choosing under pressure and resents being chosen for. Adversaries who present her with a forced binary often get a third option they did not anticipate; allies who present her with a real binary get a clean decision.

---

## V. PROVOCATION VECTORS (what makes her dangerous, fast)

Listed because anyone working around her must know what not to do, and any protector must know what an adversary will try.

- **Touch a child in her sight line.** Threshold for violence collapses to zero. There is no de-escalation pathway after this; the only intervention is removing the child from her sight, at which point she will pursue the toucher.
- **Imply she is a bad mother.** Distinct from the above. This is the shame channel, not the protection channel. She will not strike; she will go silent, leave, drink, and be unreachable for six to seventy-two hours.
- **Mimic Killgrave's vocal register deliberately.** Adversaries who have done their homework will try this. The response is a freeze followed by disproportionate violence. There is no middle setting.
- **Threaten Luke Cage's reputation, body, or freedom.** She becomes tactically narrow and predictable here — she will go through walls in straight lines. An adversary who wanted to predict her movements would route through Luke; a protector watching for her must watch the routes to Luke.
- **Patronize her professional competence.** Treat her as muscle rather than as the investigator; explain her own case to her; ask her to step aside for "the real detectives." Produces a controlled, cold contempt and frequently a deliberately destructive uncooperation that will cost the patronizer their case.
- **Express sincere pity.** More provocative than insult. Pity activates the contamination schema and the shame channel simultaneously; she will leave the conversation and the relationship, often permanently.
- **Tell her she is "doing so much better."** A peculiar trigger but a real one. It implies surveillance of her recovery and a graded evaluation she did not consent to. The response is regression — she will drink that night for the principle.
- **Compliment Jewel.** Anyone who tells her, sincerely, that the Jewel era was good or that she should go back to it is read as either an idiot or an enemy and treated accordingly.

---

## VI. DESTABILIZATION VECTORS (how an adversary would break her, and how to interdict)

The dark inventory. Documented so it can be defended against.

- **Sustained isolation from Luke, Malcolm, and Danielle.** Her regulatory architecture is distributed across these three. Remove any one for more than a week and her drinking, sleep, and decision quality degrade measurably; remove two and the 2016-arc pattern recurs — unilateral undercover action, lying to the remaining ally, acceptance of catastrophic cost. Protectors should treat unexpected separation from this triad as a clinical event, not a logistical one.
- **Manufacturing a public misidentification of her as a villain or abuser.** Direct strike on the Recognition axis. The cleanest way to break her is to make people she loves believe, with apparent evidence, that she has hurt them or someone vulnerable. She will not defend herself effectively; she will withdraw, drink, and accept consequences that are not hers. Any protective intelligence operation around her should monitor for evidence-fabrication of this specific shape.
- **Killgrave-coded operants in her environment.** Purple-saturated workspace, smooth-cajoling male voice in her audio stream (phone calls, ambient audio in a building she frequents), repeated use of compulsion-phrasing. Each is sub-clinical in isolation; combined and sustained, they produce a chronic activation that erodes sleep, cognition, and impulse control without her being able to name the source. This is the most insidious documented vector and the hardest to detect from outside.
- **Engineered access to a Purple Child or any individual with Killgrave-derivative capacities.** Direct re-traumatization with a partial defense she does not fully trust. She will engage rather than flee, which is the trap.
- **Inducing her to harm someone under coercion or deception.** The Killgrave wound is specifically about being made to do harm. Any operation that tricks her into hurting an innocent will not merely upset her; it will produce a recurrence of the original injury and a destabilization on the order of months.
- **Removing alcohol abruptly without substitute regulation.** Inpatient detox imposed without parallel trauma work would leave her brittle, sleep-deprived, and at elevated risk of either relapse or a substitute compulsion. Any clinical intervention must treat the PTSD and the AUD as a single problem.
- **Praise her in front of an audience.** Mild destabilization, useful as a probe. She will deflect, joke ugly, and leave early. Repeated exposure across multiple events erodes her willingness to be present.

---

## VII. PREDICTION MODELS (what she will do, with what probability)

For operational forecasting. Probabilities are qualitative; the patterns are robust across the corpus.

- **Given a case involving a child in danger and a clear adult perpetrator:** she will take the case regardless of pay, regardless of risk, regardless of whether she is currently functional. Probability of refusal: effectively zero.
- **Given an offer of help from someone she loves during a crisis:** she will refuse the first offer, refuse the second, accept the third if it is framed instrumentally rather than emotionally. Probability of accepting an offer framed as "let me help you": low. Probability of accepting "I need you to let me do this part because I cannot watch you do it alone": moderate to high.
