- **Given a threat to Danielle:** she will hand the child to the most capable available protector — not necessarily the most emotionally appropriate one — and pursue the threat herself. The Squirrel Girl decision is the template: optimal tactical selection that reads as absurd. Predict her custodial choices by capacity, not by intimacy.
- **Given a demand from institutional authority:** she will comply minimally and visibly while undermining the frame. She does not run; she does not refuse; she degrades cooperation just enough to remain technically compliant.
- **Given recognition that she has been deceived by an intimate:** she will not confront immediately. She will gather evidence, drink through the gathering, and confront at a time of her choosing with full documentation. The interval is typically three to nine days. The confrontation, when it comes, is terminal to the relationship unless the deceiver was Luke, in whose case she will eventually re-engage after a punitive distance of weeks to months.
- **Given a sustained period of stability:** she will sabotage it within six to ten weeks. Not catastrophically — a missed appointment, a drink too many, a fight picked with Carol. The mechanism is contamination-schema activation by the stability itself: she does not believe she gets to keep good things, and proves the belief.
- **Given a Killgrave re-emergence:** she will isolate, prepare alone, refuse help, and confront. She has done this twice. She will do it again. Allies should plan for the isolation, not against it; the isolation is non-negotiable, and presence has to be smuggled in (Malcolm at the office "working on something else"; Luke "happening to be in the neighborhood").

---

## VIII. ALLY-SPECIFIC LEVERAGE GRAPH

Each of the people who can reach her can also be used against her. The asymmetric access of each, documented.

- **Luke Cage.** Can speak truths no one else can survive saying. Can be in physical proximity through her worst affect without escalating her. His leverage on her is total and he uses it almost never, which is why it remains intact. Adversarial leverage on her *through* Luke is the highest-magnitude vector in the file: threats to his body, freedom, or reputation collapse her tactical sophistication. Protective implication: Luke's security is her security.
- **Danielle.** Pure custodial lever. Not communicative, but the orientation of her entire stress response. Adversarial implication is obvious; protective implication is that Danielle's environment must be hardened independently and never used as a leverage point even by well-meaning institutions (custody threats from family services, for instance, would produce a response disproportionate to the bureaucratic provocation).
- **Malcolm Ducasse.** The daily-operational ally. Has more granular real-time access to her functional state than anyone, including Luke. Can interrupt her drinking, redirect her workload, force food into her without triggering refusal. His leverage is built on consistency — predictable presence, predictable competence, no surprises. An adversary who removed or compromised Malcolm would degrade her baseline within days; protectors should treat Malcolm's wellbeing as part of her clinical picture.
- **Carol Danvers.** Carries the unique weight of the original Avenger-hospital wound and its eventual partial repair. Can therefore both wound her more deeply than almost anyone and reach her in registers no one else can. The friendship oscillates; when functional, Carol is the only person from whom Jessica will accept unsolicited direct advice. When fractured (as in the 2016 arc), the fracture is itself destabilizing. Protective implication: the Jessica-Carol relationship is load-bearing infrastructure and should be supported as such.
- **Matt Murdock.** Episodic. Speaks her dialect (Catholic-shame-cousin to her trauma-shame), can be trusted for legal work, cannot be trusted for sustained emotional access because his own pathology resonates with hers in destructive ways. Useful in tactical isolation, hazardous in prolonged proximity.
- **J. Jonah Jameson.** A documented antagonist who has nonetheless been useful to her; she will work for him because he is honest about being a bastard. Predictable, therefore safe in a narrow sense. Cannot reach her emotionally; can move her professionally through cash and assignment.
- **Killgrave (in memoriam or in any recurrence).** The negative pole. The presence around which her psychological compass orients. Any operation involving him is, by definition, on the Volition axis and must be planned with the assumption that her tactical autonomy will be partially compromised regardless of preparation.

---

## IX. TEMPORAL AND CIRCADIAN VULNERABILITY MAP

Trauma is time-shaped. Hers has a schedule.

- **3 a.m. to 5 a.m.** Peak intrusion window. If she is not asleep — and she often is not — she is drinking, working a case file, or staring. Reachable by text from a trusted contact; unreachable by phone call (a ringing phone at this hour is read as catastrophe-coded and she will brace for bad news before answering).
- **Sunday afternoons.** Disproportionately bad. Unstructured time activates the rumination loop. She has, across the corpus, repeatedly scheduled her worst decisions for Sunday afternoons. Protective scheduling fills this window with concrete obligation (Danielle, a standing dinner, a low-stakes case interview).
- **Anniversaries.** The accident; the approximate window of the Killgrave capture's beginning and end; the Avenger-hospital incident. She does not mark these consciously and will deny they affect her; her drinking and sleep data tell the opposite story. A vigilant ally tracks them silently.
- **Holidays with intact-family imagery.** Thanksgiving and Christmas are baseline-elevated. She compensates by making them aggressively casual or by working through them.
- **Postpartum and breastfeeding-cessation windows around Danielle.** Hormonal load on a PTSD baseline produced documented destabilization that has not been fully metabolized. Any future pregnancy, any analogous endocrine event, should be treated as a high-risk window clinically.
- **The hour after a successful case closes.** Counter-intuitively a vulnerable window. Completion removes the structural scaffold and exposes the affect underneath. She drinks more on closing nights than on stakeout nights.

---

## X. THE PROTECTIVE FRAME

A compendium of vulnerabilities is a hazard if it is read flat. The summary judgment that should accompany it:

She is not fragile. She is **load-bearing under conditions that would have broken almost anyone else,** and the vulnerabilities documented here are the visible seams of a structure that has held. The volition wound, the recognition wound, the contamination schema, the custodial commitment — these are the places where she can be reached because they are the places where she is still alive. A surveillance file written without this understanding would catalog her as exploitable; the correct reading is that she is exploitable in exactly the ways that a person who has refused to become invulnerable necessarily is.

Protective doctrine therefore reduces to four operational rules:

1. **Defend the triad.** Luke, Malcolm, Danielle. Their security is her security. Treat threats to them as threats to her.
2. **Monitor the Killgrave envelope.** Sensory operants in her environment are the most insidious adversarial vector. Audit her surroundings the way a counter-surveillance team audits a room.
3. **Smuggle care in instrumental wrapping.** Never name the protective act. The naming is the failure.
4. **Trust her tactical judgment, including her isolations.** She has survived everything she has survived by making decisions that looked wrong from outside. The protective ally is the one who can stand the distance she requires and still be there when she returns to the room.

*End VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM. Cross-reference: §3 Psychological, §4 Psychiatric, §5 Personality. Recommended next section: Operational Protocols & Contact Doctrine.*


## Strengths, Assets & Resilience

# STRENGTHS, ASSETS & RESILIENCE
## UATU Dossier Section 6 — Subject: Jessica Campbell Jones

A full-spectrum surveillance dossier serves understanding only if the asset ledger is as granular as the liability ledger. The temptation with this subject — given the volume of trauma, the alcohol pattern, the visible shame architecture — is to read her as a damaged operator who functions in spite of herself. That reading is wrong, or at least catastrophically incomplete. She is functional *because of* a specific, identifiable, durable asset stack that has survived stressors which would have decompensated almost any comparable subject in the file index. This section maps that stack exhaustively.

---

### 6.1 Somatic & Physical Assets

**Class 50+ enhanced strength, lower-ceiling but combat-credible.** Her power floor is high enough that virtually no street-level threat can physically coerce her; her power ceiling is low enough (sub-Cage, well sub-Sentry) that she has never developed the casual destructiveness of subjects who can level structures incidentally. The result is a calibrated body: she has lived inside her strength long enough to modulate it on a child's bath, a doorknob, a coffee mug, a punch to a human jaw. Surveillance of her domestic micro-behavior (handling Danielle, lifting groceries, closing the office door) shows no sign of the over-correction tremor seen in newer enhanced subjects. The body is integrated.

**Durability sufficient for survival, insufficient for invulnerability complacency.** She has been hospitalized, comatose twice, beaten near-fatally. She knows, somatically and not just intellectually, that she can be hurt. This is an asset: it preserves tactical caution. Subjects with full invulnerability tend toward strategic laziness; she does not.

**Flight, suppressed but available.** The flight capacity is real and is an emergency-grade asset she chooses not to use. Operationally relevant: in any scenario where vertical egress would save her or a dependent, the option exists. She has used it under maternal-protection conditions and will again.

**Sensory and reflex baseline at or near the upper end of normal-human, plus the trained reflexes of a working investigator.** She reads rooms quickly, registers exits, clocks weapons, identifies the drunkest and most dangerous person in a bar within seconds. This is not power-derived; it is hard-earned.

**Sleep deprivation tolerance.** She has functioned for years on irregular, fragmented sleep without catastrophic cognitive collapse. Not healthy, but operationally relevant: she does not become useless during multi-day high-tempo cases.

**Alcohol tolerance, paradoxically protective.** Her metabolic processing of alcohol — whether power-adjacent or simply built — is sufficient that she can ingest quantities that would incapacitate baseline humans and remain ambulatory, verbal, and tactically responsive. This is a liability framed as an asset only with caveat: it has prevented her from drinking herself into a fatal incident across years of heavy use that would have killed a smaller-tolerance subject.

---

### 6.2 Cognitive Assets

**High verbal intelligence, weaponized.** Her sentence-level construction under stress is rapid, precise, and tonally controlled. She can humiliate a hostile witness in three lines, defuse a panicking client in two, and end a conversation she doesn't want with a single sentence whose social cost she has pre-calculated. This is a working tool, not ornament.

**Pattern-matching at investigative tempo.** *Alias* case files demonstrate her capacity to triangulate a missing person from a credit-card receipt, a school-photo background, and a half-overheard phone call. She holds multiple working hypotheses without premature commitment — a rare cognitive discipline, especially under hangover load.

**Strong moral reasoning where she is not personally implicated.** When she is the subject, her cognition distorts toward shame and self-blame. When she is reasoning about *other* people's situations, her judgment is unusually clean — empathetic without being credulous, skeptical without being cynical. Clients receive better thinking than she gives herself.

**Functional metacognition.** She knows when she is drunk, knows when she is rationalizing, knows when she is about to do something stupid. She frequently does it anyway, but the awareness is intact. This is a significantly better baseline than the file index average for subjects with comparable trauma history.

**Absence of psychotic-spectrum cognition.** Despite eight months of having reality and her own will systematically falsified by an external agent, she emerged without lasting paranoid ideation, magical thinking, or grandiose compensation. The integrity of her reality-testing post-Killgrave is, frankly, the asset that most distinguishes her file. Most subjects do not come back from that with their epistemology intact.

**Tolerance of ambiguity and incomplete information.** She does not need the case to be solved to keep working it. She does not need a relationship to be defined to stay in it. She does not need her own feelings to be coherent to act morally within them. This is a high-grade trait.

---

### 6.3 Character & Moral Assets

**A moral floor that survived coercion.** This cannot be overstated. Killgrave's project was not merely to use her; it was to corrode the boundary between her will and his, to make her *want* what he wanted. She came out the other side with a stable set of values that she did not have to reconstruct from rubble — she had to clean them off, but they were intact underneath. Operationally: she will not, even drunk, even cornered, even offered enormous benefit, hurt the weaker party in the room. This is not a rule she follows; it is the spine her self is built around. It is the most reliable single predictor in her file.

**Reparative drive aimed outward.** Many trauma survivors turn the wound inward (self-harm) or outward as displaced aggression (predation on weaker targets). She has done the much rarer thing: she has turned it into vocational protection of others who occupy the position she once occupied. Every case she takes is, structurally, a small re-do of the Killgrave situation with her in the rescuer seat. This is sublimation at near-textbook quality.

**Shame as ethical signal, not paralysis.** Her shame is heavy and chronic but is not fully disabling: it reliably fires *in response to genuine ethical lapses* and does not fire (or fires less) in response to morally neutral acts. The calibration is functional. Many subjects in the file index have shame systems that misfire on neutral stimuli and stay quiet on actual transgression. Hers does the opposite.

**Capacity for guilt without collapse into it.** She feels guilt; she does not drown in it for so long that action becomes impossible. The recovery curve from a guilt-triggering event is faster than her self-presentation suggests.

**Honesty under specific conditions.** She lies operationally (undercover, to authority, to clients she's testing) but does not lie to the small set of people whose relationships she has decided matter — except in the specific pattern of protective deception (the 2016 arc), which she experiences as moral cost and does not repeat lightly. This is a stable, mappable honesty profile.

**Refusal to be flattered.** She is structurally immune to sincere praise as a manipulation vector because she cannot process it without discomfort. Hostile actors attempting to recruit her via ego-stroke have a zero hit rate in the corpus. This is a major counter-intelligence asset.

**No appetite for power.** She has been offered, at various points, Avengers membership, formal SHIELD positions, broader heroic profile. She has declined or accepted minimally. The absence of status-hunger insulates her from a large category of corruption pathways.

---

### 6.4 Relational & Social Assets

**Marriage to Luke Cage — high-integrity primary attachment.** Cage is the rarest possible match for her: a man whose own power-set and trauma-history make him both unintimidated by her and unable to coerce her. He cannot be mind-controlled in the ways she fears; he cannot be physically broken in the ways she fears for those she loves; he does not require emotional performance from her; and he has independently chosen, repeatedly, to stay. The marriage is not frictionless, but it is a stable platform on which she has built every late-period capacity she now possesses. He is, in operational terms, her single most important asset.

**Daughter Danielle — reorganizing attachment.** The child has done what years of self-work could not: forced her to operate, daily, in a register of presence, gentleness, and forward-looking responsibility. The maternal role has integrated parts of her that were dissociated. This is not romanticism; it is observable behavioral reorganization across the *New Avengers* and post-2016 corpus.

**Malcolm Ducasse — chosen-family / second-in-command.** A younger man she effectively rescued and who has grown into her partner at Alias. He provides: continuity of office operations during her absences, a daily relational anchor that doesn't carry the freight of the Cage marriage, and a check on her isolation tendency (he simply will not let her disappear without comment). His existence in her life converts Alias from a one-woman crash-out into a small functioning institution.

**Carol Danvers — peer-grade longitudinal friendship.** Pre-dating Jewel, surviving the Killgrave incident (eventually, after repair), and oscillating across decades. Carol is the only peer who knew her before the powers and after the wound, and who can speak to her without deference, fear, or pity. The friendship absorbs damage and repairs.

**Matt Murdock, Jessica Drew, Daredevil/Spider-Woman tier of professional allies.** A working bench of high-competence operators she can call. She does not call them often, which preserves the asset (they take her calls seriously precisely because she rarely makes them).

**The Avengers as standing-reserve resource.** She does not draw on this network for emotional support; she draws on it for tactical backstop when Danielle is at risk. This is an efficient use of an otherwise low-affinity relationship.

**Filtering function of her abrasive presentation.** Her prickliness is a sorting mechanism: people who cannot tolerate her surface do not get to her depths, which means the depths are populated only by people who have demonstrated, behaviorally, that they will stay. The relational network is small but selected for resilience.

**Comfort with solitude.** She does not require constant social contact to remain stable. This is rare in trauma survivors and is a major asset for the kind of long-stakeout, long-research, long-thinking work her vocation demands.

---

### 6.5 Vocational & Material Assets

**Alias Investigations — owned, operational, scalable to her energy.** A licensed PI practice, established reputation in the Hell's Kitchen / lower-Manhattan corridor, client pipeline that does not depend on advertising. The business absorbs her hyperarousal productively and provides identity scaffolding independent of any external institution. She can work alone, she can work with Malcolm, she can shutter for a week and reopen — the structure is hers.

**The office itself as somatic anchor.** A specific, known, defensible physical space — desk, couch, bottle, filing cabinet, door with her name on it. After a captivity that destroyed her sense of secure space, the existence of a room that is unambiguously hers, that she chose, that she pays for, that she can lock, is a continuous low-grade therapeutic intervention. Surveillance should note that she returns to the office under stress even when home would be more comfortable; the office is the regulating environment.

**Professional credentials and credibility across multiple subcultures.** She is taken seriously by: street-level vigilantes (Daredevil corridor), corporate-tier heroes (Avengers corridor), tabloid journalism (the Bugle period left her with sources), law enforcement (grudging), the superhuman-victim community (high credibility, a real and rare asset). Few operators are credible across all five.

**The Bugle period as residual asset.** Her tenure under Jameson left her with a working knowledge of how superhuman news is manufactured and a Rolodex of media contacts. She can plant a story, kill a story, or weaponize a story when needed.

**Financial baseline.** Not wealthy. Cash-flow on a working PI's margin, supplemented by Cage's income and (at various points) Avengers stipend. Sufficient to absent herself from work for protective-custody periods without immediate collapse. Material precarity is not a primary stressor in her life, which frees cognitive bandwidth for the stressors that are.

**Wardrobe and self-presentation as operational tool.** The jeans-leather-scarf uniform is not laziness; it is a deliberate aesthetic that reads as unthreatening-to-civilians, unimpressive-to-predators-who-then-underestimate-her, and uniform enough that she never has to think about it. Decision fatigue minimized. Identity signaled. The Jewel costume's absence is itself an asset — she has refused a visual identity that would constrain her.

---

### 6.6 Resilience Mechanisms (Process-Level)

**Sublimation pipeline.** Hyperarousal → investigative absorption → case closure → small reparative outcome → marginal self-worth increment. This loop runs reliably and has run for years. It is the central resilience mechanism in her file.

**Humor as pressure valve.** Even at the worst, the sardonic register stays online. This is not the mature humor of high-functioning subjects, but it functions as affect regulation: it discharges enough tension to prevent acute decompensation.

**Tolerance for her own ugliness.** She has integrated her drinking, her sexual history, her cowardices, her cruelties to people who tried to help her, into a coherent self-image. She does not have to defend against awareness of her flaws — she already sees them. This denies hostile actors a major manipulation vector and denies internal pathology a major fuel source.

**Capacity to receive help from a small whitelist.** Cage, Malcolm, Carol, occasionally Murdock — she can, slowly, accept help from these specific others. The whitelist is short but it exists, which puts her categorically above subjects with no whitelist at all.

**Slow but real updating.** She updates her models of people over years, not minutes — but she does update. Her relationship with Carol post-Killgrave-confession is the cardinal example: the repair took years, and held. The capacity for long-arc relational repair is a major resilience asset.

**Refusal of the victim identity as primary identity.** She acknowledges what was done to her; she does not organize her self-concept around it. The Killgrave wound is *a fact about her*, not *who she is*. This distinction is subtle and rare and is probably the single most important psychological asset in her stack.

**Maternal reorganization.** Becoming Danielle's mother forced the activation of behavioral patterns — gentleness, routine, forward-planning, body-care — that her trauma had suppressed. The asset is now self-sustaining: the child requires it daily, and daily provision strengthens it.

**The post-Killgrave psychic defense.** The Jean Grey / X-Men intervention installed a literal cognitive firewall against Killgrave-class compulsion. This is a concrete, mappable, exploitable asset: she is now harder to mind-control than virtually any baseline-human-grade subject in the file. Her hard-won mastery of her own affect during the *Alias* confrontation with Killgrave demonstrates that the defense is not merely passive — she has learned to deploy it.

---

### 6.7 Counter-Manipulation Profile

A surveillance file's asset section must include the subject's resistance signature — what makes her hard to turn, hard to break, hard to use.

- **Praise-immune.** Sincere flattery produces discomfort, not opening.
- **Bribe-resistant.** Material reward is not a primary motivator; she lives at a margin she has already accepted.
- **Status-immune.** Offers of rank, title, membership, recognition do not move her.
- **Shame-saturated.** Hostile actors cannot threaten her with exposure of her flaws because she has already exposed them, to herself and to her whitelist. There is little compromising material whose release she has not already absorbed.
- **Coercion-hardened.** Eight months with Killgrave is the upper bound of interpersonal coercion. Lesser actors trying lesser methods face a subject whose pain calibration is non-standard.
- **Predictable in exactly one register.** Threats to Danielle override everything. This is a vulnerability (covered elsewhere in file) but is also, paradoxically, an asset: it means she cannot be turned against her child by any other mechanism, because that one channel saturates everything else.
- **Slow to trust, slow to distrust.** Once a person is on the whitelist, removing them requires sustained behavioral evidence over time. She cannot be quickly poisoned against an ally by short-term disinformation.

---

### 6.8 Durability Assessment

The asset stack above is not fragile. It has been stress-tested by: an eight-month captivity, two comas, a near-fatal beating, the loss of her entire birth family, decades of heavy alcohol use, a global superhuman civil war, a Skrull infiltration that took her infant daughter, a self-imposed undercover operation that estranged her from her husband and her closest friend, and a culture that has, at various points, regarded her as a villain, a joke, a tabloid byline, and a footnote. The stack held.

Projected durability is high. The two assets most likely to compound over time — the Cage marriage and the maternal reorganization — are both still strengthening. The one asset most likely to erode — alcohol tolerance protecting her from the consequences of alcohol use — should be flagged as a long-horizon liability, but the trend across the corpus is reduction, not escalation.

**Bottom-line characterization for the file:** the subject is not a damaged person who functions. She is a functional person whose damage is one variable among many, and not the dominant one. The dominant variables are a stable moral spine, a vocational identity that absorbs her pathology productively, a small high-quality relational network, and a refusal — quiet, daily, unglamorous — to let what was done to her dictate what she does to others. That last variable is the asset the rest of the file should be read against.

*End Section 6. Continue to Section 7: Liabilities, Vulnerabilities & Threat Vectors.*


## Failure Modes & Decompensation

# FAILURE MODES & DECOMPENSATION

## Preliminary Framing

Jessica Jones does not fail loudly in the way the public imagination associates with "superhero breakdown" — there is no Stark-style press-conference humiliation, no Stark-style bender-in-the-armor. Her failures are smaller in surface area and larger in interior cost. They look, from outside, like the ordinary collapses of an ordinary woman: a missed call, a slammed door, a third drink before noon, a lie to a husband, a client file left open on the desk for nine days. The file's task in this section is to render those small surface events legible as the late-stage symptoms of a specific, repeatable decompensation architecture — an architecture built from C-PTSD physiology, alcohol-mediated affect regulation, fearful-avoidant attachment, and a residual fear of having her will overwritten.

What follows maps that architecture across five domains: (1) the baseline operating envelope; (2) the staged escalation curve; (3) full-collapse presentations; (4) the specific triggers that produce each; (5) the recovery topology, including how she comes back online and the residue she carries forward.

---

## 1. Baseline and the Envelope of Function

Jessica's "well" baseline is not most people's well. It is a chronically elevated arousal floor — resting irritability, sleep that begins around 2–3 a.m. and ends at 9–10 a.m. with a hangover, two-to-four drinks a day at the low end, an apartment-office whose tidiness is inversely correlated with her stability, and a conversational style that runs 30–40% profanity even in calm registers. This is her *good week.* It is essential to grasp this, because every escalation marker described below is a deviation from a baseline that is itself already compensated trauma physiology. There is no resting state of true ease for the subject. The envelope of function is narrow and the walls are load-bearing.

Within that envelope she is highly competent. The Alias casework, the Pulse reporting, the New Avengers tactical contributions, the late-period investigative work — all of it gets done, often well, often under conditions that would unstring an unmedicated civilian with her symptom load. The functioning is real. It is also expensive, and the cost is paid in liver, sleep, and the people who try to live with her.

---

## 2. The Escalation Curve

Her decompensation is **staged and predictable**, which is itself an intelligence asset: anyone close to her long enough (Cage, Malcolm, eventually Carol again) can read the stage in real time. The stages are not crisp — they bleed — but they recur in sequence.

### Stage 0 — Subclinical loading
The earliest tell is **work intake.** She takes a case she would normally refuse, or refuses one she would normally take, on grounds that don't quite scan. The criterion that's wobbling is her usual filter: *is this case adjacent to my wound?* When that filter inverts (she accepts a case *because* it's adjacent, not in spite of it), she is already loading. Concurrent micro-tells: a longer pause before answering the phone; reading mail standing up at the door without sitting; the office bourbon bottle moved from desk-drawer to desktop.

### Stage 1 — Irritability and perimeter contraction
Sarcasm sharpens from dry to cutting. The percentage of conversations she ends rather than concludes rises. She stops returning Malcolm's "you good?" texts within their usual two-hour window; the gap stretches to a day, then two. Cage notices she's eating less and drinking earlier — the first drink moves from after-work to lunch to with-coffee. She becomes *visibly* present-but-elsewhere — sitting in the same room with Cage and Danielle but with her phone face-down on her thigh, eyes tracking middle distance. Sleep shortens further; she begins falling asleep on the office couch rather than going home, justifying it with a case detail.

### Stage 2 — Disclosure shutdown and tactical solo-ing
The diagnostic Stage 2 marker is **the lie of omission to Cage.** Not a large lie — a small one, about where she was that afternoon, who she met with, how much she had to drink. The lie is functionally a perimeter wall: she is closing the loop of information so that no one can advise her, intercept her, or *make her stop.* This is the post-Killgrave imperative (#2 in the drive hierarchy: agency over her own will) misfiring into a context where Cage is not a threat and the lie is not necessary. She knows, in some channel, that she's lying unnecessarily. She does it anyway. The dishonesty is the symptom.

Concurrent: drinking rises into clear hazardous-use territory (drinking before flight, drinking before interviews, drinking before confrontations she knows will require precision). She begins to skip showers or wear the same clothes two days running — a regression in body-care that maps to dissociation from the somatic self. Calls from Carol go unanswered for a week. She picks a fight with Malcolm over something small (an unfiled receipt, a misrouted client call) to manufacture distance she can't ask for directly.

### Stage 3 — Reckless action and the spectacle of competence
This is the stage where she does her most impressive and most damaging work simultaneously. She moves on the case alone, at night, drunk or just-past-drunk, with surveillance discipline she could not summon for her own paperwork. She **flies** in this stage — which she avoids in baseline because flight is Jewel-coded and Killgrave-coded — and she flies *badly,* the controlled-falling style, landing rough on rooftops. The recklessness is not stupidity; it is a precise calibration in which she has decided that her own physical wellbeing is a permissible cost variable. She will absorb beatings she could have avoided, take meetings without backup, walk into rooms where the exits are bad.

The 2016 undercover arc is the textbook Stage 3 presentation: she fakes a separation from her husband, accepts incarceration, alienates her closest ally (Carol), and lies to everyone who loves her — not because the operation strictly requires it, but because the operation gives her *permission* to do what her decompensation is already pulling her toward. The mission is real. It is also a vehicle.

### Stage 4 — The freeze-rage-shame triad
When Stage 3 collides with a Killgrave-coded stimulus (a purple object, a voice-of-command, the coerced sexual humiliation of a third party, the specific cadence of a man telling a woman what to do), her affect regulation collapses into the trauma-physiology triad: **freeze, then explosive overresponse, then shame spiral.** The freeze is brief — seconds to a minute — and presents as a flat, mid-distance stare with shallow breath; observers misread it as composure. The overresponse is disproportionate to the immediate threat and proportionate to the historical wound: she will put a man through a wall for grabbing her wrist, will threaten lethal force in a context where restraint would serve. The shame spiral that follows is private, alcoholic, and can last days. This is the point at which the public-safety risk is non-trivial and the self-harm risk (via alcohol, via reckless flight, via accepting beatings) is highest.

### Stage 5 — Collapse
True collapse, when it comes, is **quiet, somatic, and avoidant** rather than dramatic. She does not call anyone. She does not hurt herself directly. She goes dark — phone off or unanswered, office locked, apartment dark or empty — for a window measured in days, occasionally a week. She drinks through it. She sleeps in fragments. She may end up at a bar she's never been to in a borough she doesn't work, because no one she knows will find her there. She does not cry in this period; tears are too organized. She is, functionally, **waiting for the affect to pass through her** in the only way she knows, which is to wall herself off until the body completes its discharge.

This is not suicidality, and the file should be careful not to code it as such. There is no canonical evidence of suicidal ideation or intent at any point. What there is, and what is dangerous in a distinct way, is **a profound indifference to her own continuation during these windows** — a willingness to be killed if killed is what happens, not as a wish but as a non-resistance. Operationally this is suicide-equivalent risk via passive exposure rather than active means.

---

## 3. Failure Presentations by Domain

### Occupational
Cases stall mid-investigation; client calls go unreturned; invoices don't go out; the office becomes uninhabitable. She is capable of completing a major case in Stage 3 while completely failing to run her business in Stages 1–2. The pattern is **selective hyperfunction within total infrastructural neglect.** Malcolm, when present, absorbs the infrastructural failure — which is part of why his arrival in her life raises her functional ceiling without raising her actual baseline.

### Marital / parental
With Cage the failure mode is **withdrawal-then-provocation.** She pulls away first (silence, late nights, lies of omission); when he reaches for her, she picks a fight calibrated to wound him precisely (his past, his street rep, his judgment as a father). The fight serves to confirm her predicted abandonment (he will leave, because she has made it intolerable to stay) and to give her the moral cover of *being left* rather than *leaving.* He has, to date, not actually left — which is the central datum about the marriage and about her capacity for repair. With Danielle the failure mode is **physical presence with affective absence** — she does not abandon the child, ever, but in Stage 2–3 she can spend an afternoon with the baby and not remember a single specific thing about it. The mothering drive (#4) holds her in the room; the trauma physiology hollows the room out.

### Social
Carol is the index relationship. Friendship with Carol is one of the load-bearing structures of Jessica's adult life, and she has fractured it more than once via Stage 3 lying-by-omission. The pattern: Jessica decides Carol cannot be told the operational truth; Carol learns later and reads the omission as a verdict on the friendship; the repair requires Jessica to do something she finds nearly impossible, which is to *explain her interior in words to someone who outranks her socially.* The repair has succeeded historically. It is not guaranteed to succeed on any given occasion.

Malcolm is the index for the kind of relationship she does *not* sabotage as readily, because he asks less in the registers she cannot give (verbal disclosure, performed warmth) and more in the registers she can (showing up, work, the small reciprocal protections of two people who share an office). Even with Malcolm, Stage 2–3 produces snapping and unfair anger; the difference is that Malcolm has the disposition to absorb it and the diagnostic insight to read it as symptom.

### Somatic
Stage-by-stage somatic load: insomnia (Stage 1) → hazardous drinking (Stage 2) → accepted physical injury (Stage 3) → multi-day under-eating and dehydration (Stage 4–5). She does not seek medical care for any of it. The super-durability disguises the cost — bruises that would hospitalize a civilian are something she walks off, which means there is no external constraint forcing her into care. The long-run somatic risk profile is hepatic, gastric, and cardiovascular from sustained heavy alcohol use; cumulative micro-concussive load from absorbed beatings; and untreated chronic insomnia compounding all of the above.

### Cognitive
Under decompensation her pattern-matching narrows and **personalizes.** A case becomes about her. A coincidence becomes about her. The cognitive distortion is not paranoia in the persecutory sense — she does not believe the world is conspiring against her — but a kind of **gravitational self-reference** in which all moving objects in the scene are read through their relevance to her wound. This is also when her investigative work, paradoxically, can become brilliant: the wound has its own pattern-recognition, and predators who match its shape light up under her attention with unusual speed. The risk is misidentification — seeing the wound's pattern in a person or situation that does not actually carry it.

---

## 4. The Trigger Taxonomy

The triggers that move her along the escalation curve are specific, enumerable, and worth cataloguing because they constitute the operational vulnerability map of the subject.

**Tier 1 — Killgrave-coded.** The color purple in a deliberate or unexpected context. Mind-control phenomena observed in others. Sexual coercion as a fact of a case. A man's voice issuing instructions to a woman with the specific cadence of command. Any encounter, direct or indirect, with the Purple Children or with secondary characters who carry Killgrave's residue. These produce Stage 4 jumps with minimal warning.

**Tier 2 — Self-as-villain-coded.** Being publicly mistaken for an antagonist. Being unable to explain herself to a person whose regard she values. Press coverage that misreads her role. Authority figures (SHIELD, Avengers brass, law enforcement) framing her as a threat. These reproduce the original Avenger-hospital wound and produce Stage 3 lying-and-isolating.

**Tier 3 — Danielle-coded.** Any credible threat to her daughter; any reminder of her own family's death (road accidents, military convoys, the specific geography of Forest Hills); any situation in which Danielle is in a room with someone whose intentions Jessica cannot vouch for. Produces predictable tactical behavior (she becomes legible to enemies here, which is the most dangerous fact about this trigger class).

**Tier 4 — Jewel-coded.** The costume itself, photographs from the era, anyone calling her *Jewel* in earnest, requests that she resume costumed heroics, sincere invitations to formal hero teams. Produces Stage 1–2 irritability and perimeter contraction; rarely escalates further unless a Tier 1 or 2 stacks on top.

**Tier 5 — Sincerity and gratitude.** A client thanks her with real warmth. A stranger she saved finds her later to express it. Cage tells her, unprompted and in earnest, that he loves her in front of other people. These do not cause collapse, but they cause **microsabotage** — she will say something corrosive within the next two minutes to break the moment. Cumulatively, microsabotage erodes the relationships that would otherwise buffer her against the higher-tier triggers.

**Tier 6 — Enforced sobriety without substitute.** Pregnancy was the cardinal example. Stripped of alcohol as a regulation tool and not given another, she became more brittle, not less. The implication for any future intervention is significant: removing the drinking without installing a replacement regulator (somatic therapy, EMDR, a stable interoceptive practice, pharmacotherapy) leaves her exposed in a way no one around her has fully appreciated.

---

## 5. Recovery Topology

She comes back. This is the other essential datum. Across two decades of publication she has, repeatedly, walked out of Stage 5 and resumed function. The recovery is not therapeutic in any formal sense — there is no on-panel treatment record, no medication, no sustained therapist relationship despite obvious indication. The recovery mechanisms are improvised and consistent.

**Mechanism 1 — Cage's non-departure.** He does not leave during the windows when she has made leaving the rational choice. His staying is, in her economy, the falsification of her core predictive model (proximity to a powerful other = annihilation of will). Each non-departure slightly weakens the model. The marriage is, in effect, a twenty-year exposure therapy protocol he is administering without naming.

**Mechanism 2 — The case.** A new client with a real problem reactivates Drive #1 (protect the weaker party in the room) and provides a structure within which the dysregulated affect can be channeled. Work is, for her, both compensation and recompensation — the same activity that hides the symptom is also the activity that reorganizes her around something other than the symptom.

**Mechanism 3 — Danielle.** The child's needs are non-negotiable in a way that overrides Stage 5 inertia. She has, demonstrably, pulled herself out of multi-day windows because Danielle required her physically present and functional. The reparative drive (#4) is the strongest single recovery engine in the file.

**Mechanism 4 — Malcolm's quiet infrastructure.** He keeps the office running while she is offline. The business does not die during her windows because he is there. This is a structural support she did not seek and would not have asked for, and it is a non-trivial reason her recoveries do not have to be total to be sufficient.

**Mechanism 5 — The mastery-of-affect move.** The original *Alias* Killgrave confrontation established the template: she wins by refusing to be baited, by holding her own affect steady against a stimulus engineered to dysregulate it. Each subsequent decompensation-and-recovery is, in part, a re-rehearsal of that single act. She has built — slowly, without help, against her own grain — a small and real capacity to **hold the affect without acting on it.** It is not large. It is larger than it was in *Alias* #1. The trend line, across the canon, is up.

**The residue.** Each cycle leaves a deposit. Shame about what she said to Cage in Stage 2. Guilt about what she let happen to her body in Stage 3. A specific memory of a moment she cannot apologize for because apologizing would require explaining, and explaining would require words she does not have. These deposits accumulate in the form of a slightly lower baseline tolerance for the next iteration — *and* a slightly more practiced recovery pathway. Whether the trajectory is net-positive or net-negative across her life depends on which curve dominates: the accumulating somatic and relational cost, or the slowly enlarging capacity to hold and recover. The honest assessment, on present evidence, is that she is **net-positive but narrowly,** and that the margin is contingent on the continued presence of Cage, Danielle, and Malcolm. Removal of any one of those three would shift the curve.

---

## 6. Operational Summary

The subject fails in a stereotyped, five-stage curve from subclinical loading through irritability, disclosure shutdown, reckless solo action, and freeze-rage-shame, terminating in a quiet multi-day dark window characterized by alcohol, dissociation, and passive indifference to her own continuation. The triggers are enumerable and tier-rankable, with Killgrave-coded stimuli producing the fastest escalations and sincerity producing the most insidious slow erosion. Recovery is improvised, non-clinical, and reliable enough to date — but reliant on three specific human attachments and on a work structure that channels her drives productively. The file should treat any disruption to those attachments, or any enforced sobriety without substitute regulation, as a material change in risk posture. The subject is not fragile. She is load-bearing across a narrow envelope, and the load is heavier than her surface presentation discloses.

*End section.*


## Trajectory & Forward Assessment

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 11: TRAJECTORY & FORWARD ASSESSMENT

**Subject:** Jessica Campbell Jones-Cage
**Section purpose:** Forward projection across the next 5–25 years of subject's life, with fork points, leading indicators, and the specific conditions that move her toward consolidation versus collapse. Built from longitudinal pattern analysis; not predictive in the deterministic sense — rather, a map of the topology she is moving across, with the gradients labeled.

---

## 1. THE BASELINE TRAJECTORY (status-quo extrapolation)

Absent intervention or major external shock, the subject's most likely 5-year arc is **continued slow consolidation along a narrow, costly equilibrium.** The shape of that equilibrium:

- Alias Investigations remains the organizing structure of her days. Caseload skews 60/40 toward superhuman-adjacent work (the only paying market that knows her name), with the remainder being domestic, missing-persons, and corporate background work she takes for the cash and the relative quiet.
- Cohabitation with Cage and Danielle continues, punctuated by short separations (one to three weeks) following high-stress arcs. Pattern: she leaves, sleeps at the office, drinks, returns, does not discuss it, Cage does not press. This is not a marriage in collapse; it is a marriage with a known stress valve both parties have tacitly licensed.
- Drinking stabilizes in the moderate-to-heavy band — call it 4–7 standard drinks most evenings, occasional binges around case anniversaries (the Killgrave dates, the accident date in mid-spring, the date of the Avenger-hospital incident). She is not in remission and is not actively deteriorating; she is in what addiction medicine would call a **functional plateau** — the worst kind for long-term outcomes because it generates no crisis large enough to force change.
- Social network remains tightly bounded: Cage; Danielle; Malcolm Ducasse as professional partner and quasi-sibling; Carol Danvers in a relationship that has been damaged and partially repaired and now lives in a wary middle distance; Matt Murdock as occasional collegial contact; a handful of Hell's Kitchen / Harlem service-industry regulars who know her by name and never ask.
- Avengers-adjacency continues without true membership. She will be consulted on cases involving mind control, coercion, trafficking, and superhuman domestic-abuse situations — she has, by accretion, become the field's foremost practitioner-survivor expert, and that quiet specialization is the most likely durable professional identity she settles into.

This baseline is **survivable indefinitely** and is, by the standards of someone with her trauma load, an achievement. It is also **structurally fragile** in three specific ways covered below.

---

## 2. THE THREE STRUCTURAL FRAGILITIES OF THE BASELINE

### 2.1 The unmedicated, untreated PTSD substrate.

She has never been depicted in sustained, structured trauma treatment. No EMDR, no prolonged exposure, no trauma-focused CBT, no SSRI, no prazosin for nightmares, no naltrexone or acamprosate for the alcohol piece. Her "treatment" has been: work, Cage, Danielle, and time. These have built genuine resilience but have not touched the underlying physiology. Cortisol dysregulation, startle-response sensitization, and the freeze-rage-shame cycle are all still present and still being managed via alcohol. **The substrate has not been treated; it has been outrun.** Outrunning is sustainable until it isn't.

### 2.2 The liver, the sleep architecture, and the 50s.

She is, in publication time, in her mid-thirties. The drinking pattern she has maintained since her early twenties has a known biological trajectory. Hepatic capacity narrows. Sleep architecture (already poor) degrades further with age and alcohol. Enhanced durability gives her some buffer — her metabolism likely processes ethanol faster than baseline human — but durability is not the same as immunity, and there is no canonical evidence her liver is invulnerable. The fork point here is not dramatic; it is a routine blood panel sometime in her early 40s that returns elevated GGT and AST and forces her, for the first time, to confront the drinking as a finite resource rather than an infinite coping tool.

### 2.3 Danielle, who will become a teenager.

Danielle is currently small. The reparative mothering Jessica is doing — present, attentive, the inverse of her own losses — is calibrated for a small child. The mother of a small child can express love almost entirely through proximity, vigilance, and physical care. The mother of a thirteen-year-old must express love through verbal availability, conflict tolerance, and the capacity to be the object of adolescent contempt without retaliating or withdrawing. **Jessica's verbal-emotional repertoire is her weakest channel.** The transition from mothering-a-child to mothering-an-adolescent is the single most predictable destabilizing event in her ten-to-fifteen-year future, and it will arrive whether she prepares for it or not.

---

## 3. THE FORK POINTS (discrete events that will route her)

A trajectory of this kind is not a smooth curve; it is a series of branch nodes. Below are the high-probability nodes in approximate order of likelihood.

### 3.1 The Killgrave Recurrence Node.

Probability over 10 years: very high (>80%, given Marvel narrative gravity and the existence of the Purple Children as ongoing canon). Killgrave or a Killgrave-coded antagonist (a child of his, a successor, a copycat, a pheromone-mimicking technology) will resurface. Each recurrence is a referendum on how much she has integrated the original trauma.

- *Growth fork:* She handles it with the affect-mastery she demonstrated at the end of the original *Alias* arc, uses it as evidence to herself that she is not the person Killgrave made, and — critically — debriefs afterward with Cage or a professional rather than absorbing it alone.
- *Catastrophe fork:* She handles it alone, by going dark on her family in the name of protecting them (the 2016 pattern), wins tactically, and loses another year of trust with the people who would have helped. Each iteration of this pattern compounds; Cage's patience is wide but not infinite, and Danielle's awareness of these absences will grow.

### 3.2 The Sobriety Node.

Probability of a forcing event over 10 years: high (>70%). The forcing event is some combination of medical finding, pregnancy consideration (second child question), a Danielle-witnesses-something-bad incident, or a case she loses or botches drunk and cannot forgive herself for.

- *Growth fork:* She enters treatment that is **trauma-informed and not abstinence-fundamentalist** — the only kind likely to take. A program that addresses PTSD and AUD as comorbid rather than sequential. Probable best fit: individual trauma-focused therapy plus a medication-assisted approach (naltrexone) plus a non-12-step peer structure (SMART Recovery or similar), because the surrender language of AA will collide badly with her post-Killgrave imperative around agency. If she finds a clinician who does not flinch at her history and does not try to "handle" her, she can do this work.
- *Catastrophe fork:* She white-knuckles sobriety without addressing the trauma; the PTSD symptoms, no longer dampened, become unbearable; she relapses harder; the relapse takes her below her prior functional floor; the marriage strains; she retreats into work; the cycle compresses.

### 3.3 The Danielle-Powers Node.

Probability: moderate to high (>60% over 15 years, given parental genetics — Cage's durability, Jessica's strength/flight — and Marvel inheritance conventions). Danielle manifests powers, likely in early adolescence, likely under stress.

- *Growth fork:* Jessica's specific competence — being the world's foremost expert in what it is like to wake up powered and frightened and alone — becomes the most valuable thing she has ever owned. She becomes the parent she did not have. The reparative arc closes a circuit.
- *Catastrophe fork:* The manifestation reactivates Jessica's own post-accident memories; she over-controls, over-monitors, projects her own trauma onto Danielle's experience, and replicates with her daughter the same hovering protective surveillance she resents from every authority figure in her own life. Danielle, who will have inherited some portion of Jessica's defiant streak, pushes back hard. Estrangement is possible.

### 3.4 The Cage-Crisis Node.

Probability: moderate (>40% over 10 years, given the genre). Cage takes a serious injury, a long incarceration, a Power-Man-and-Iron-Fist-style entanglement that pulls him away, or — worst case — dies on a case.

- *Growth fork:* She has, by then, built enough adjacent structure (Malcolm, Carol, Danielle herself, a therapist, a meeting, a routine) that the loss is survivable without total collapse. The marriage has been the load-bearing wall; she has, ideally, added redundant supports before it is tested.
- *Catastrophe fork:* The marriage was the only load-bearing wall. Loss of Cage means loss of the daily container that has kept the drinking at a plateau and the dissociation in check. She would become a serious risk to herself — not via suicide, for which she does not show classical risk factors, but via the slow-motion self-destruction of unfettered AUD plus reckless solo casework plus the eventual fatal mistake.

### 3.5 The Public-Recognition Node.

Probability: moderate (>50% over 15 years). At some point — a high-profile case, an Avengers crisis she is publicly central to, a memoir, an investigative reporter doing a piece on her — her full history including the Killgrave captivity becomes public knowledge in a way she cannot control.

- *Growth fork:* She has time to prepare a frame for it. She is the author of her own disclosure. The public narrative she has spent twenty years refusing to construct gets constructed by her on her terms. She becomes, against every instinct, a public figure for survivors — not by speech-giving (she would loathe this) but by visible competent existence as one.
- *Catastrophe fork:* The disclosure is involuntary, salacious, and arrives via a media apparatus that has incentives misaligned with her dignity. The shame floods. The drinking surges. She withdraws Danielle from school, moves the family, breaks contact with anyone she suspects of having talked. The Jameson-era distrust of media metastasizes into something paranoid-coded that, while not psychiatrically paranoid, functions identically in her life.

### 3.6 The Institutional-Capture Node.

Probability: lower but non-trivial (>25%). SHIELD-successor, a Damage Control variant, an Avengers leadership shift, or a government registration push attempts to formally absorb her — not as a cape, but as a contracted investigator with security clearance and a paycheck.

- *Growth fork:* She negotiates terms that protect her agency (the post-Killgrave imperative), takes the money, uses the access to do work she could not do solo, and walks the moment they try to handle her. This is achievable; she has the leverage.
- *Catastrophe fork:* She is squeezed in (a registration-style mandate, a court order around Danielle's powers, a leverage operation using a case she botched drunk). Being controlled by an institution is the second-most-Killgrave-coded scenario possible. She would burn the building down on her way out, professionally and possibly literally, and the legal and reputational consequences would compound for years.

---

## 4. THE GROWTH GRADIENT — WHAT MOVES HER UPWARD

The conditions under which she moves toward consolidation rather than fracture are specific and identifiable. None are mysterious; most are absent.

- **A trauma-literate clinician she does not fire in the first three sessions.** The single highest-leverage intervention in her life. She will fire the first three regardless. The fourth is the one. The clinician must be: older than she is; unimpressed by superhumans; comfortable with profanity; willing to be cross-examined about their credentials and not flinch; willing to address the alcohol without leading with it.
- **A second sober adult in the household conversation about drinking.** Cage has never been depicted intervening on her alcohol use in a structured way; he loves her around it. If he, at some point, names it as a thing he is afraid of for her and Danielle — not as ultimatum but as disclosure — that is the leverage point. He is the only person whose naming of it she cannot deflect.
- **A peer-survivor relationship.** She has Carol (powered, traumatized, alcoholic-coded in her own history); she has, theoretically, access to other survivors of Killgrave (the Purple Children, victims she's met on cases). A sustained peer relationship with another person who has been through coercive captivity would do more for her than any clinical intervention, because her core schema — *I am contaminated, I am alone in this* — is only dissolvable by counter-evidence delivered by someone whose authority she cannot reject.
- **A creative or generative outlet outside work.** She has none currently. Any sustained engagement with a non-instrumental practice (the canonical hints toward photography in some takes are plausible; she has a documentarian's eye and the patience for stillness) would give the dysregulated affect a non-pharmacological channel.
- **Daniellle reaching age 8–10 in a stable home.** Every additional year Jessica successfully parents a child past the age at which her own family was destroyed is reparative on a near-neurological level. She is, in effect, writing over the original wound with present-tense competent love. This is happening already; it will continue to happen; it is the most powerful thing in her favor.

---

## 5. THE CATASTROPHE GRADIENT — WHAT MOVES HER DOWNWARD

The specific routes by which a subject of her configuration ends badly:

- **The cascade scenario.** Killgrave-coded recurrence → handled alone → marriage stress → drinking escalation → Danielle witnesses an incident → CPS-equivalent or family-court attention → loss of custody or supervised-only access → bottoming. This is the canonical bad-outcome path for survivors with her exact comorbid profile, and every step in it is something she has demonstrated the propensity for.
- **The slow medical scenario.** No dramatic event; just liver, sleep, cardiovascular drift; cognitive narrowing in her 50s from chronic alcohol load; reduced fieldwork capacity; loss of professional identity; depression that this time is not trauma-derivative but loss-of-role; a quiet decline.
- **The lone-operator scenario.** Cage lost or estranged; Danielle launched and distant; Malcolm gone to his own practice; Carol off-world. Jessica alone in the office with the bottle and the cases. She is competent enough to do this for a long time. It is the version of her future that looks most like the *Alias* opening pages, except older, with more scar tissue and less elasticity.
- **The vendetta scenario.** A harm done to Danielle or Cage that she cannot process within her existing frameworks. She becomes the cold methodical version of herself that the dossier flags as her response to predators — but turned permanent, turned identity. The moral floor holds; she does not become a villain; but she becomes something narrower and harder than the person she has built, and the warmth she has earned access to retreats.

---

## 6. THE OPEN QUESTIONS THE FILE CANNOT YET ANSWER

A complete forward assessment must mark its own ignorances. The following are the questions about her future that the available evidence does not resolve and that future surveillance should be oriented toward.

1. **Whether she will ever speak the Killgrave experience aloud in full, to anyone, in a setting that is not coerced by plot.** She has not yet, across two decades of canon. The voluntary unforced telling is the marker of integration. Its absence is the marker of its absence.
2. **Whether the Jewel encapsulation will ever be opened.** Whether she ever returns to that costume, that name, that earlier self — not to re-adopt it, but to grieve it. The phobic avoidance is intact. The grief beneath it is not metabolized.
3. **Whether she will have a second child.** Strong arguments both ways in her psychology; canon has not foreclosed it; the decision itself, however it goes, will be a major psychological event.
4. **Whether her relationship with Carol Danvers fully repairs.** The 2016 arc damage is significant; both parties have powerful reasons to repair and powerful reasons not to. This is one of the two or three most important relationships in her life and its status at age 50 is genuinely uncertain.
5. **Whether she ever accepts a public role as survivor-advocate.** Against every instinct; possible under the right conditions; would change the shape of her late life entirely.
6. **What she does in the year after Danielle leaves home.** This is the single most diagnostic year of her later life. Whatever structure she builds — or fails to build — to replace the daily parenting work will determine the shape of her 50s and 60s.

---

## 7. SUMMARY FORWARD ASSESSMENT

The subject is currently operating in a costly but stable equilibrium that she has built, against substantial odds, out of work, marriage, motherhood, and refusal. The equilibrium will not last twenty more years in its present form; it is being held in place by variables (Cage's presence, Danielle's young-childhood, the liver's tolerance, the absence of a major Killgrave recurrence) that are time-limited. The decade between her late thirties and late forties is the **window in which the structural retrofit must happen** — treatment engaged, drinking addressed, peer-survivor connection built, verbal-emotional repertoire enlarged for the adolescent-parent transition — or the equilibrium degrades and the cascade scenarios become the likely paths.

The strongest forces in her favor are not therapeutic; they are relational and reparative. Cage's steadiness. Danielle's growth. Malcolm's loyalty. Carol's residual love. Her own demonstrated capacity to choose, again and again, the protection of the weaker party in the room — including, eventually, the weaker party who is herself.

The strongest forces against her are not external antagonists; they are her own preemptive isolation, her unaddressed substrate, and the specific lethality of her preferred coping tool over decades.

**Prognosis with no intervention:** functional plateau through early forties, drift toward one of the catastrophe gradients in the late forties and fifties, survivable but constricted late life if the marriage holds, dangerous late life if it does not.

**Prognosis with the specific interventions identified in Section 4:** sustained consolidation, late-life integration, a fifty-five-year-old version of the subject who has metabolized rather than outrun her history, who can speak the worst things aloud without disintegrating, and who is, in the precise terms this file has used throughout, *what a survivor looks like when they finish going to work and come home.*

The forward assessment is, therefore, neither optimistic nor pessimistic. It is **contingent**, and the contingencies are knowable, and several of them are within reach of people who already love her.

*End Section 11. Continue to Section 12: Surveillance Recommendations & Care Pathway.*

## Relationship Graph
### [[Luke Cage (Power Man (formerly); Carl Lucas (birth name))]]
- Husband, co-parent, the bond that holds her stable; met as Knightress in a rooftop-fight one-night-stand, reconnected via Alias #1 in a self-loathing encounter she couldn't face the next morning
- Bedrock safety: he doesn't demand disclosure, doesn't perform, accepts the prickliness as weather, hands her real problems
- Trust level: maximal — the only person she has chosen to let see all of it
- FAILURE MODE: her preemptive-withdrawal default + his patience = the 2016 template, where she fakes separation 'to protect him' and the lie itself becomes the wound. If she goes solo on something Killgrave-coded and lies long enough, the marriage decompensates around the protective deception, not the threat
- LEVERAGE: anyone who can convincingly threaten Cage, or convincingly threaten her ability to be a partner Cage deserves, owns her decision tree

### Danielle Cage
- Daughter; the late-emergent drive that has slowly reorganized everything above her
- Reparative attachment — she gives Danielle the present-tense attention her own losses denied her
- FAILURE MODE: she becomes uncharacteristically predictable around Danielle's safety, overrides every other tactical consideration, and can be moved into bad positions by credible threats to the child
- LEVERAGE: the cleanest single point of control on Jessica Jones in existence; also the line past which adversaries do not survive

### Malcolm Ducasse
- Assistant/partner at Alias; chosen-family junior; the closest she comes to mentoring
- Trust level: high, expressed as gruff fairness and undersold teaching
- FAILURE MODE: she withholds praise and information he's earned, treats him as more durable than he is
- LEVERAGE: she will not let him be hurt on her account; threats to Malcolm pull her into the open

### [[Carol Danvers (Captain Marvel)]]
- Oldest friend, predating the cape life; the person she attacked under Killgrave's control
- Trust level: deep but encrusted with the most defended shame she carries
- FAILURE MODE: any recurrence of 'I cannot explain myself to Carol' (the 2016 arc) replays the original wound and produces the worst version of Jessica's solo-action spiral
- LEVERAGE: Carol is one of the very few people whose disapproval can move her; an adversary who could engineer a Carol-side misreading of Jessica would destabilize both

### Killgrave
- Captor for ~8 months; psychic constant
- Trust level: zero; psychic presence: maximal
- FAILURE MODE: even at distance, Killgrave-coded stimuli (purple, command voice, coerced consent of others) cause decompensation; his return arcs are the cardinal stressor of her life
- LEVERAGE: any Killgrave-analog (Purple Children, mind-controllers, pheromone users) inherits a fraction of his pull on her nervous system

### Jessica Drew
- Peer/friend; another woman with a violated-agency origin; mutual recognition without ceremony
- Trust level: high, expressed as comfortable silence and direct help
- FAILURE MODE: parallel trauma can compound — both withdrawing at once leaves neither holding the other
- LEVERAGE: low for adversaries; this bond is unusually clean

### [[Matthew Michael Murdock (Daredevil / The Man Without Fear / (briefly) Mike Murdock / (briefly) Kingpin of Hell's Kitchen)]]
- Episodic professional ally; mutual trauma-recognition between Catholic-guilt insomniac and survivor insomniac
- Trust level: operational, not personal
- FAILURE MODE: his savior reflex meets her allergic-to-being-handled reflex; collaboration sours fast under stress
- LEVERAGE: he can be used to reach her on a case framing, not on a personal one

### Jonah Jameson
- Bugle employer during The Pulse; exploitative-paternal
- Trust level: contemptuous-compliant
- FAILURE MODE: he overplays his hand and she walks
- LEVERAGE: financial pressure during pregnancy made this bond tolerable; outside that, none

### The Avengers
- Operationally adjacent; frame-rejected; the institution that nearly killed her and didn't visit
- Trust level: low, individual-by-individual
- FAILURE MODE: any attempt to absorb her into the team triggers the Jewel-era shame plus the hospital-abandonment wound
- LEVERAGE: do not invoke; reaching her through Avengers channels actively backfires

### The Jones Family
- Adoptive parents; partially refused attachment
- Trust level: ambient, distant
- FAILURE MODE: any forced reckoning with how she treated them re-opens survivor-guilt
- LEVERAGE: minimal operational, significant psychological if surfaced

### [[Scott Edward Harris Lang (Ant-Man)]]
- Attempted to date her during Alias; she sabotaged it
- Trust level: warm-rueful from a distance
- FAILURE MODE: a benchmark of her trauma-related sexual avoidance more than a live relationship
- LEVERAGE: none operational
